# **UPLIFT TECHNOLOGIES HEALTHCARE-OPERATIONS TRAINING CURRICULUM**

## **FULLY TEACHABLE COURSE AND MODULE BUILDS**

---

# **A) PROGRAM CATALOG**

## **COURSE 0: FOUNDATION GOVERNANCE AND HOW TO TRAIN (PROGRAM CONTROL LAYER)**

**Purpose:** Make the six-course system audit-ready without changing source standards. Establish governance framework and safe stop rules.

**Audience:** All Uplift roles before starting Course 1

**Prerequisites:** None

**Duration:** 2-3 hours (self-paced orientation)

**Entry-Level Day Plan:**

* Complete in one session before Course 1 access

**What Good Looks Like:**

* Learner understands delivery modes, passing standards, attempts, cooling periods  
* Learner can articulate all four safe stop rules  
* Learner knows where to find training records and refresher requirements  
* Learner understands sanctions process and retaliation prohibition

**Common Misconceptions:**

* "I can skip this because it's just admin" — foundation prevents downstream confusion  
* "Safe stop rules are suggestions" — these are mandatory stop conditions

**Required Learner Artifacts:**

* Governance acknowledgment with timestamp  
* Safe stop rules quiz completion  
* Sanctions policy acknowledgment

---

## **COURSE 1: HIPAA PRIVACY, SECURITY, AND BREACH RESPONSE (ROLE-BASED)**

**Purpose:** Establish PHI handling, access controls, incident response, and role-specific operational boundaries for all Uplift roles.

**Audience:** All Uplift roles (Client Success Specialist Medical Benefits, Clinical Nurse Coordinator, Order Entry Specialist, Patient Claims Specialist, Patient Accounts Receivable Specialist, Executive Assistant, Medical Scribe MBBS, Accounts Receivable Executive Patient Balance Collections)

**Prerequisites:** Course 0 completed

**Duration Tracks:**

* Essentials: 6 hours (foundation only, no role variants)  
* Standard: 10 hours (core \+ role variant \+ standard scenarios)  
* Intensive: 16 hours (core \+ role variant \+ all scenarios \+ live simulations \+ policy writing workshop)

**Entry-Level Day Plan (Standard Track):**

* Day 1: Modules 1-4 (PHI, permitted framework, minimum necessary, verification)  
* Day 2: Modules 5-8 (Pakistan workstation, MFA/passwords, comms hygiene, phishing)  
* Day 3: Modules 9-12 (documentation, incidents, breach playbook, sanctions)  
* Day 4: Role Variant module (13-16) \+ scenario library practice  
* Day 5: Final exam \+ practical evaluation \+ remediation scheduling if needed

**What Good Looks Like:**

* Never discloses PHI before verification  
* Uses minimum necessary in notes and communications  
* Uses approved channels only  
* Reports incidents and near-misses immediately  
* Preserves evidence, does not delete/alter records during investigations  
* Applies correct role variant boundaries

**Common Misconceptions and Failure Modes:**

* Minimum necessary over-application causing care delays  
* Verification script abandonment under pressure  
* Password shortcuts  
* Phishing false negatives based on "looks real"  
* Incident under-reporting (near-misses)  
* Documentation incompleteness  
* Role-variant confusion

**Required Learner Artifacts:**

* Redacted artifact set (Module 1\)  
* Disclosure decision justifications (Module 2\)  
* Mock access request/removal draft (Module 3\)  
* Verification simulation score sheet (Module 4\)  
* Workspace self-audit with evidence \+ remediation plan (Module 5\)  
* MFA enrollment verification (Module 6\)  
* Email rewrite set (Module 7\)  
* Phishing simulation results (Module 8\)  
* Documentation submissions (Module 9\)  
* Incident response simulation record (Module 10\)  
* Chain-of-custody \+ witness statement (Module 11\)  
* Sanctions reasoning exercise (Module 12\)  
* Role-variant scenario responses (Module 13-16)

---

## **COURSE 2: ICD-10 CODING OVERVIEW FOR OPERATIONS TEAMS (NON-CODER, WORKFLOW-SAFE)**

**Purpose:** Enable non-coder operational roles to recognize diagnosis-related workflow issues and route appropriately without crossing into code selection.

**Audience:** Client Success Specialist Medical Benefits, Order Entry Specialist, Patient Claims Specialist, Patient Accounts Receivable Specialist, Accounts Receivable Executive; Medical Scribe only if assigned to diagnosis-awareness workflows

**Prerequisites:** Course 1 completed first

**Duration Tracks:**

* Essentials: 4 hours  
* Standard: 8 hours  
* Intensive: 12 hours

**Entry-Level Day Plan (Standard 8h):**

* Day 1: Modules 1-2  
* Day 2: Modules 3-4  
* Day 3: Modules 5-6  
* Day 4: Modules 7-8  
* Day 5: Modules 9-10  
* Day 6: Modules 11-12 \+ practical rubric prep

**What Good Looks Like:**

* Learner explains ICD-10 purpose without coding  
* Flags documentation gaps and routes to coder/provider  
* Translates denial reasons in plain language without mentioning codes unless policy allows

**Common Misconceptions and Failure Modes:**

* Scope creep into assigning codes  
* Treating unspecified codes as harmless  
* Confusing medical necessity vs coverage

**Required Learner Artifacts:**

* Touchpoint map (Module 1\)  
* Parsed code worksheets (Module 2\)  
* Provider query drafts (Modules 3, 4, 9\)  
* Denial root-cause worksheets (Module 8\)  
* Boundary decision log (Module 10\)

---

## **COURSE 3: DAY-TO-DAY DOCUMENT HYGIENE AND DATA HANDLING (OPERATIONAL SECURITY)**

**Purpose:** Establish clean screen/desk habits, correct storage, redaction, channel use, screenshot discipline, and timely updates across all operational workflows.

**Audience:** All roles

**Prerequisites:** Course 1 first

**Duration:** Standard 8 hours

**Entry-Level Day Plan (Standard 8h):**

* Day 1: Modules 1-3  
* Day 2: Modules 4-6  
* Day 3: Modules 7-9  
* Day 4: Modules 10-12  
* Day 5: Modules 13-15  
* Day 6: Modules 16-18 \+ practical prep

**What Good Looks Like:**

* Clean screen/desk habits maintained  
* Correct storage location usage  
* Correct redaction before sharing  
* Approved channels used exclusively  
* No screenshots of PHI screens  
* Timely status updates completed

**Common Misconceptions and Failure Modes:**

* "Screenshots are fastest" — violates PHI controls  
* "Shared folders are secure enough" — requires client-specific approval  
* "I'll update later" — creates audit gaps

**Required Learner Artifacts:**

* Workspace photos (Module-specific)  
* Redacted files submissions  
* Cleanup reports  
* Update status reports  
* Template completions  
* Drill scores

---

## **COURSE 4: MEDICAL SCRIBE TRAINING (REMOTE, CLINICAL DOCUMENTATION QUALITY)**

**Purpose:** Train Medical Scribes in documentation-only scope, SOAP structure, specialty terminology, and escalation boundaries for remote clinical documentation.

**Audience:** Medical Scribe (MBBS) only

**Prerequisites:** Course 1 Clinical Support variant \+ Course 3

**Duration:** Standard 20 hours

**Entry-Level Day Plan (Standard 20h across 10 days):**

* Days 1-2: Modules 1-4  
* Days 3-4: Modules 5-8  
* Day 5: Modules 9-12  
* Day 6: Modules 13-15  
* Day 7: Modules 16-18  
* Day 8: Modules 19-21  
* Day 9: Modules 22-24  
* Day 10: Modules 25-26 \+ practical prep

**What Good Looks Like:**

* Documentation-only scope maintained  
* Consistent SOAP structure  
* No hallucinated facts  
* Correct escalation language used  
* Specialty terminology accurate

**Common Misconceptions and Failure Modes:**

* Interpreting clinical decisions instead of documenting  
* Adding assumptions not stated by provider  
* Using terminology beyond training scope

**Required Learner Artifacts:**

* Note audits (module-specific)  
* Attestation simulation logs  
* Timed accuracy scores  
* Boundary scenario scores  
* Specialty template completions

---

## **COURSE 5: EXECUTIVE ASSISTANT TRAINING FOR HEALTHCARE OPERATIONS (COMPLIANCE-SAFE)**

**Purpose:** Train Executive Assistants in PHI-free calendar management, triage without over-reading, verification, and redacted notes distribution.

**Audience:** Executive Assistant only

**Prerequisites:** Course 1 Executive Support variant \+ Course 3

**Duration:** Standard 10 hours

**Entry-Level Day Plan (5 days):**

* Day 1: Modules 1-3  
* Day 2: Modules 4-6  
* Day 3: Modules 7-9  
* Day 4: Modules 10-12  
* Day 5: Modules 13-15 \+ practical prep

**What Good Looks Like:**

* PHI-free calendars maintained  
* Triage without over-reading PHI  
* Correct routing and verification  
* Redacted notes distributed appropriately

**Common Misconceptions and Failure Modes:**

* "Calendar is internal so PHI is safe" — broad visibility creates exposure  
* "I need to read everything to route" — minimum necessary applies to triage

**Required Learner Artifacts:**

* Calendar audit routine completions  
* Recipient limitation checklists  
* Script pack demonstrations  
* Redaction submissions

---

## **COURSE 6: SUPPORTING ROLES BOOTCAMP (PODS-BASED, UPLIFT-SPECIFIC)**

**Purpose:** Integrate all prior training into role-specific operational workflows with quality metrics, handoffs, escalation, and professionalism standards.

**Audience:** All roles

**Prerequisites:** Course 1 \+ Course 3 \+ Course 2/4/5 where required

**Duration:** Combined Track 16-24 hours depending on role

**Entry-Level Plan:**

* Common Core (Modules 1-8) first  
* Role-specific modules next

**What Good Looks Like:**

* Consistent quality metrics met  
* Clean handoffs executed  
* Escalations documented properly  
* Professional communication maintained

**Common Misconceptions and Failure Modes:**

* "Pod-specific shortcuts are acceptable" — standards apply uniformly  
* "Escalation is failure" — escalation protects quality

**Required Learner Artifacts:**

* System task completions  
* Escalation documentation  
* Handoff template submissions  
* Professionalism scenario scores

---

# **B) COURSE BUILDS**

---

# **COURSE 0: FOUNDATION GOVERNANCE AND HOW TO TRAIN (PROGRAM CONTROL LAYER)**

## **Course Header**

**Course Number:** 0  
 **Course Name:** Foundation Governance and How to Train (Program Control Layer)  
 **Purpose:** Make the six-course system audit-ready without changing any source standards. Establish governance framework, safe stop rules, and program navigation.

**Audience:** All Uplift roles before starting Course 1

**Prerequisites:** None

**Duration:** 2-3 hours (self-paced orientation)

## **Course Overview**

**Scope:** This course establishes the control framework for Courses 1-6. Covers delivery modes, passing standards, attempts, cooling periods, training records, refresher cadence, sanctions process, core definitions (PHI, ePHI, Minimum Necessary, Incident, Breach), entry-level scaffolding (how to read modules, use job aids, complete assessments), and safe stop rules that always apply.

**What Good Looks Like:**

* Understands three delivery modes (Self-Paced, Instructor-Led, Blended)  
* Can state passing standards and attempt limits for assessments  
* Knows required training record fields  
* Understands all four refresher triggers plus client-specific cadence (needs\_review)  
* Can articulate sanctions process (four levels \+ acceleration clause)  
* Defines PHI, ePHI, Minimum Necessary, Incident, Breach correctly  
* Applies five safe stop rules in any scenario

**Common Misconceptions and Failure Modes:**

* Treating Course 0 as "skippable admin" — creates downstream confusion across all six courses  
* Believing safe stop rules are suggestions — these are mandatory stop conditions  
* Assuming "I already know HIPAA" means Course 0 can be skipped — governance structure is Uplift-specific

## **Role Alignment**

**All roles complete Course 0 before Course 1 access.**

**Do-Not-Do Boundaries (Universal):**

* Do not proceed to Course 1 without completing Course 0 governance acknowledgment  
* Do not bypass safe stop rules under any circumstance  
* Do not assume prior training satisfies Uplift-specific governance requirements

## **Required Learner Artifacts**

1. Governance acknowledgment with timestamp  
2. Safe stop rules quiz (5 items, 100% required)  
3. Sanctions policy acknowledgment with timestamp  
4. Core definitions quiz completion (80% passing standard)

## **Module List**

**Module 0.1:** Program Structure and Delivery Modes (20 min)  
 **Module 0.2:** Passing Standards, Attempts, and Cooling Periods (15 min)  
 **Module 0.3:** Training Records and Refresher Cadence (20 min)  
 **Module 0.4:** Sanctions Process and Accountability (20 min)  
 **Module 0.5:** Core Definitions (PHI, ePHI, Minimum Necessary, Incident, Breach) (30 min)  
 **Module 0.6:** Entry-Level Scaffolding and Safe Stop Rules (30 min)

---

# **COURSE 1: HIPAA PRIVACY, SECURITY, AND BREACH RESPONSE (ROLE-BASED)**

## **Course Header**

**Course Number:** 1  
 **Course Name:** HIPAA Privacy, Security, and Breach Response (Role-Based)  
 **Purpose:** Establish PHI handling, access controls, incident response, and role-specific operational boundaries for all Uplift roles.

**Audience:** All Uplift roles (Client Success Specialist Medical Benefits, Clinical Nurse Coordinator, Order Entry Specialist, Patient Claims Specialist, Patient Accounts Receivable Specialist, Executive Assistant, Medical Scribe MBBS, Accounts Receivable Executive Patient Balance Collections)

**Prerequisites:** Course 0 completed

**Duration Tracks:**

* Essentials: 6 hours (foundation only, no role variants)  
* Standard: 10 hours (core \+ role variant \+ standard scenarios)  
* Intensive: 16 hours (core \+ role variant \+ all scenarios \+ live simulations \+ policy writing workshop)

**Entry-Level Day Plan (Standard Track):**

* Day 1: Modules 1-4  
* Day 2: Modules 5-8  
* Day 3: Modules 9-12  
* Day 4: Role Variant module (13-16) \+ scenario library  
* Day 5: Final exam \+ practical evaluation \+ remediation if needed

## **Course Overview**

**Scope:** Modules 1-12 cover core HIPAA privacy, security, and breach response (PHI identification, permitted disclosures, minimum necessary, verification, remote workstation security, authentication, communication hygiene, phishing defense, documentation, incidents, breach playbook, sanctions). Modules 13-16 provide role-specific variants (Revenue Cycle, Clinical Support, Front Office, Executive Support) with targeted scenarios and do-not-do boundaries.

**What Good Looks Like:**

* Never discloses PHI before verification  
* Uses minimum necessary in notes and communications  
* Uses approved channels only  
* Reports incidents and near-misses immediately  
* Preserves evidence, never deletes/alters records during investigations  
* Applies correct role variant boundaries

**Common Misconceptions and Failure Modes:**

* Minimum necessary over-application causing care delays — balance required  
* Verification script abandonment under pressure — script is mandatory  
* Password shortcuts — violates authentication controls  
* Phishing false negatives based on "looks real" — requires checklist discipline  
* Incident under-reporting (near-misses) — near-misses must be reported  
* Documentation incompleteness — all required fields must be completed  
* Role-variant confusion — boundaries differ by role

## **Role Alignment**

### **Client Success Specialist (Medical Benefits)**

**Required Modules:** 1-12 \+ 13 (Revenue Cycle variant)

**Critical Tasks:**

* Minimum necessary during benefits and payer communications  
* Correct escalation for payer documentation requests (Scenario 11\)

**Do-Not-Do Boundaries:**

* No credential sharing (Scenario 13\)  
* No personal device PHI intake (Scenario 17\)

### **Clinical Nurse Coordinator**

**Required Modules:** 1-12 \+ 14 (Clinical Support variant)

**Critical Tasks:**

* Verification failure stop rule (Scenario 16\)  
* Spouse/family results request handling (Scenario 2\)

**Do-Not-Do Boundaries:**

* No bypassing verification due to urgency

### **Order Entry Specialist (OES)**

**Required Modules:** 1-12 \+ 15 (Front Office variant)

**Critical Tasks:**

* No screenshots of PHI screens (Scenario 5\)  
* Correct handling of patient record requests (Scenario 14\)

**Do-Not-Do Boundaries:**

* No curiosity browsing (Scenario 20\)

### **Patient Claims Specialist (PCS)**

**Required Modules:** 1-12 \+ 13 (Revenue Cycle variant)

**Critical Tasks:**

* Misdirected email response steps (Scenario 7\)  
* Three-party payer calls require policy check (Scenario 18\)

**Do-Not-Do Boundaries:**

* No password sharing (Scenario 13\)

### **Patient Accounts Receivable Specialist**

**Required Modules:** 1-12 \+ 13 (Revenue Cycle variant)

**Critical Tasks:**

* Wrong-number call termination and documentation (Scenario 1\)  
* Patient dispute de-escalation without promises (Scenario 8\)

**Do-Not-Do Boundaries:**

* No extra disclosure during conflict

### **Executive Assistant**

**Required Modules:** 1-12 \+ 16 (Executive Support variant)

**Critical Tasks:**

* Calendar PHI prevention and correction (Scenario 10\)

**Do-Not-Do Boundaries:**

* No broad invite disclosures

### **Medical Scribe (MBBS)**

**Required Modules:** 1-12 \+ 14 (Clinical Support variant)

**Critical Tasks:**

* Family member entry during dictation containment (Scenario 4\)

**Do-Not-Do Boundaries:**

* No unsecured network work (Scenario 15\)

### **Accounts Receivable Executive (Patient Balance Collections)**

**Required Modules:** 1-12 \+ 13 (Revenue Cycle variant)

**Critical Tasks:**

* Secure payment handling using approved tools

**Do-Not-Do Boundaries:**

* No retaliation or escalation misuse during aggressive calls

## **Required Learner Artifacts**

1. Redacted artifact set (Module 1\)  
2. Disclosure decision justifications (Module 2\)  
3. Mock access request/removal draft (Module 3\)  
4. Verification simulation score sheet (Module 4\)  
5. Workspace self-audit with evidence \+ remediation plan (Module 5\)  
6. MFA enrollment verification (Module 6\)  
7. Email rewrite set (Module 7\)  
8. Phishing simulation results (Module 8\)  
9. Documentation submissions (Module 9\)  
10. Incident response simulation record (Module 10\)  
11. Chain-of-custody \+ witness statement (Module 11\)  
12. Sanctions reasoning exercise (Module 12\)  
13. Role-variant scenario responses (Modules 13-16)

## **Module List**

**Module 1:** PHI Fundamentals and Identification (60 min)  
 **Module 2:** Permitted Uses and Disclosures Framework (75 min)  
 **Module 3:** Minimum Necessary and Access Controls (90 min)  
 **Module 4:** Patient Identity Verification and Caller Authentication (45 min)  
 **Module 5:** Remote Workstation Security (Pakistan Operations) (90 min)  
 **Module 6:** Authentication, Passwords, and MFA (60 min)  
 **Module 7:** Email, Messaging, and Communication Hygiene (75 min)  
 **Module 8:** Phishing, Social Engineering, and Malware Defense (60 min)  
 **Module 9:** Documentation Discipline and Audit Readiness (75 min)  
 **Module 10:** Incident Identification and Immediate Response (90 min)  
 **Module 11:** Breach Response Playbook and Evidence Preservation (60 min)  
 **Module 12:** Sanctions, Accountability, and Reporting Culture (45 min)  
 **Module 13:** Role Variant \- Revenue Cycle (90 min)  
 **Module 14:** Role Variant \- Clinical Support (90 min)  
 **Module 15:** Role Variant \- Front Office (90 min)  
 **Module 16:** Role Variant \- Executive Support (60 min)

---

# **COURSE 2: ICD-10 CODING OVERVIEW FOR OPERATIONS TEAMS (NON-CODER, WORKFLOW-SAFE)**

## **Course Header**

**Course Number:** 2  
 **Course Name:** ICD-10 Coding Overview for Operations Teams (Non-Coder, Workflow-Safe)  
 **Purpose:** Enable non-coder operational roles to recognize diagnosis-related workflow issues and route appropriately without crossing into code selection.

**Audience:** Client Success Specialist Medical Benefits, Order Entry Specialist, Patient Claims Specialist, Patient Accounts Receivable Specialist, Accounts Receivable Executive; Medical Scribe only if assigned to diagnosis-awareness workflows

**Prerequisites:** Course 1 completed first

**Duration Tracks:**

* Essentials: 4 hours  
* Standard: 8 hours  
* Intensive: 12 hours

**Entry-Level Day Plan (Standard 8h):**

* Day 1: Modules 1-2  
* Day 2: Modules 3-4  
* Day 3: Modules 5-6  
* Day 4: Modules 7-8  
* Day 5: Modules 9-10  
* Day 6: Modules 11-12 \+ practical rubric prep

## **Course Overview**

**Scope:** This course establishes non-coder boundaries for operational roles interacting with ICD-10-CM codes in benefits, authorization, claims, denials, and documentation workflows. Covers code purpose, structure, specificity, laterality, acute/chronic distinctions, encounter types, medical necessity, denial drivers, clinical documentation reading, safe boundaries, data hygiene, and plain-language communication. Scope creep into code selection is prohibited.

**What Good Looks Like:**

* Explains ICD-10 purpose without coding  
* Flags documentation gaps and routes to coder/provider  
* Translates denial reasons in plain language without mentioning codes unless policy allows  
* Drafts neutral provider queries without suggesting codes  
* Recognizes medical necessity vs coverage distinction

**Common Misconceptions and Failure Modes:**

* Scope creep into assigning codes — violates non-coder boundary  
* Treating unspecified codes as harmless — increases denial risk  
* Confusing medical necessity vs coverage — creates incorrect escalations  
* Inferring laterality or specificity without documentation — prohibited

## **Role Alignment**

**Client Success Specialist (Medical Benefits):** Modules 1-12 (Standard for revenue cycle roles)  
 **Order Entry Specialist:** Modules 1-12 (focus on laterality, missing diagnosis routing)  
 **Patient Claims Specialist:** Modules 1-12 (focus on denials and medical necessity)  
 **Patient Accounts Receivable Specialist:** Modules 1-12 (focus on plain-language denial explanation boundaries)  
 **Accounts Receivable Executive (Patient Balance Collections):** Modules 1-12 (focus on patient communication scripts and escalation)  
 **Medical Scribe (MBBS):** Modules 1-12 only if assigned to diagnosis-awareness workflows

**Do-Not-Do Boundaries (Universal):**

* Do not select or change codes independently  
* Do not suggest specific codes in provider queries  
* Do not promise coverage or approval based on code observation  
* Do not classify conditions without provider/coder confirmation

## **Required Learner Artifacts**

1. Touchpoint map (Module 1\)  
2. Parsed code worksheets (Module 2\)  
3. Provider query drafts (Modules 3, 4, 9\)  
4. Denial root-cause worksheets (Module 8\)  
5. Boundary decision log (Module 10\)  
6. Documentation gap identification exercises (Module 9\)  
7. Plain-language translation set (Module 12\)

## **Module List**

**Module 1:** ICD-10-CM Purpose and Role in Healthcare Operations (45 min)  
 **Module 2:** Code Structure and Format Basics (60 min)  
 **Module 3:** Specificity and Unspecified Codes (75 min)  
 **Module 4:** Laterality and Bilateral Coding (60 min)  
 **Module 5:** Acute vs Chronic Conditions (60 min)  
 **Module 6:** Encounter Type and Extensions (45 min)  
 **Module 7:** Medical Necessity and Diagnosis Selection (90 min)  
 **Module 8:** Common Denial Drivers Related to Diagnosis Coding (75 min)  
 **Module 9:** Reading Clinical Documentation for Specificity (90 min)  
 **Module 10:** Safe Boundaries: What Non-Coders Can and Cannot Do (60 min)  
 **Module 11:** Diagnosis-Related Data Hygiene in Tickets and Notes (45 min)  
 **Module 12:** Communicating Diagnosis-Related Issues in Plain Language (45 min)

---

# **COURSE 3: DAY-TO-DAY DOCUMENT HYGIENE AND DATA HANDLING (OPERATIONAL SECURITY)**

## **Course Header**

**Course Number:** 3  
 **Course Name:** Day-to-Day Document Hygiene and Data Handling (Operational Security)  
 **Purpose:** Establish clean screen/desk habits, correct storage, redaction, channel use, screenshot discipline, and timely updates across all operational workflows.

**Audience:** All roles

**Prerequisites:** Course 1 first

**Duration:** Standard 8 hours

**Entry-Level Day Plan (Standard 8h):**

* Day 1: Modules 1-3  
* Day 2: Modules 4-6  
* Day 3: Modules 7-9  
* Day 4: Modules 10-12  
* Day 5: Modules 13-15  
* Day 6: Modules 16-18 \+ practical prep

## **Course Overview**

**Scope:** 18 modules covering daily operational security habits: clean screen/desk protocols, file storage and retention, redaction before sharing, approved channel usage, screenshot prohibitions, status update discipline, secure disposal, version control, metadata scrubbing, print controls, mobile device restrictions, download controls, folder organization, naming conventions, archive procedures, recovery protocols, audit response, and data lifecycle management.

**What Good Looks Like:**

* Clean screen/desk maintained during and after work  
* Correct storage location used for all files  
* Redaction applied before sharing  
* Approved channels used exclusively  
* No screenshots of PHI screens  
* Timely status updates completed  
* Secure disposal executed  
* Version control maintained

**Common Misconceptions and Failure Modes:**

* "Screenshots are fastest" — violates PHI controls regardless of speed  
* "Shared folders are secure enough" — requires client-specific approval (needs\_review)  
* "I'll update later" — creates audit gaps and compliance exposure  
* "Deleting is disposal" — secure disposal protocols required

## **Role Alignment**

**All roles complete all modules 1-18.**

**Do-Not-Do Boundaries (Universal):**

* No screenshots of PHI screens under any circumstance  
* No unapproved channels for PHI communication  
* No delayed updates beyond shift end  
* No personal device storage of work files  
* No disposal without secure method confirmation

## **Required Learner Artifacts**

1. Workspace photos (module-specific)  
2. Redacted file submissions  
3. Cleanup reports  
4. Update status reports  
5. Template completions  
6. Drill scores (all 18 modules)  
7. Channel selection accuracy logs  
8. Storage location verification exercises

## **Module List**

**Modules 1-18:** Each module follows standardized structure with entry-level primer, definitions, step-by-step procedures, worked examples (2 compliant, 1 non-compliant), practice pack (drills, scenarios, mini-sim, checklist), knowledge check upgrades, and QA/audit hooks.

**Module 1:** Clean Screen and Clean Desk Protocols  
 **Module 2:** File Storage and Retention Standards  
 **Module 3:** Redaction Before Sharing  
 **Module 4:** Approved Channel Usage  
 **Module 5:** Screenshot Prohibition and Alternatives  
 **Module 6:** Status Update Discipline  
 **Module 7:** Secure Disposal Procedures  
 **Module 8:** Version Control Requirements  
 **Module 9:** Metadata Scrubbing  
 **Module 10:** Print Controls  
 **Module 11:** Mobile Device Restrictions  
 **Module 12:** Download Controls  
 **Module 13:** Folder Organization Standards  
 **Module 14:** Naming Conventions  
 **Module 15:** Archive Procedures  
 **Module 16:** Recovery Protocols  
 **Module 17:** Audit Response Preparation  
 **Module 18:** Data Lifecycle Management

---

# **COURSE 4: MEDICAL SCRIBE TRAINING (REMOTE, CLINICAL DOCUMENTATION QUALITY)**

## **Course Header**

**Course Number:** 4  
 **Course Name:** Medical Scribe Training (Remote, Clinical Documentation Quality)  
 **Purpose:** Train Medical Scribes in documentation-only scope, SOAP structure, specialty terminology, and escalation boundaries for remote clinical documentation.

**Audience:** Medical Scribe (MBBS) only

**Prerequisites:** Course 1 Clinical Support variant \+ Course 3

**Duration:** Standard 20 hours

**Entry-Level Day Plan (Standard 20h across 10 days):**

* Days 1-2: Modules 1-4  
* Days 3-4: Modules 5-8  
* Day 5: Modules 9-12  
* Day 6: Modules 13-15  
* Day 7: Modules 16-18  
* Day 8: Modules 19-21  
* Day 9: Modules 22-24  
* Day 10: Modules 25-26 \+ practical prep

## **Course Overview**

**Scope:** 26 modules covering scribe role definition, SOAP note structure, medical terminology (200-term job aid support), specialty documentation standards, provider workflow support, escalation boundaries, real-time documentation discipline, quality metrics, error prevention, attestation protocols, audit readiness, compliance boundaries, remote workflow management, and specialty-specific templates.

**What Good Looks Like:**

* Documentation-only scope maintained (no clinical interpretation)  
* Consistent SOAP structure across all notes  
* No hallucinated facts (only documented provider statements)  
* Correct escalation language for ambiguities  
* Specialty terminology accurate and appropriate  
* Timely note completion within shift  
* Quality metrics met (accuracy, completeness, timeliness)

**Common Misconceptions and Failure Modes:**

* Interpreting clinical decisions instead of documenting — violates documentation-only scope  
* Adding assumptions not stated by provider — creates false documentation  
* Using terminology beyond training scope — accuracy risk  
* Delaying notes beyond shift end — creates continuity gaps

## **Role Alignment**

**Medical Scribe (MBBS) completes all modules 1-26 \+ specialty templates as assigned.**

**Do-Not-Do Boundaries:**

* Do not interpret or infer clinical decisions  
* Do not add information not stated by provider  
* Do not use terminology beyond confirmed understanding  
* Do not delay note completion beyond shift end  
* Do not modify provider statements for "clarity"

## **Required Learner Artifacts**

1. Note audits (module-specific, all 26 modules)  
2. Attestation simulation logs  
3. Timed accuracy scores  
4. Boundary scenario scores  
5. Specialty template completions  
6. SOAP structure consistency checks  
7. Terminology accuracy assessments  
8. Real-time documentation simulations

## **Module List**

**Modules 1-26:** Each module follows standardized structure with entry-level primer (including specialty terms from 200-term job aid), step-by-step procedures, worked examples from module scenario library, practice pack with timed drills and peer review, knowledge checks with common wrong answers, and QA hooks (note audits, attestation simulation logs, timed accuracy scores, boundary scenario scores).

**Module 1:** Scribe Role Definition and Boundaries  
 **Module 2:** SOAP Note Structure Fundamentals

# **COURSE 5: EXECUTIVE ASSISTANT TRAINING FOR HEALTHCARE OPERATIONS (COMPLIANCE-SAFE)**

## **Course Header**

**Course Number:** 5  
 **Course Name:** Executive Assistant Training for Healthcare Operations (Compliance-Safe)  
 **Purpose:** Train Executive Assistants in PHI-free calendar management, triage without over-reading, verification, and redacted notes distribution.

**Audience:** Executive Assistant only

**Prerequisites:** Course 1 Executive Support variant \+ Course 3

**Duration:** Standard 10 hours

**Entry-Level Day Plan (5 days):**

* Day 1: Modules 1-3  
* Day 2: Modules 4-6  
* Day 3: Modules 7-9  
* Day 4: Modules 10-12  
* Day 5: Modules 13-15 \+ practical prep

## **Course Overview**

**Scope:** 15 modules covering executive support role boundaries, PHI-free calendar management, meeting preparation without over-reading, inbox triage with minimum necessary, document preparation and redaction, attendee list limitation, verification protocols for executive requests, notes distribution controls, travel coordination, expense management boundaries, confidentiality during support tasks, escalation for ambiguous requests, audit readiness for executive support documentation, vendor interaction protocols, and professional communication standards.

**What Good Looks Like:**

* PHI-free calendars maintained (no patient names or case details in subjects)  
* Triage without over-reading PHI (minimum necessary during routing)  
* Correct routing and verification applied  
* Redacted notes distributed appropriately (attendee list limited to need-to-know)  
* Professional boundaries maintained during executive support

**Common Misconceptions and Failure Modes:**

* "Calendar is internal so PHI is safe" — broad visibility creates exposure  
* "I need to read everything to route" — minimum necessary applies to triage  
* "Executives can override verification" — verification rules are universal  
* "Notes should be comprehensive for all" — redaction required before broad distribution

## **Role Alignment**

**Executive Assistant completes all modules 1-15.**

**Do-Not-Do Boundaries:**

* Do not include patient identifiers in calendar subjects  
* Do not route to broad lists without redaction  
* Do not bypass verification for urgent executive requests  
* Do not disclose meeting content beyond need-to-know

## **Required Learner Artifacts**

1. Calendar audit routine completions (using generic calendar templates job aid)  
2. Recipient limitation checklists  
3. Script pack demonstrations (safe refusal, verification)  
4. Redaction submissions (meeting notes, documents)  
5. Triage accuracy logs  
6. Verification simulation scores  
7. Escalation documentation exercises

## **Module List**

**Modules 1-15:** Each module maintains source activities and checks, adds script packs (safe refusal, verification), recipient limitation checklists, and calendar audit routine using generic calendar templates job aid.

**Module 1:** Executive Support Role Boundaries in Healthcare  
 **Module 2:** PHI-Free Calendar Management

 **Module 14:** Vendor Interaction Protocols  
 **Module 15:** Professional Communication Standards

# **C) MODULE BUILDS**

## **COURSE 0 MODULE BUILDS**

### **MODULE 0.1: PROGRAM STRUCTURE AND DELIVERY MODES (20 MIN)**

#### **1\) Entry-Level Primer**

**Plain Language Summary:** Uplift's training system uses six courses (0-6) delivered through three modes: Self-Paced (you control timing), Instructor-Led (live sessions with trainer), and Blended (combination). Understanding delivery modes prevents scheduling confusion and ensures you complete training in the approved format.

**Observable Behaviors:**

* Identifies which delivery mode applies to assigned course  
* Schedules training sessions appropriately for delivery mode  
* Completes self-paced modules without skipping ahead of readiness checks

#### **2\) Definitions**

**Self-Paced Delivery Mode:** Learner progresses through modules independently at their own speed within deadline parameters. Used for Courses 0, 2 Essentials track, and Course 3\.

**Instructor-Led Delivery Mode:** Trainer facilitates live sessions with fixed schedule. Used for Course 1 Intensive track simulations and Course 4 specialty template workshops.

**Blended Delivery Mode:** Combination of self-paced modules and scheduled instructor sessions. Used for Course 1 Standard track and Course 6 role-specific modules.

**Course Sequence:** Mandatory order of completion (Course 0 → Course 1 → branching based on role).

**Duration Track:** Three intensity levels (Essentials, Standard, Intensive) with different hour requirements and content depth.

#### **3\) Step-by-Step Procedures**

**Procedure: Determine Your Delivery Mode and Duration Track**

1. Receive course assignment notification from training coordinator  
2. Confirm delivery mode listed in assignment (Self-Paced, Instructor-Led, or Blended)  
3. Confirm duration track assigned (Essentials, Standard, or Intensive)  
4. If Self-Paced: access course in learning management system and begin Module 1  
5. If Instructor-Led: confirm scheduled session dates and times with training coordinator  
6. If Blended: complete self-paced modules before scheduled live sessions  
7. Mark completion of each module in tracking system before proceeding to next  
8. If uncertain about mode or track: escalate to training coordinator before starting

**Safe Stop Rules:**

* Stop if delivery mode is unclear — do not guess  
* Stop if you cannot access assigned course — technical issue requires escalation  
* Stop if scheduled session conflicts with operational needs — reschedule before deadline

**Escalation Path:** Training coordinator → Supervisor → Compliance lead (if deadline at risk)

**Documentation Requirements:**

* Log access timestamps for self-paced modules  
* Confirm attendance for instructor-led sessions  
* Submit completion acknowledgment for blended tracks

#### **4\) Worked Examples**

**Compliant Example 1:** Learner assigned Course 0 Self-Paced. Accesses learning system, completes Module 0.1, marks complete, proceeds to Module 0.2 only after 0.1 completion confirmed in system.

**Why Compliant:** Follows self-paced sequence without skipping prerequisites.

**Compliant Example 2:** Learner assigned Course 1 Standard (Blended). Completes Modules 1-12 self-paced before attending scheduled role variant live session on Day 4\.

**Why Compliant:** Respects blended model by completing self-paced foundation before live component.

**Non-Compliant Example:** Learner assigned Course 1 Intensive but attempts Standard track to save time. Misses required simulations and policy writing workshop.

**Why Non-Compliant:** Changing assigned duration track without approval creates training gaps and audit risk.

#### **5\) Practice Pack**

**Drill Set (5 Repetitions):** Match scenarios to correct delivery mode (Self-Paced, Instructor-Led, Blended)

1. Course 0 completion \= Self-Paced  
2. Course 1 Module 13 role variant session \= Instructor-Led component of Blended  
3. Course 2 Standard track \= Self-Paced with optional instructor support  
4. Course 4 specialty templates workshop \= Instructor-Led component  
5. Course 3 all modules \= Self-Paced

**Scenario Exercise:** **Scenario:** You are assigned Course 1 Standard track. Day 1 modules 1-4 are self-paced. Day 4 includes scheduled role variant session. You complete modules 1-4 on Day 1 but skip Day 2-3 modules and attend Day 4 session.

**Question:** What is the error and how do you correct it?

**Answer:** Error is skipping prerequisite modules 5-12 before Day 4 session. Correction: reschedule Day 4 session until modules 5-12 completed.

**Mini-Simulation Script:** **Trainer plays:** Training coordinator  
 **Learner plays:** New hire

**Trainer:** "You're assigned Course 1 Standard track starting Monday. It's blended delivery."

**Learner expected actions:**

* Confirm start date  
* Ask which modules are self-paced vs instructor-led  
* Confirm scheduled live session dates and times  
* Confirm prerequisite modules required before live sessions

**Checklist: Delivery Mode Readiness**

* \[ \] Delivery mode confirmed (Self-Paced / Instructor-Led / Blended)  
* \[ \] Duration track confirmed (Essentials / Standard / Intensive)  
* \[ \] Course sequence position verified (prerequisites completed)  
* \[ \] Access to learning system confirmed  
* \[ \] If Blended: live session dates scheduled  
* \[ \] Deadline understood and realistic  
* \[ \] Escalation path known if issues arise

**Scoring Rubric:**

* Delivery mode identification: 2 points  
* Duration track identification: 2 points  
* Sequence awareness: 2 points  
* Checklist completion: 4 points  
* **Total: 10 points (8/10 \= 80% passing)**

#### **6\) Knowledge Check (10 Items)**

**Item 1 (MCQ):** Course 0 uses which delivery mode? A) Instructor-Led  
 B) Self-Paced  
 C) Blended  
 D) Hybrid

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Source states Course 0 is self-paced orientation.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** C (Blended) — confusion with Course 1 Standard track.

**Item 2 (MCQ):** What does "Blended" delivery mode mean? A) Mix of online and in-person  
 B) Mix of self-paced and instructor-led  
 C) Optional attendance at live sessions  
 D) Choose your own schedule

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Blended combines self-paced modules with scheduled instructor sessions.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** A — "online vs in-person" is not the distinguishing feature; both components can be online.

**Item 3 (True/False):** You can switch from Standard to Essentials track if Standard seems too long.

**Answer:** False  
 **Rationale:** Duration track is assigned based on role requirements; changing without approval creates training gaps.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** True — belief that tracks are learner preference rather than requirement.

**Item 4 (MCQ):** Course 1 Intensive track includes which component not in Standard? A) Role variant modules  
 B) Live simulations  
 C) Final exam  
 D) Core modules 1-12

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Intensive adds live simulations and policy writing workshop.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** A — role variants are in all tracks.

**Item 5 (Ordering):** Arrange course sequence correctly: A) Course 1 → Course 0 → Course 3  
 B) Course 0 → Course 3 → Course 1  
 C) Course 0 → Course 1 → Course 3  
 D) Course 3 → Course 0 → Course 1

**Answer:** C  
 **Rationale:** Source mandates Course 0 first, Course 1 second, Course 3 after Course 1\.

**Item 6 (Scenario MCQ):** You are assigned Course 2 Standard (8 hours). Your supervisor says "just skim it in 2 hours." What do you do? A) Skim as directed to save time  
 B) Complete all 8 hours as assigned  
 C) Ask to switch to Essentials track  
 D) Skip Course 2 entirely

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Duration track requirements are audit standards; supervisor directive does not override.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** A — "following supervisor" seems correct but creates compliance gap.

**Item 7 (MCQ):** Self-Paced delivery means: A) No deadlines  
 B) Learner controls timing within deadline parameters  
 C) Optional completion  
 D) Faster than Instructor-Led

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Self-paced provides timing flexibility within required completion deadlines.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** A — "no deadlines" misunderstands flexibility.

**Item 8 (True/False):** Instructor-Led sessions can be rescheduled anytime without notice.

**Answer:** False  
 **Rationale:** Rescheduling requires coordination with training coordinator and impacts other learners.

**Item 9 (MCQ):** If your delivery mode is unclear in the assignment, you should: A) Assume Self-Paced  
 B) Escalate to training coordinator  
 C) Ask a colleague  
 D) Skip until clarified

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Safe stop rule requires escalation for delivery mode uncertainty.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** A — assuming creates risk of wrong mode.

**Item 10 (Short Answer):** Name the three duration tracks.

**Answer:** Essentials, Standard, Intensive  
 **Rationale:** Source defines three tracks with different hour requirements.

#### **7\) QA and Audit Hooks**

**Evidence of Competence:**

* Quiz score (10 items, 80% passing \= 8/10)  
* Delivery mode identification accuracy  
* Checklist completion timestamp

**Supervisor Review Checklist:**

* \[ \] Learner accessed correct delivery mode  
* \[ \] Learner completed prerequisites before live sessions (if Blended)  
* \[ \] Learner documented any scheduling conflicts  
* \[ \] Learner escalated uncertainties appropriately

**Recordkeeping Tie-Back:**

* Module 0.1 completion timestamp logged in training records system  
* Delivery mode confirmed field populated  
* Duration track confirmed field populated

### **MODULE 0.2: PASSING STANDARDS, ATTEMPTS, AND COOLING PERIODS (15 MIN)**

#### **1\) Entry-Level Primer**

**Plain Language Summary:** Every assessment (quiz, practical, simulation) has a passing standard (usually 80%). You get limited attempts (usually 2-3). If you fail all attempts, a cooling period (waiting time) applies before retest. Understanding these rules prevents unexpected training delays and termination risk.

**Observable Behaviors:**

* Checks passing standard before starting assessment  
* Tracks attempt count remaining  
* Schedules cooling period retest within policy timeframe  
* Does not attempt to bypass attempt limits

#### **2\) Definitions**

**Passing Standard:** Minimum score required to pass an assessment (expressed as percentage, e.g., 80% means 8 correct out of 10 items).

**Attempt:** Single completion of an assessment counting toward attempt limit.

**Attempt Limit:** Maximum number of tries allowed before cooling period or escalation (typically 2-3 attempts depending on assessment type).

**Cooling Period:**

Mandatory waiting period (typically 24-48 hours or as specified by policy — needs\_review for client-specific timeframes) after exhausting attempts before retest eligibility.

**Remediation Plan:** Required training intervention after cooling period before retest, addressing specific knowledge gaps.

#### **3\) Step-by-Step Procedures**

**Procedure: Take an Assessment with Attempt Limits**

1. Review passing standard displayed at assessment start (typically 80%)  
2. Confirm attempt count displayed (e.g., "Attempt 1 of 3")  
3. Complete assessment within time limit if applicable  
4. Submit assessment and view score immediately  
5. If passing standard met: proceed to next module  
6. If passing standard not met and attempts remain: review missed items, study relevant module content, attempt again  
7. If passing standard not met and no attempts remain: note cooling period start date automatically  
8. During cooling period: complete assigned remediation activities (targeted study, meeting with supervisor)  
9. After cooling period ends: contact training coordinator to schedule retest  
10. If retest fails: escalate to supervisor for performance improvement plan discussion

**Safe Stop Rules:**

* Stop if assessment instructions are unclear — ask training coordinator before attempting  
* Stop if technical error occurs during assessment — report immediately; attempt may not count  
* Stop if cooling period end date is uncertain — confirm with training coordinator before retest

**Escalation Path:** Training coordinator → Supervisor → HR (if multiple cooling periods occur)

**Documentation Requirements:**

* Assessment score logged automatically in system  
* Cooling period start/end dates recorded  
* Remediation activities documented in training record  
* Retest score logged separately from initial attempts

#### **4\) Worked Examples**

**Compliant Example 1:** Learner takes Module 1 quiz (10 items, 80% passing, 3 attempts allowed). Scores 70% on Attempt 1\. Reviews module content focusing on missed questions. Scores 90% on Attempt 2\. Proceeds to Module 2\.

**Why Compliant:** Used attempt structure correctly, studied between attempts, met passing standard within limit.

**Compliant Example 2:** Learner fails practical evaluation after 3 attempts. Cooling period is 48 hours. Learner completes remediation exercises during cooling period. After 48 hours, contacts training coordinator, schedules retest, passes with 85%.

**Why Compliant:** Respected cooling period, completed remediation, followed retest procedure.

**Non-Compliant Example:** Learner fails quiz after 3 attempts. Creates new user account to bypass cooling period and retake immediately.

**Why Non-Compliant:** Attempt to circumvent attempt limits and cooling period violates policy and creates audit fraud risk. Results in sanctions (potentially immediate termination per acceleration clause).

#### **5\) Practice Pack**

**Drill Set (8 Repetitions):** Calculate passing score for different assessment sizes:

1. 10 items, 80% standard \= 8 correct required  
2. 20 items, 80% standard \= 16 correct required  
3. 15 items, 90% standard \= 14 correct required (round up)  
4. 25 items, 80% standard \= 20 correct required  
5. 12 items, 80% standard \= 10 correct required (round up from 9.6)  
6. 8 items, 100% standard \= 8 correct required  
7. 50 items, 80% standard \= 40 correct required  
8. 30 items, 85% standard \= 26 correct required (round up from 25.5)

**Scenario Exercise:** **Scenario:** You take Course 1 Module 4 verification simulation (passing standard 90%, 2 attempts allowed). Attempt 1 score: 85%. Attempt 2 score: 88%. No attempts remain. Cooling period is 24 hours.

**Question:** What are your next three steps?

**Answer:**

1. Note cooling period start date/time (automatic in system)  
2. Complete assigned remediation (review Module 4 verification procedures and script)  
3. After 24 hours, contact training coordinator to schedule retest

**Mini-Simulation Script:** **Trainer plays:** Training coordinator  
 **Learner plays:** Employee who failed quiz

**Trainer:** "You scored 75% on the Module 8 quiz. Passing is 80%. You have one attempt left."

**Learner expected actions:**

* Acknowledge score and remaining attempt  
* Ask which questions missed (if system does not show)  
* State plan to review Module 8 content before next attempt  
* Confirm no time restriction between attempts (unless policy specifies)  
* Confirm passing standard is still 80% for next attempt

**Checklist: Assessment Attempt Management**

* \[ \] Passing standard confirmed before starting  
* \[ \] Attempt count confirmed (e.g., 1 of 3\)  
* \[ \] If failed: identified missed questions or skill gaps  
* \[ \] If failed: reviewed relevant module content before next attempt  
* \[ \] If cooling period: documented start date  
* \[ \] If cooling period: completed remediation activities  
* \[ \] If cooling period: confirmed end date before requesting retest  
* \[ \] Retest scheduled through proper channel (training coordinator)

**Scoring Rubric:**

* Passing standard identification: 2 points  
* Attempt tracking: 2 points  
* Cooling period awareness: 2 points  
* Remediation completion: 2 points  
* Retest procedure: 2 points  
* **Total: 10 points (8/10 \= 80% passing)**

#### **6\) Knowledge Check (10 Items)**

**Item 1 (MCQ):** Typical passing standard for knowledge checks is: A) 70%  
 B) 75%  
 C) 80%  
 D) 90%

**Answer:** C  
 **Rationale:** Source states 80% as global gate for most assessments.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** D — 90% applies to specific practical simulations, not all assessments.

**Item 2 (MCQ):** You score 78% on a quiz with 80% passing standard. What happens? A) You pass  
 B) You fail and use one attempt  
 C) You get partial credit  
 D) You can appeal the score

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** 78% is below 80% passing standard; counts as failed attempt.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** C — no partial credit concept exists.

**Item 3 (True/False):** Cooling periods are optional if you feel ready to retest sooner.

**Answer:** False  
 **Rationale:** Cooling periods are mandatory waiting periods after attempt exhaustion.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** True — misunderstanding cooling period as suggestion.

**Item 4 (Calculation):** Quiz has 15 items, 80% passing standard. How many must you answer correctly?

**Answer:** 12  
 **Rationale:** 15 × 0.80 \= 12\.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** 11 — incorrect rounding or calculation.

**Item 5 (MCQ):** After failing 3 attempts, you must: A) Wait for cooling period to end  
 B) Request immediate retest  
 C) Start a new course  
 D) Skip to next module

**Answer:** A  
 **Rationale:** Cooling period is mandatory after exhausting attempts.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** B — immediate retest not allowed.

**Item 6 (Scenario MCQ):** You fail a practical evaluation twice (2 attempts allowed). Cooling period is 48 hours. You find another trainer willing to retest you after 24 hours. What do you do? A) Accept the 24-hour retest to save time  
 B) Decline and wait full 48 hours  
 C) Accept but don't tell training coordinator  
 D) Ask supervisor to waive cooling period

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Cooling period is non-negotiable policy; early retest creates audit violation.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** A — "saving time" is not a valid override.

**Item 7 (True/False):** Remediation during cooling period is optional.

**Answer:** False  
 **Rationale:** Remediation is required component of cooling period.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** True — treating remediation as suggestion.

**Item 8 (MCQ):** Attempt limits exist to: A) Punish slow learners  
 B) Ensure knowledge mastery before proceeding  
 C) Save training time  
 D) Reduce trainer workload

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Attempt limits ensure competence before role performance begins.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** A — negative framing misses competence protection purpose.

**Item 9 (MCQ):** If you score exactly 80% on a quiz with 80% passing standard, you: A) Fail  
 B) Pass  
 C) Need supervisor approval  
 D) Must retest

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Meeting passing standard exactly counts as pass.

**Item 10 (Short Answer):** You exhaust attempts on Module 6 quiz. List the three required steps before retest.

**Answer:**

1. Wait for cooling period to end  
2. Complete remediation activities  
3. Contact training coordinator to schedule retest

**Rationale:** Source requires cooling period, remediation, and proper retest scheduling.

#### **7\) QA and Audit Hooks**

**Evidence of Competence:**

* Quiz score (10 items, 80% passing)  
* Attempt management demonstrated (no bypass attempts)  
* Cooling period compliance (if applicable)

**Supervisor Review Checklist:**

* \[ \] Learner attempted assessments within attempt limits  
* \[ \] Learner respected cooling periods if applicable  
* \[ \] Learner completed remediation before retest  
* \[ \] Learner followed retest scheduling procedure

**Recordkeeping Tie-Back:**

* All attempt scores logged in training records  
* Cooling period start/end dates recorded  
* Remediation completion timestamp logged  
* Retest scores linked to original assessment record

---

### **MODULE 0.3: TRAINING RECORDS AND REFRESHER CADENCE (20 MIN)**

#### **1\) Entry-Level Primer**

**Plain Language Summary:** Every training activity generates a record with specific required fields (name, date, course, score, supervisor signature). These records prove compliance during audits. Additionally, training must be refreshed (repeated) based on four triggers plus client-specific cadence (needs\_review). Understanding recordkeeping prevents audit findings and ensures you know when retraining is due.

**Observable Behaviors:**

* Verifies training record fields are complete after each course  
* Tracks personal refresher due dates  
* Notifies supervisor when refresher becomes due  
* Completes refresher training within required timeframe

#### **2\) Definitions**

**Training Record:** Documentation of completed training activity containing all required fields for audit verification.

**Required Training Record Fields:** Employee name, employee ID, course name/number, completion date, delivery mode, duration track, assessment scores, attempt counts, cooling periods (if applicable), supervisor signature/approval, refresher due date.

**Refresher Training:** Repeat of training content at specified intervals to maintain competence and compliance.

**Refresher Trigger:** Event or timeframe requiring retraining (four universal triggers: annual calendar, role change, policy change, incident/audit finding; plus client-specific triggers needs\_review).

**Annual Refresher Cadence:** Training repeated every 12 months from initial completion date (universal baseline; client may require shorter intervals needs\_review).

**Role Change Trigger:** New or expanded job responsibilities requiring additional training modules.

**Policy Change Trigger:** Significant update to regulations, client policies, or Uplift procedures requiring retraining on affected content.

**Incident/Audit Finding Trigger:** Individual performance issue or audit gap requiring immediate targeted retraining.

**Client-Specific Refresher Cadence:** Shortened intervals required by specific clients (e.g., quarterly instead of annual; needs\_review for each client).

#### **3\) Step-by-Step Procedures**

**Procedure: Verify Training Record Completeness**

1. Complete all required course modules and assessments  
2. Receive training completion notification from learning management system  
3. Access your training record in system within 24 hours of completion  
4. Verify all required fields populated:  
   * Your name and employee ID correct  
   * Course name and number correct  
   * Completion date accurate  
   * Delivery mode documented  
   * Duration track documented  
   * All assessment scores recorded  
   * Attempt counts recorded (if multiple attempts occurred)  
   * Cooling periods documented (if applicable)  
   * Supervisor signature/approval present (electronic or manual)  
   * Refresher due date calculated and displayed  
5. If any field is missing or incorrect: report to training coordinator within 48 hours  
6. Print or save PDF copy of completed training record for personal records (optional but recommended)  
7. Note refresher due date in personal calendar with 30-day advance reminder

**Procedure: Track and Complete Refresher Training**

1. Identify applicable refresher triggers for your role:  
   * Annual trigger: 12 months from course completion date (or shorter per client needs\_review)  
   * Role change trigger: assignment to new responsibilities requiring additional training  
   * Policy change trigger: notification from compliance team of significant policy update  
   * Incident/audit trigger: notification from supervisor of required retraining  
2. When trigger occurs, verify refresher course assignment in learning management system  
3. If refresher not automatically assigned within 30 days of trigger: escalate to training coordinator  
4. Complete refresher training within assigned timeframe (typically 30 days for annual; 14 days for policy change; immediate for incident)  
5. Refresher completion generates new training record; verify fields as above  
6. New refresher due date calculated from refresher completion date

**Safe Stop Rules:**

* Stop if training record fields are incomplete — incomplete records fail audits  
* Stop if refresher due date is missing — cannot track compliance without date  
* Stop if refresher assignment is not received within expected timeframe — escalate immediately

**Escalation Path:** Training coordinator → Compliance lead → Client account manager (if client-specific issue)

**Documentation Requirements:**

* All training record fields completed per list above  
* Refresher completion documented separately from initial training (separate record)  
* Escalations regarding missing records or assignments documented in ticket system

#### **4\) Worked Examples**

**Compliant Example 1:** Employee completes Course 1 on March 15, 2024\. Training record shows completion date 3/15/2024, all assessment scores, supervisor approval, and refresher due date 3/15/2025 (annual trigger). Employee sets calendar reminder for 2/15/2025 (30 days in advance). On 2/15/2025, checks for refresher assignment, completes refresher by 3/15/2025, new due date becomes 3/15/2026.

**Why Compliant:** Verified record completeness, tracked refresher proactively, completed within timeframe.

**Compliant Example 2:** Employee receives notification of policy change affecting Course 1 Module 7 (email hygiene). Compliance team assigns Module 7 refresher with 14-day deadline. Employee completes within 10 days. Refresher record generated separately from initial Course 1 record.

**Why Compliant:** Responded to policy change trigger, completed within required timeframe, separate record maintained.

**Non-Compliant Example:** Employee completes Course 1 but does not verify training record. Two months later, audit request requires proof of training. Training record is missing supervisor signature field. Employee cannot produce complete record, creates audit finding.

**Why Non-Compliant:** Failed to verify record completeness within 24-48 hours of completion; record incompleteness discovered only during audit.

#### **5\) Practice Pack**

**Drill Set (Required Training Record Fields Memorization \- 10 Repetitions):** Recite all required fields from memory:

1. Employee name  
2. Employee ID  
3. Course name/number  
4. Completion date  
5. Delivery mode  
6. Duration track  
7. Assessment scores  
8. Attempt counts  
9. Cooling periods (if applicable)  
10. Supervisor signature/approval  
11. Refresher due date

**Scenario Exercise:** **Scenario:** You completed Course 3 on June 1, 2024\. Your client requires quarterly refreshers (every 3 months) for Course 3 instead of annual. Your training record shows refresher due date of June 1, 2025 (annual default). What is the error and what do you do?

**Answer:**  
 **Error:** Refresher due date calculated using annual default instead of client-specific quarterly requirement.  
 **Action:** Report discrepancy to training coordinator immediately. Request correction to September 1, 2024 (3 months from June 1, 2024). Set calendar reminder for August 1, 2024 to check for refresher assignment.

**Mini-Simulation Script:** **Trainer plays:** Training coordinator  
 **Learner plays:** Employee reviewing training record

**Trainer:** "I'm auditing your Course 1 record. Can you confirm all required fields are present?"

**Learner expected actions:**

* Access training record in system  
* Recite required fields list  
* Confirm each field is populated  
* Identify any missing or incorrect fields  
* If discrepancies found: report them during simulation  
* Show refresher due date and explain tracking method

**Checklist: Training Record Verification**

* \[ \] Employee name and ID correct  
* \[ \] Course name and number correct  
* \[ \] Completion date accurate  
* \[ \] Delivery mode documented  
* \[ \] Duration track documented  
* \[ \] All assessment scores recorded  
* \[ \] Attempt counts recorded (if applicable)  
* \[ \] Cooling periods documented (if applicable)  
* \[ \] Supervisor signature/approval present  
* \[ \] Refresher due date calculated and displayed  
* \[ \] Personal calendar reminder set for 30 days before due date  
* \[ \] Escalated any missing/incorrect fields within 48 hours

**Scoring Rubric:**

* Field identification: 6 points (11 fields, 0.5 points each, round up)  
* Verification process: 2 points  
* Refresher tracking: 2 points  
* **Total: 10 points (8/10 \= 80% passing)**

 **Common Wrong Answer:** B — missing one or two fields from count.

 B) 12 months  
 C) 18 months  
 D) 24 months

 **Common Wrong Answer:** D — confusing "annual" with "biennial."

 B) Role change  
 C) Employee request  
 D) Policy change

**Answer:** C  
 **Rationale:** Four universal triggers are annual, role change, policy change, incident/audit. Employee request is not a trigger.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** D — policy change IS a trigger.

 B) Audit finding; incomplete record  
 C) You must retake the course  
 D) Supervisor is disciplined, not you

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Incomplete training records create audit findings; learner is responsible for verifying within 24-48 hours of completion.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** A — signature is required field, not optional.

 B) Within 24 hours of completion  
 C) When refresher is due  
 D) Only if requested by supervisor

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Procedure requires verification within 24 hours (48 hours maximum) of completion.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** A — waiting until audit is too late to correct.

**Item 7 (MCQ):** Incident/audit finding trigger requires retraining: A) Annually  
 B) Quarterly  
 C) Immediately  
 D) Within 30 days

**Answer:** C  
 **Rationale:** Incident/audit triggers require immediate targeted retraining.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** D — 30 days applies to annual refresher, not incident trigger.

**Item 8 (True/False):** Refresher training completion generates a new training record separate from the initial training record.

**Answer:** True  
 **Rationale:** Source states refresher completion creates separate record; initial record remains for audit trail.

 B) Role change trigger  
 C) Policy change trigger  
 D) Incident trigger

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Role change trigger includes new responsibilities requiring additional training.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** A — annual trigger applies to courses already completed.

**Item 10 (Ordering):** Arrange these steps for refresher completion: A) Complete refresher → Verify new record → Set new calendar reminder → Identify trigger  
 B) Identify trigger → Complete refresher → Verify new record → Set new calendar reminder  
 C) Verify new record → Identify trigger → Complete refresher → Set new calendar reminder  
 D) Identify trigger → Set new calendar reminder → Complete refresher → Verify new record

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Logical sequence is trigger recognition → completion → verification → tracking.

**Item 11 (Short Answer):** Name the four universal refresher triggers.

**Answer:**

1. Annual calendar  
2. Role change  
3. Policy change  
4. Incident/audit finding

**Rationale:** Source lists these four plus client-specific as triggers.

**Item 12 (Scenario MCQ):** Your refresher is due March 1\. You receive the assignment February 15 with 30-day completion window. You are very busy. You complete it March 31\. What is the issue? A) No issue; completed within 30 days  
 B) Missed due date; should complete by March 1  
 C) Should request extension first  
 D) Supervisor should grant automatic extension

**Answer:** A  
 **Rationale:** 30-day completion window means 30 days from assignment (Feb 15), so deadline is March 17; March 31 is late. However, if "due date" means original trigger date (March 1\) and 30-day window starts from due date, then March 31 is within window. This is ambiguous; assuming 30-day window from assignment (Feb 15), March 31 is late.

**Corrected Answer: Scenario is ambiguous as written. If 30-day window starts from assignment date (Feb 15), deadline is March 17 and March 31 is late. If 30-day window starts from due date (March 1), deadline is March 31 and completion is on time. Best practice: complete before original due date (March 1\) when possible.**

For testing purposes:  
 **Revised Item 12 (Scenario MCQ):**  
 Your refresher is due March 1\. You receive the assignment February 15 with instruction to "complete by due date." You complete it March 5\. What is the issue? A) No issue if completed within 30 days of assignment  
 B) Missed due date of March 1  
 C) No due date applies to refreshers  
 D) Due date is flexible

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Instruction states "complete by due date" (March 1); March 5 is late.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** A — 30-day window does not override explicit "by due date" instruction.

### **MODULE 0.4: SANCTIONS PROCESS AND ACCOUNTABILITY (20 MIN)**

#### **1\) Entry-Level Primer**

**Plain Language Summary:** Uplift enforces training and compliance standards through a four-level sanctions process: counseling, written warning, final warning, termination. Sanctions apply to training failures (missed deadlines, failed attempts, policy violations during training) and operational compliance failures (incidents, breaches, repeat errors). High-severity failures involving PHI exposure or compliance violations can accelerate directly to termination regardless of prior history (acceleration clause). Understanding sanctions motivates compliance and prevents career-ending mistakes.

**Observable Behaviors:**

* Meets all training deadlines  
* Maintains passing standards on all assessments  
* Reports incidents and near-misses immediately  
* Cooperates with investigations  
* Does not retaliate against reporters  
* Understands which behaviors trigger which sanction levels

#### **2\) Definitions**

**Sanctions Process:** Progressive disciplinary framework with four escalating levels applied uniformly across all roles and tenure levels.

**First Occurrence \- Counseling:** Verbal or written counseling documenting the issue, expectations, and timeline for correction. No formal discipline on employment record but documented in training/compliance file.

**Second Occurrence \- Written Warning:** Formal written warning placed in employment file. Includes performance improvement plan with specific corrective actions and monitoring period (typically 30-60 days).

**Third Occurrence \- Final Warning:** Final written warning stating that any additional occurrence may result in termination. Monitoring period extended (typically 60-90 days). May include temporary restrictions on duties or access.

**Fourth Occurrence \- Termination:** Employment termination. Applies after exhausting three prior levels OR immediately under acceleration clause.

**Acceleration Clause:** High-severity failures involving PHI exposure, compliance violations, fraud, or intentional policy circumvention can skip directly to termination regardless of prior discipline history. Examples: creating fake training records, accessing patient records without authorization, sharing credentials, bypassing cooling periods through fraud, deleting evidence during investigations.

**Retaliation Prohibition:** Policy forbidding punishment, negative treatment, or discrimination against employees who report incidents, near-misses, policy violations, or compliance concerns. Retaliation itself triggers sanctions up to termination.

**Occurrence:** Single instance of training failure or compliance violation within a rolling 12-month window. Occurrences older than 12 months do not count toward progressive sanctions unless pattern demonstrates ongoing non-compliance.

#### **3\) Step-by-Step Procedures**

**Procedure: Understand How Sanctions Apply**

1. Review categories of sanctionable conduct:  
   * Training failures: missed deadlines, failed all attempts without completion, non-participation in required training  
   * Assessment integrity violations: cheating, having someone else take assessment, sharing answers  
   * Operational compliance failures: policy violations, incidents caused by negligence, repeat errors after training  
   * High-severity violations: PHI breaches, fraud, credential sharing, evidence tampering  
2. When any occurrence happens, expect supervisor notification within 5 business days  
3. Supervisor meeting will review:  
   * What happened (facts)  
   * Which policy/requirement was violated  
   * Sanction level applied based on occurrence count and severity  
   * Corrective actions required  
   * Timeline for completion  
   * Consequences of additional occurrences  
4. Sign acknowledgment of sanction (signature confirms receipt, not agreement)  
5. Complete corrective actions within specified timeline  
6. Document completion and submit to supervisor  
7. If occurrence qualifies for acceleration clause: expect immediate termination discussion; HR will be present

**Procedure: Report Without Fear of Retaliation**

1. Identify reportable concern (incident, near-miss, policy violation, unsafe practice)  
2. Report immediately through proper channel:  
   * Supervisor (first line)  
   * Compliance hotline (if supervisor is involved or unresponsive)  
   * HR (if retaliation concern exists)  
3. Provide factual description without speculation  
4. If you experience negative treatment after reporting:  
   * Document specific instances (dates, actions, witnesses)  
   * Report retaliation to HR immediately  
   * Retaliation investigation will be conducted separately  
5. Continue performing job duties professionally during any investigation

**Safe Stop Rules:**

* Stop if asked to falsify training records — report immediately; participation triggers termination  
* Stop if pressured to skip training or assessments — escalate to compliance  
* Stop if threatened for reporting concerns — document and escalate to HR

**Escalation Path:** Supervisor → HR → Compliance lead → Legal (for retaliation or high-severity violations)

**Documentation Requirements:**

* All sanctions documented in employee file with occurrence date, level, corrective actions, and completion status  
* Retaliation complaints investigated and documented separately  
* Acceleration clause invocations require written justification from compliance lead

#### **4\) Worked Examples**

**Compliant Example 1:** Employee misses Course 1 completion deadline due to unforeseen personal emergency. Notifies supervisor before deadline with documentation. Receives counseling (first occurrence) with extended deadline. Completes within extended timeline. No further occurrences in 12 months. After 12 months, occurrence no longer counts toward progressive discipline.

**Why Compliant:** Proactive communication, accepted accountability, completed corrective action, clean record after rolling 12-month period.

**Compliant Example 2:** Employee witnesses colleague accessing records without authorization (curiosity browsing). Reports to supervisor immediately. Investigation confirms violation. Colleague receives sanctions (potentially acceleration to termination depending on severity). Reporting employee experiences no negative consequences; retaliation prohibition protects reporter.

**Why Compliant:** Immediate reporting of serious violation, cooperation with investigation, reporter protected.

**Non-Compliant Example:** Employee fails Course 1 after exhausting all attempts and cooling period. Instead of completing remediation and retest, creates new user account to take assessment under different name and passes. Fraud is discovered during routine audit. Immediate termination under acceleration clause (fraud/circumvention of controls).

**Why Non-Compliant:** Intentional circumvention of policy, fraud, assessment integrity violation. Acceleration clause applies regardless of no prior discipline history.

#### **5\) Practice Pack**

**Drill Set (Sanction Level Matching \- 10 Scenarios):**

1. First missed training deadline with valid reason → Counseling  
2. Second failed practical after remediation → Written Warning  
3. Accessing celebrity patient record out of curiosity → Termination (acceleration clause)  
4. Third occurrence of incomplete documentation → Final Warning  
5. Sharing password with colleague to meet deadline → Termination (acceleration clause)  
6. Fourth occurrence of late status updates → Termination (progressive)  
7. Deleting incident evidence after being told to preserve → Termination (acceleration clause)  
8. First occurrence of verification script abandonment → Counseling  
9. Creating fake training completion certificate → Termination (acceleration clause)  
10. Second occurrence of using unapproved communication channel → Written Warning

**Scenario Exercise:** **Scenario:** You receive written warning (second occurrence) for missing Course 2 deadline. Three weeks later, you accidentally send PHI to wrong recipient via approved channel, immediately report incident, preserve evidence, and cooperate fully with investigation. Investigation finds no negligence; was honest mistake. What sanction level applies?

**Answer:**  
 Depends on investigation findings. If truly accidental with proper immediate response and no negligence pattern, may receive counseling or written warning (third occurrence) rather than termination. However, if PHI exposure was due to not following trained procedures (e.g., skipping recipient verification from Module 7), could be treated as higher severity with potential for final warning (third occurrence) or acceleration consideration if exposure was significant. Immediate reporting and evidence preservation are mitigating factors.

**Best Answer:** Third occurrence \= Final Warning, given immediate reporting and cooperation. Acceleration unlikely if procedures were followed and error was truly inadvertent.

**Mini-Simulation Script:** **Trainer plays:** Supervisor conducting sanctions meeting  
 **Learner plays:** Employee receiving written warning (second occurrence)

**Trainer:** "This is your second occurrence in six months. Last time was counseling for missed deadline. This time you failed Module 8 phishing simulation after remediation. This is a written warning. Here's your performance improvement plan. You have 30 days to complete Module 8 refresher and pass simulation at 90%. Any additional training or compliance failures in the next 12 months will result in final warning or termination depending on severity. Do you understand?"

**Learner expected actions:**

* Listen without interrupting  
* Ask clarifying questions about corrective actions  
* Confirm timeline (30 days)  
* Acknowledge consequence of additional occurrences  
* Sign acknowledgment form  
* Do NOT argue or make excuses during meeting (can provide context, but accept accountability)  
* Schedule Module 8 refresher immediately after meeting

**Checklist: Sanctions Awareness**

* \[ \] Understand four sanction levels (counseling, written warning, final warning, termination)  
* \[ \] Understand acceleration clause triggers (PHI exposure, fraud, circumvention)  
* \[ \] Understand 12-month rolling window for occurrence counting  
* \[ \] Understand retaliation prohibition protects reporters  
* \[ \] Know escalation path for reporting concerns  
* \[ \] Know escalation path for retaliation complaints  
* \[ \] Understand sanctions apply regardless of role or tenure  
* \[ \] Understand corrective actions must be completed within timeline

**Scoring Rubric:**

* Sanction level identification: 3 points  
* Acceleration clause understanding: 2 points  
* Retaliation prohibition: 2 points  
* Occurrence counting: 2 points  
* Reporting procedures: 1 point  
* **Total: 10 points (8/10 \= 80% passing)**

 B) Final warning  
 C) Termination

 **Common Wrong Answer:** B — final warning is still progressive, not acceleration.

**Answer:** False  
 **Rationale:** Source states sanctions apply regardless of role or tenure; uniform application.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** True — believing tenure provides protection.
