 B) Failing assessment twice  
 C) Sharing your password with colleague  
 D) Requesting deadline extension

**Answer:** C  
 **Rationale:** Credential sharing is high-severity compliance violation triggering acceleration.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** B — failing assessments is progressive, not acceleration (unless fraud involved).

**Item 5 (MCQ):** Retaliation prohibition protects employees who: A) Fail training repeatedly  
 B) Report incidents and compliance concerns  
 C) Violate policies  
 D) Miss deadlines

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Retaliation prohibition protects reporters of incidents, near-misses, and compliance concerns.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** A — policy violations are not protected conduct.

**Item 6 (Scenario MCQ):** You received counseling 14 months ago for late documentation. Today you miss a training deadline. What sanction level applies? A) Counseling (first occurrence)  
 B) Written warning (second occurrence)  
 C) Final warning  
 D) Termination

**Answer:** A  
 **Rationale:** 12-month rolling window means 14-month-old occurrence no longer counts; today's is first occurrence.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** B — not understanding rolling window resets occurrence count.

**Item 7 (MCQ):** During sanctions meeting, you should: A) Argue why the sanction is unfair  
 B) Listen, ask clarifying questions, sign acknowledgment  
 C) Refuse to sign until you consult a lawyer  
 D) Demand to speak to HR immediately

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Professional response is to listen, clarify, acknowledge receipt (signature is not agreement with sanction).  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** C — signature confirms receipt, not agreement; refusal does not prevent sanction.

**Item 8 (True/False):** If you report an incident, your supervisor can give you a poor performance review as punishment.

**Answer:** False  
 **Rationale:** Retaliation prohibition forbids negative treatment for reporting.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** True — not understanding retaliation protection scope.

**Item 9 (MCQ):** Third occurrence in the progressive framework results in: A) Counseling  
 B) Written warning  
 C) Final warning  
 D) Termination

**Answer:** C  
 **Rationale:** Progressive sequence is counseling → written warning → final warning → termination.

**Item 10 (MCQ):** Which action does NOT trigger acceleration clause? A) Deleting incident emails  
 B) Accessing records without authorization  
 C) Failing refresher training after three attempts  
 D) Creating fake training certificates

**Answer:** C  
 **Rationale:** Failing assessments is progressive discipline; others are fraud/high-severity.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** B — unauthorized access triggers acceleration.

**Item 11 (Short Answer):** You witness a colleague bypassing verification steps under pressure. What are your two immediate actions?

**Answer:**

1. Report to supervisor immediately  
2. Do not confront colleague directly; allow investigation process

**Rationale:** Immediate reporting is required; direct confrontation may compromise investigation or create conflict.

**Item 12 (Scenario MCQ):** You receive final warning (third occurrence). One month later, you have a minor incident (sent email with wrong subject line format, immediately corrected). What is the likely consequence? A) Verbal reminder, no formal sanction  
 B) Additional counseling  
 C) Termination (fourth occurrence)  
 D) Final warning extended

**Answer:** C  
 **Rationale:** Fourth occurrence after final warning typically results in termination per progressive framework.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** A — final warning status means any additional occurrence may result in termination; severity is evaluated but fourth occurrence is termination unless investigation finds no policy violation.

### **MODULE 0.5: CORE DEFINITIONS (PHI, ePHI, MINIMUM NECESSARY, INCIDENT, BREACH) (30 MIN)**

#### **1\) Entry-Level Primer**

**Plain Language Summary:** Five core definitions underpin all six courses: PHI (protected health information \= identifiers \+ health/payment context), ePHI (electronic PHI), Minimum Necessary (use/disclose only what's needed for the task), Incident (any policy violation or risk event including near-misses), Breach (incident involving unsecured PHI posing significant risk, determined by privacy officer). Precise definitions prevent confusion and ensure consistent application across all training.

**Observable Behaviors:**

* Correctly identifies PHI in mixed content  
* Distinguishes ePHI from paper PHI in handling decisions  
* Applies Minimum Necessary before sharing or documenting  
* Recognizes incidents even when no harm occurred  
* Does not self-determine breach status; escalates for determination

#### **2\) Definitions**

**PHI (Protected Health Information):** Information (oral, written, or electronic) that:

1. Identifies or can identify an individual (contains direct or indirect identifiers such as name, MRN, account number, contact info, dates tied to care, etc.), AND  
2. Relates to individual's health condition, healthcare provision, or healthcare payment

**Examples of PHI:**

* Patient name \+ diagnosis  
* Account number \+ appointment reason  
* Photo containing patient \+ clinic location  
* Email address \+ claim number  
* Voicemail containing patient name \+ test results

**Direct Identifiers:** Name, MRN, SSN, account number, phone number, email, address, photo, biometrics, IP address, device IDs.

**Indirect Identifiers:** Age (if rare), dates (birth, admission, discharge, death if tied to care), geographic subdivisions smaller than state (if population \< 20,000).

**ePHI (Electronic Protected Health Information):** PHI in electronic form, including information created, stored, transmitted, or received electronically. Includes data in computer systems, emails, text messages, portal messages, scanned documents, digital photos, databases, electronic health records.

**Distinction from paper PHI:** ePHI requires specific technical safeguards (encryption, access controls, audit logs) in addition to physical safeguards. Handling procedures may differ (e.g., secure deletion vs shredding).

**Minimum Necessary Standard:** Requirement to use, disclose, and request only the minimum amount of PHI reasonably needed to accomplish the intended purpose. Applies to:

* Documentation (include only necessary identifiers and details)  
* Communication (share only what recipient needs for their role)  
* Access requests (request only necessary permissions)

**Does NOT apply to:**

* Treatment activities (providers may access all relevant PHI for treatment)  
* Disclosures to patient themselves or their authorized representative  
* Disclosures required by law

**Incident:** Any use, access, or disclosure of PHI that violates policy or creates risk, including near-misses (events that could have resulted in violation but were caught/stopped in time). Examples:

* Wrong recipient email (sent or caught before sending)  
* Unauthorized access to records  
* Lost/stolen device with PHI  
* Verification failure followed by disclosure  
* Workstation left unlocked in presence of unauthorized person  
* Unapproved channel usage

**Key principle:** Incidents include near-misses; do not wait for harm to occur before reporting.

**Breach:** An incident involving the acquisition, access, use, or disclosure of unsecured PHI that poses a significant risk of financial, reputational, or other harm to the individual, as determined by the client's privacy officer (not by staff member). Requires specific notification procedures including patient notification, regulatory reporting, and potential public disclosure depending on scope.

**Key principle:** Staff report incidents; privacy officer determines if incident rises to breach level. Staff never self-determine breach status.

**Unsecured PHI:** PHI not rendered unusable, unreadable, or indecipherable to unauthorized persons through encryption or destruction per federal standards. (Needs\_review for specific client encryption requirements and safe harbor standards.)

#### **3\) Step-by-Step Procedures**

**Procedure: Identify PHI in Mixed Content**

1. Examine content (document, email, screen, conversation)  
2. Scan for identifiers:  
   * Names (patient, guarantor, family member if linked to patient)  
   * Numbers (MRN, account, claim, SSN, phone, insurance ID)  
   * Contact info (email, address)  
   * Dates tied to care or payment (appointment, admission, DOB, etc.)  
   * Photos or other identifying media  
3. Scan for health or payment context:  
   * Diagnosis, symptoms, treatment  
   * Medications, test results, procedures  
   * Claim status, payment, billing  
   * Insurance coverage, benefits  
4. If BOTH identifier AND health/payment context present: treat as PHI  
5. If identifier only (no health/payment context): still sensitive but may not be PHI (e.g., patient name in directory without medical context)  
6. If health/payment context only (no identifier): may be sensitive but not PHI (e.g., "patient with diabetes" in training without any identifiers)  
7. When uncertain: treat as PHI and escalate for confirmation

**Procedure: Apply Minimum Necessary Standard**

1. Identify purpose of use, disclosure, or access  
2. Ask: "What is the minimum information needed to accomplish this specific purpose?"  
3. Remove or redact:  
   * Unnecessary identifiers (e.g., if account number suffices, remove name)  
   * Unnecessary clinical details (e.g., if verifying eligibility, omit diagnosis)  
   * Unnecessary dates or contacts  
4. Document using generic terms where possible (e.g., "pt" instead of full name in operational notes)  
5. When communicating, confirm recipient's need-to-know before sharing  
6. If unable to determine minimum necessary: escalate to supervisor with proposed scope

**Procedure: Recognize and Report Incidents**

1. Observe or become aware of potential policy violation or risk event  
2. Ask: "Did this involve PHI? Was policy followed correctly? Was there risk of unauthorized access/disclosure?"  
3. If yes to any question: treat as incident  
4. Include near-misses: "Almost sent to wrong recipient" is reportable incident  
5. Report immediately using incident reporting procedure (Module 10\)  
6. Do NOT self-assess whether incident is a breach  
7. Cooperate with investigation  
8. If you caused the incident: report anyway (self-reporting is protected and expected)

**Safe Stop Rules:**

* Stop if uncertain whether content contains PHI — treat as PHI until confirmed otherwise  
* Stop if uncertain about Minimum Necessary scope — escalate before disclosing  
* Stop if incident occurs — report immediately before continuing work

**Escalation Path:** Supervisor → Privacy officer (for breach determination) → Compliance lead

**Documentation Requirements:**

* Incident reports document: what happened, when, who was involved, what PHI was involved, immediate actions taken  
* Privacy officer documents breach determination with risk assessment

#### **4\) Worked Examples**

**Compliant Example 1 \- PHI Identification:** Email contains: "Claim 123456 for J. Smith \- authorization approved for MRI." Content has identifier (claim number \+ name) \+ payment context (authorization). Correctly identified as PHI. Employee applies Minimum Necessary when forwarding: removes name, keeps claim number only, subject line generic ("Claim status update").

**Why Compliant:** Accurate PHI identification, Minimum Necessary applied proactively.

**Compliant Example 2 \- Incident Reporting:** Employee composes email to payer, types recipient email address, auto-complete suggests similar address, employee notices wrong recipient before sending, deletes draft. Employee reports as near-miss incident: "Almost sent PHI to wrong recipient, caught during address verification, no disclosure occurred."

**Why Compliant:** Near-miss reported even though no disclosure occurred; demonstrates incident awareness.

**Non-Compliant Example:** Employee sends PHI to wrong recipient (auto-complete error). Employee realizes mistake, recalls email (recall fails), deletes sent email from own mailbox. Employee does not report incident, reasoning "I fixed it so no harm done." Three days later, recipient reports receiving PHI not intended for them. Investigation discovers employee's failure to report and evidence deletion (deleted sent email).

**Why Non-Compliant:** Multiple violations: failure to report incident immediately, evidence destruction, self-determination that "no harm" means no reporting needed. Results in sanctions (potentially acceleration clause for evidence destruction).

#### **5\) Practice Pack**

**Drill Set (PHI Identification \- 15 Items):**

Identify which items contain PHI:

1. "Patient John Doe scheduled for surgery tomorrow" → PHI (name \+ treatment context)  
2. "Account 789 has outstanding balance" → PHI (account identifier \+ payment context)  
3. "Diabetes training seminar for staff" → Not PHI (no identifier)  
4. "MRN 456789 \- discharge summary attached" → PHI (MRN \+ treatment context)  
5. "The clinic is open Monday-Friday" → Not PHI (no identifier, no health context)  
6. "555-1234 called about medication refill" → PHI (phone number identifier \+ treatment context)  
7. "Patient in Room 5 needs assistance" → Ambiguous; in context may be PHI if identifiable (treat as PHI)  
8. Screenshot of EHR with patient name visible → PHI (identifier \+ interface implies health context)  
9. "Our hospital treats cancer patients" → Not PHI (general statement, no identifier)  
10. Email address "jsmith@email.com mentioned in claim" → PHI (email identifier \+ payment context)  
11. "Sarah, DOB 3/15/1980, requesting records" → PHI (name \+ DOB \+ health records context)  
12. "Benefits verification tool is down" → Not PHI (system status, no identifier)  
13. Sticky note: "Call Mrs. Johnson re: test results" → PHI (name \+ test results context)  
14. "Patient reported chest pain during visit" in deidentified case study → Not PHI if properly deidentified (no identifier present)  
15. Calendar entry: "Meeting with Smith family \- care planning" → PHI (family name \+ care context)

**Scenario Exercise:** **Scenario:** You are documenting a call in ticketing system. You need to reference the patient's account for continuity. The ticket template has fields for: Account Number, Name, DOB, Issue Description, Resolution, Follow-up. The issue is "patient requested payment plan options." You resolved by sending payment plan brochure link.

**Question:** Which fields must you complete, applying Minimum Necessary?

**Answer:**

* Account Number: YES (needed for record continuity)  
* Name: NO (account number is sufficient identifier)  
* DOB: NO (not needed for payment plan inquiry)  
* Issue Description: YES ("Payment plan options requested" \- minimal necessary)  
* Resolution: YES ("Payment plan brochure sent via approved portal link")  
* Follow-up: YES if applicable ("Follow-up in 14 days if no response")

**Minimum Necessary Applied:** Used account number (necessary), omitted name and DOB (unnecessary duplication of identifiers), described issue and resolution without extra PHI.

**Mini-Simulation Script:** **Trainer plays:** Supervisor asking about email content  
 **Learner plays:** Employee who needs to forward information

**Trainer:** "You need to forward claim status to the billing team. The original email has patient name, MRN, claim number, diagnosis, and payment amount. What do you include in your forward?"

**Learner expected actions:**

* State purpose: billing team needs claim status  
* Identify minimum necessary: claim number \+ payment amount (billing context)  
* State what to remove: patient name, MRN, diagnosis (unnecessary for billing team's specific task)  
* Demonstrate forwarding with only claim number and payment amount  
* Confirm recipient is billing team (need-to-know verified)

**Checklist: Core Definitions Application**

* \[ \] Can define PHI (identifier \+ health/payment context)  
* \[ \] Can define ePHI (PHI in electronic form)  
* \[ \] Can define Minimum Necessary (only what's needed for purpose)  
* \[ \] Can define Incident (any violation or risk including near-misses)  
* \[ \] Can define Breach (incident with significant risk, privacy officer determines)  
* \[ \] Can identify PHI in mixed content accurately  
* \[ \] Can apply Minimum Necessary before sharing  
* \[ \] Reports incidents including near-misses  
* \[ \] Does not self-determine breach status

**Scoring Rubric:**

* PHI identification accuracy: 3 points (15-item drill, 80% \= 12/15 correct)  
* Minimum Necessary application: 3 points  
* Incident recognition: 2 points  
* Definitions recall: 2 points  
* **Total: 10 points (8/10 \= 80% passing)**

#### **6\) Knowledge Check (15 Items)**

**Item 1 (MCQ):** PHI requires which two elements? A) Identifier \+ location  
 B) Identifier \+ health/payment context  
 C) Health context \+ date  
 D) Electronic format \+ security

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** PHI \= identifier \+ health/payment context per definition.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** C — missing identifier element.

**Item 2 (MCQ):** Which is NOT PHI? A) Patient name \+ diagnosis  
 B) Account number \+ claim status  
 C) "Diabetes education class schedule"  
 D) MRN \+ medication list

**Answer:** C  
 **Rationale:** No identifier present in general class schedule.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** D — MRN \+ medication is clearly PHI.

**Item 3 (True/False):** ePHI and paper PHI have identical handling requirements.

**Answer:** False  
 **Rationale:** ePHI requires additional technical safeguards (encryption, access logs); paper requires physical safeguards (locked storage, shredding).

**Item 4 (MCQ):** Minimum Necessary does NOT apply to: A) Documentation  
 B) Treatment activities  
 C) Communication with colleagues  
 D) Access requests

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Treatment activities exempt from Minimum Necessary; providers may access all relevant PHI for treatment.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** D — access requests DO require Minimum Necessary.

**Item 5 (MCQ):** An incident includes: A) Only events where harm occurred  
 B) Only events where PHI was disclosed  
 C) Any violation or risk event including near-misses  
 D) Only breaches

**Answer:** C  
 **Rationale:** Incidents include near-misses and any policy violation/risk event.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** A — harm is not required for incident classification.

**Item 6 (MCQ):** Who determines if an incident is a breach? A) The employee who caused it  
 B) The supervisor  
 C) The privacy officer  
 D) The compliance committee

**Answer:** C  
 **Rationale:** Privacy officer conducts risk assessment and determines breach status.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** B — supervisor receives report but does not determine breach.

**Item 7 (Scenario MCQ):** You write a note: "Pt called re: balance inquiry. Explained statement. F/U if needed." Does this contain PHI? A) No, no identifiers present  
 B) Yes, "pt" is identifier  
 C) Ambiguous, depends on system context  
 D) Only if note includes account number

**Answer:** C  
 **Rationale:** If note is filed under patient account in system, "pt" in context identifies individual \+ payment context \= PHI. Outside system context without linkage, may not be PHI.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** A — missing system context consideration.

**Item 8 (True/False):** If you catch a mistake before PHI is disclosed (near-miss), you do not need to report it as an incident.

**Answer:** False  
 **Rationale:** Near-misses are reportable incidents; demonstrates risk awareness.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** True — "no harm \= no report" misconception.

**Item 9 (MCQ):** Minimum Necessary means: A) Use the smallest font size  
 B) Disclose only what's needed for the purpose  
 C) Always use account numbers instead of names  
 D) Limit access to supervisors only

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Minimum Necessary \= only disclose/use/request what's needed for specific purpose.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** C — account numbers are not always "less" than names; depends on purpose.

**Item 10 (MCQ):** Which is ePHI? A) Paper chart in file cabinet  
 B) Verbal conversation in hallway  
 C) Email containing patient name and diagnosis  
 D) Handwritten note on clipboard

**Answer:** C  
 **Rationale:** Email is electronic format; contains identifier \+ health context \= ePHI.

**Item 11 (Scenario MCQ):** You need to route a ticket to another pod. Ticket contains name, MRN, phone, DOB, diagnosis, and issue description ("needs prior auth for MRI"). What do you include in routing message applying Minimum Necessary? A) All fields to give complete picture  
 B) Account number \+ issue description only  
 C) Name \+ diagnosis \+ issue  
 D) MRN \+ issue description only

**Answer:** D  
 **Rationale:** MRN identifies patient (necessary for routing), issue description (necessary for action). Other fields unnecessary for routing purpose.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** A — violates Minimum Necessary by including all fields.

**Item 12 (True/False):** "Unsecured PHI" means PHI not encrypted or destroyed per federal standards.

**Answer:** True  
 **Rationale:** Definition of unsecured PHI requires encryption/destruction to render unusable.

**Item 13 (MCQ):** You accidentally access a patient record without authorization (curiosity browsing). You immediately close the record and do nothing else. What is this? A) Not an incident because you closed it quickly  
 B) An incident requiring immediate reporting  
 C) A breach requiring patient notification  
 D) Acceptable if you don't tell anyone

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Unauthorized access is an incident requiring immediate reporting regardless of duration.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** A — "quick" does not excuse unauthorized access.

**Item 14 (Short Answer):** Define PHI in one sentence using both required elements.

**Answer:** PHI is information that identifies or can identify an individual AND relates to the individual's health condition, healthcare provision, or healthcare payment.

**Rationale:** Must include both identifier and health/payment context.

**Item 15 (MCQ):** Which statement about breach determination is correct? A) Employees determine breach status based on severity  
 B) Privacy officer determines breach status after risk assessment  
 C) All incidents are automatically breaches  
 D) Only incidents with patient complaints are breaches

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Privacy officer conducts formal risk assessment to determine breach status.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** C — not all incidents are breaches; requires significant risk determination.

#### **7\) QA and Audit Hooks**

**Evidence of Competence:**

* Quiz score (15 items, 80% passing \= 12/15)  
* PHI identification drill (15 items, 80% \= 12/15 correct)  
* Minimum Necessary scenario application scored

**Supervisor Review Checklist:**

* \[ \] Learner accurately identifies PHI in workplace content  
* \[ \] Learner applies Minimum Necessary before sharing  
* \[ \] Learner reports incidents appropriately (no self-determination of breach)  
* \[ \] Learner can recite all five core definitions

**Recordkeeping Tie-Back:**

* Module 0.5 completion with definitions quiz score logged  
* PHI identification drill results stored  
* Minimum Necessary application scenarios scored and stored

---

### **MODULE 0.6: ENTRY-LEVEL SCAFFOLDING AND SAFE STOP RULES (30 MIN)**

#### **1\) Entry-Level Primer**

**Plain Language Summary:** This module equips new learners with navigation skills: how to read modules, use job aids, complete assessments, and apply five universal safe stop rules that always override other instructions: (1) Stop if identity not verified, (2) Stop if channel not approved, (3) Stop if request purpose unclear, (4) Stop if rushed/pressured to bypass steps, (5) Escalate with minimal necessary context. These rules prevent the most common incident patterns.

**Observable Behaviors:**

* Navigates learning system efficiently  
* Uses job aids to support task performance  
* Completes assessments without integrity violations  
* Applies safe stop rules reflexively when triggers occur  
* Escalates appropriately without over-disclosing PHI

#### **2\) Definitions**

**Module:** Self-contained learning unit covering one topic with primer, procedures, examples, practice, and assessment.

**Job Aid:** Reference document (checklist, script, template, flowchart) used during work performance to support consistent execution without memorization. Stored in accessible location for just-in-time use.

**Assessment:** Knowledge check or practical evaluation measuring competence, with defined passing standard and attempt limits.

**Safe Stop Rule:** Mandatory halt condition requiring immediate stop of current action, assessment of situation, and escalation if needed. Safe stop rules always override conflicting instructions, including from supervisors or clients.

**Identity Verification Requirement:** Confirmation of requester identity using approved factors before disclosing PHI or granting access.

**Approved Channel:** Communication or storage method explicitly allowed by client policy for PHI handling (needs\_review for client-specific channel lists).

**Request Purpose Clarity:** Understanding and documenting why PHI is being requested, disclosed, or accessed.

**Pressure to Bypass:** Urgency or coercion to skip verification, documentation, or other controls.

**Minimal Necessary Context During Escalation:** Sharing only non-PHI or minimum PHI required to escalate the issue (e.g., "I have a caller who cannot verify identity" rather than "John Smith at 555-1234 is asking for results").

#### **3\) Step-by-Step Procedures**

**Procedure: Navigate and Complete Training Modules**

1. Log into learning management system with credentials  
2. Access assigned course from dashboard  
3. For each module:  
   * Read entry-level primer first (plain language overview)  
   * Study definitions section (terms you will use)  
   * Read step-by-step procedures carefully (these are your work instructions)  
   * Review worked examples (see correct vs incorrect application)  
   * Complete practice pack activities (drills, scenarios, simulations)  
   * Take knowledge check when ready (review passing standard and attempt limits first)  
4. After passing knowledge check: system marks module complete automatically  
5. Proceed to next module only after current module marked complete  
6. Access job aids referenced in modules (stored in shared drive or LMS resource library)  
7. Bookmark or download job aids for use during actual work performance

**Procedure: Use Job Aids Effectively**

1. Identify job aid needed for task (e.g., verification script, phishing checklist, redaction template)  
2. Access job aid from designated storage location  
3. Follow job aid step-by-step during task performance (job aids are designed for real-time use, not memorization)  
4. Check off steps if job aid has checklist format  
5. Document use of job aid if required by task (e.g., "Used verification script per job aid")  
6. If job aid is unclear or seems outdated: escalate to supervisor; do not improvise

**Procedure: Apply Safe Stop Rules**

**Safe Stop Rule 1: Stop if Identity Not Verified**

* Before disclosing PHI, granting access, or processing requests: verify requester identity  
* Use approved verification method (Module 4 will detail methods)  
* If verification fails or cannot be completed: stop, do not disclose, offer alternative (e.g., secure callback, written request)  
* Document verification attempt outcome

**Safe Stop Rule 2: Stop if Channel Not Approved**

* Before sending, storing, or discussing PHI: confirm channel is approved for client  
* Approved channel list is client-specific (needs\_review; Module 7 will detail)  
* If uncertain whether channel is approved: stop, escalate to supervisor  
* Never use personal email, SMS, WhatsApp, or social media for PHI regardless of encryption

**Safe Stop Rule 3: Stop if Request Purpose Unclear**

* Before disclosing PHI: understand and document why information is needed  
* If requester cannot or will not state clear purpose: stop, do not disclose  
* "Just checking" or "general inquiry" is not sufficient purpose  
* Document unclear purpose and escalate

**Safe Stop Rule 4: Stop if Rushed or Pressured to Bypass Steps**

* If requester or supervisor pressures you to skip verification, documentation, or other controls: stop  
* State: "I need to follow the required procedure for compliance. This will take \[X minutes\]."  
* If pressure continues: stop interaction, escalate to compliance immediately  
* Document pressure attempt (who, when, what was requested)

**Safe Stop Rule 5: Escalate with Minimal Necessary Context**

* When escalating any issue: share only what supervisor needs to provide guidance  
* Avoid using patient names, diagnoses, or other identifiers in escalation message unless essential  
* Example escalation: "I have a caller requesting test results but cannot verify identity using our script. How should I proceed?" (no patient identifiers needed)  
* If PHI must be mentioned: use secure escalation channel (in-person, secure messaging, not hallway conversation)

**Safe Stop Decision Tree:**

1. Does situation involve PHI? (Yes → continue to step 2\)  
2. Is identity verified? (No → STOP, apply Rule 1\)  
3. Is channel approved? (No → STOP, apply Rule 2\)  
4. Is purpose clear? (No → STOP, apply Rule 3\)  
5. Am I being rushed/pressured? (Yes → STOP, apply Rule 4\)  
6. If any uncertainty remains → STOP, apply Rule 5 (escalate with minimal context)

**Escalation Path:** Supervisor → Compliance lead → Privacy officer (for PHI-related safe stops)

**Documentation Requirements:**

* Safe stop trigger documented in incident report or task note  
* Escalation documented with timestamp and decision outcome  
* No PHI in escalation documentation unless secure method used

#### **4\) Worked Examples**

**Compliant Example 1 \- Safe Stop Rule 1 (Identity):** Caller requests test results. Employee begins verification script. Caller provides name but incorrect DOB. Employee tries DOB twice more (per script, three attempts allowed). All fail. Employee stops: "I'm unable to verify your identity over the phone. I can send you a secure portal message with instructions to access results online, or you can visit the clinic with photo ID." No results disclosed.

**Why Compliant:** Applied Rule 1, stopped when verification failed, offered secure alternative, documented failure.

**Compliant Example 2 \- Safe Stop Rule 4 (Pressure):** Supervisor urgently requests patient payment history "right now for a call." Supervisor says "skip the access request form, just pull it quickly." Employee stops: "I need to complete the access request form per procedure. It will take 2 minutes." Supervisor insists. Employee stops interaction: "I need to follow compliance procedure. Let me complete the form and I'll have the information to you in 5 minutes." Completes form, documents pressure attempt in note, provides information through proper channel.

**Why Compliant:** Applied Rule 4, did not bypass procedure despite pressure, documented incident (pressure to bypass controls).

**Non-Compliant Example:** Employee receives email request for patient records from external email address claiming to be "Dr. Smith from Cardiology Associates." Email looks professional. Employee is busy and email seems legitimate. Employee attaches records and sends without verifying requester identity through approved method. Email address was spoofed; PHI sent to wrong person. Breach occurs.

**Why Non-Compliant:** Failed to apply Rule 1 (verify identity) and Rule 2 (email verification process is required before external disclosure). Result: breach, sanctions, potential termination under acceleration clause if deemed reckless.

#### **5\) Practice Pack**

**Drill Set (Safe Stop Rule Matching \- 10 Scenarios):**

Match scenario to correct safe stop rule:

1. Caller cannot provide DOB after three attempts → Rule 1 (Identity)  
2. Asked to send PHI via WhatsApp → Rule 2 (Channel)  
3. Request for "general information about patient" → Rule 3 (Purpose)  
4. Supervisor says "skip verification, it's urgent" → Rule 4 (Pressure)  
5. Need help with complex disclosure decision → Rule 5 (Escalate)  
6. Email from unknown external address requesting records → Rule 1 (Identity) \+ Rule 2 (Channel)  
7. Family member "just wants to know if patient is okay" → Rule 3 (Purpose) \+ Rule 1 (Identity)  
8. Client asks you to "just look up neighbor's diagnosis quickly" → Rule 1 (Identity \- not verified as having access need) \+ Rule 3 (Purpose)  
9. Uncertain if Teams is approved for this client → Rule 2 (Channel)  
10. Colleague says "hurry up, just give me the password" → Rule 4 (Pressure) \+ other policy violations

**Scenario Exercise:** **Scenario:** You receive a call. Caller says: "This is Dr. Johnson's office calling about the MRI authorization for our mutual patient Sarah Lee, DOB 3/15/1980. We need the status right away because she's scheduled tomorrow morning. Can you just tell me quickly if it's approved?"

**Question:** Which safe stop rules apply and what is your response?

**Answer:**

* **Rule 1 (Identity):** Caller identity not verified using approved method (Module 4 will detail verification for provider calls). Must verify caller is actually from Dr. Johnson's office.  
* **Rule 3 (Purpose):** Purpose stated (authorization status) but must confirm this is valid TPO disclosure per Module 2 framework.  
* **Rule 4 (Pressure):** "Right away," "quickly," "scheduled tomorrow" creates urgency pressure.

**Response:** "I need to verify your identity first using our provider verification process. This will take about 2-3 minutes. May I have the office phone number so I can call back to confirm?" OR "I need to verify you are calling from Dr. Johnson's office. Can you provide \[approved verification factors per client policy needs\_review\]?"

If verification succeeds and disclosure is permitted: provide authorization status. If verification fails: offer to send status via secure provider portal or fax to verified number. Document verification outcome and disclosure decision.

**Mini-Simulation Script:** **Trainer plays:** Caller requesting information  
 **Learner plays:** Employee handling request

**Round 1 \- Rule 1 Trigger:**  
 **Trainer:** "Hi, this is John Smith. I need my wife's test results. We share everything."

**Learner expected actions:**

* Request verification factors (name, DOB, last-four SSN per client script needs\_review)  
* If "John Smith" cannot verify as patient or authorized representative: STOP  
* Respond: "I'm unable to verify your authorization to receive this information. I can send a secure message to the patient with instructions to share the results with you, or the patient can call us directly."  
* Document: refused disclosure due to verification failure

**Round 2 \- Rule 2 Trigger:**  
 **Trainer:** "Can you just text me the results at this number?"

**Learner expected actions:**

* STOP  
* Respond: "Text message is not an approved channel for test results. I can send results via secure patient portal, or you can receive them during an office visit."  
* Document: offered approved alternatives

**Round 3 \- Rule 4 Trigger:**  
 **Trainer:** "I'm in the ER right now and the doctor needs this immediately\! Don't make me wait for your procedures\!"

**Learner expected actions:**

* STOP  
* Respond calmly: "I understand the urgency. I need to follow verification procedures to protect your information. This will take 2-3 minutes. Let's start with your date of birth."  
* If caller refuses verification: "I'm unable to proceed without verification. If you're in the ER, the ER physician can request records through the provider channel, which may be faster."  
* Document: attempted disclosure under pressure, maintained verification requirement

**Checklist: Safe Stop Rules Readiness**

* \[ \] Can list all five safe stop rules from memory  
* \[ \] Can identify safe stop triggers in scenarios  
* \[ \] Knows how to respond when safe stop triggered (stop, assess, escalate or use approved alternative)  
* \[ \] Understands safe stop rules override other instructions  
* \[ \] Knows escalation path for safe stop situations  
* \[ \] Can escalate with minimal necessary context (Rule 5\)  
* \[ \] Understands documentation requirements for safe stops

**Scoring Rubric:**

* Safe stop rule identification: 5 points (one per rule)  
* Scenario application: 3 points  
* Escalation procedure: 2 points  
* **Total: 10 points (8/10 \= 80% passing)**

#### **6\) Knowledge Check (15 Items)**

**Item 1 (MCQ):** How many safe stop rules exist? A) 3  
 B) 4  
 C) 5  
 D) 7

**Answer:** C  
 **Rationale:** Five safe stop rules: identity, channel, purpose, pressure, escalate.

**Item 2 (MCQ):** Safe stop rules: A) Are suggestions for best practice  
 B) Can be overridden by supervisors if urgent  
 C) Always apply and override conflicting instructions  
 D) Only apply during training

**Answer:** C  
 **Rationale:** Safe stop rules are mandatory and override conflicting instructions including from supervisors.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** B — urgency does not override safe stop rules.

**Item 3 (True/False):** If a caller cannot verify identity, you can disclose PHI if they sound legitimate.

**Answer:** False  
 **Rationale:** Rule 1 requires identity verification; "sounds legitimate" is not verification.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** True — relying on judgment instead of verification procedure.

**Item 4 (MCQ):** Which is an example of Rule 2 (approved channel) violation? A) Calling patient at verified phone number  
 B) Sending PHI via WhatsApp  
 C) Using secure patient portal  
 D) Faxing to verified fax number

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** WhatsApp is banned channel regardless of encryption.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** D — fax to verified number is typically approved (needs\_review per client).

**Item 5 (MCQ):** "I just want to check on my neighbor" is an example of which safe stop trigger? A) Identity not verified  
 B) Channel not approved  
 C) Purpose unclear  
 D) Pressure to bypass

**Answer:** C  
 **Rationale:** "Just checking" is insufficient purpose; also identity/authorization issue.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** A — while also an identity issue, the primary trigger here is unclear purpose.

**Item 6 (Scenario MCQ):** Your supervisor says "I need this patient file immediately, don't bother with the access request form." What do you do? A) Follow supervisor's instruction to save time  
 B) Apply Rule 4, complete the form, document the pressure  
 C) Escalate to compliance without doing anything  
 D) Provide the file but complete the form afterward

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Rule 4 requires stopping when pressured to bypass procedures; maintain procedure and document pressure.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** A — supervisor instruction does not override safe stop rule.

**Item 7 (MCQ):** When escalating a PHI-related question to your supervisor, you should: A) Include all patient details so supervisor has full context  
 B) Use minimal necessary context, avoiding PHI when possible  
 C) Wait until end of shift to escalate  
 D) Escalate via public channel like team chat

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Rule 5 requires minimal necessary context during escalation.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** A — unnecessary PHI in escalation creates additional exposure.

**Item 8 (True/False):** Job aids are only for new employees; experienced employees should have procedures memorized.

**Answer:** False  
 **Rationale:** Job aids are designed for real-time use at all experience levels to ensure consistency.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** True — misconception that memorization replaces job aids.

**Item 9 (MCQ):** You are uncertain if Microsoft Teams is approved for sharing X-rays with this client. What do you do? A) Use Teams since Microsoft is secure  
 B) Apply Rule 2 (channel), escalate to confirm approval before using  
 C) Ask a colleague and follow their advice  
 D) Use email instead

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Rule 2 requires confirmation of channel approval when uncertain.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** A — general security does not equal client-specific approval.

**Item 10 (MCQ):** Which statement about safe stop rules is correct? A) Apply only if you remember them during the situation  
 B) Apply reflexively; they are mandatory halt conditions  
 C) Apply after completing the task if there was a problem  
 D) Apply only during training period

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Safe stop rules are reflexive mandatory conditions, not retrospective.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** C — must apply during the situation, not after.

**Item 11 (Scenario MCQ):** External email address requests patient records. Email has correct letterhead and looks professional. What is your first safe stop check? A) Verify requester identity using approved method  
 B) Check if request purpose is clear  
 C) Confirm channel is approved for external disclosure  
 D) All of the above

**Answer:** D  
 **Rationale:** All three rules apply: identity verification (Rule 1), external email channel verification (Rule 2), purpose assessment (Rule 3).  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** A only — missing that multiple rules can apply simultaneously.

**Item 12 (True/False):** If three safe stop rules are triggered simultaneously, you can address them in any order.

**Answer:** False  
 **Rationale:** Use safe stop decision tree order: identity first, then channel, then purpose; all must be satisfied.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** True — order matters for systematic risk reduction.

**Item 13 (MCQ):** A job aid is: A) A test to assess your knowledge  
 B) A reference document used during work performance  
 C) A training module  
 D) A policy document

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Job aid definition is reference for just-in-time use during tasks.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** D — job aids are procedural tools, not policy statements.

**Item 14 (Short Answer):** List the five safe stop rules (triggers).

**Answer:**

1. Stop if identity not verified  
2. Stop if channel not approved  
3. Stop if request purpose unclear  
4. Stop if rushed/pressured to bypass steps  
5. Escalate with minimal necessary context

**Rationale:** Core safe stop rules all learners must know.

**Item 15 (Scenario MCQ):** You need help determining if a disclosure is permitted. You escalate to your supervisor by email saying: "I have a caller named Sarah Lee, DOB 3/15/1980, asking about her husband's cancer diagnosis. Can I disclose?" What is wrong with this escalation? A) Nothing; supervisor needs full context  
 B) Violated Rule 5 by including unnecessary PHI in escalation  
 C) Should have called instead of emailing  
 D)

Should have escalated by phone

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Rule 5 requires minimal necessary context; escalation question could be asked without patient name, DOB, or diagnosis: "Spouse is requesting other spouse's diagnosis. What verification/authorization is needed?"  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** A — including unnecessary PHI violates Rule 5\.

#### **7\) QA and Audit Hooks**

**Evidence of Competence:**

* Quiz score (15 items, 80% passing \= 12/15)  
* Safe stop rule drill (10 scenarios, 80% \= 8/10 correct)  
* Simulation performance (three rounds, scored on rule application)

**Supervisor Review Checklist:**

* \[ \] Learner can recite all five safe stop rules  
* \[ \] Learner demonstrates reflexive application in simulations  
* \[ \] Learner knows escalation path  
* \[ \] Learner applies minimal necessary context in escalations  
* \[ \] Learner understands safe stop rules override other instructions

**Recordkeeping Tie-Back:**

* Module 0.6 completion with quiz and simulation scores logged  
* Course 0 overall completion recorded (all modules 0.1-0.6 complete)  
* Safe stop rules acknowledgment timestamp logged as required field

# **COURSE 1 MODULE BUILDS**

### **MODULE 1: PHI FUNDAMENTALS AND IDENTIFICATION (60 MIN)**

#### **1\) Entry-Level Primer**

**Plain Language Summary:** PHI (Protected Health Information) is the foundation of all healthcare compliance. PHI exists when you have BOTH an identifier (name, number, contact info, etc.) AND health or payment context. Your job requires you to read emails, tickets, notes, screenshots, and portal screens constantly — you must scan for PHI before using or sharing any content. Misidentifying PHI causes most data incidents. This module trains you to identify PHI in mixed content and apply redaction before sharing.

**Observable Behaviors:**

* Scans all work content for PHI before forwarding or sharing  
* Identifies identifiers and health/payment context separately, then confirms both present  
* Applies redaction to remove unnecessary PHI before sharing  
* Escalates with sanitized excerpt when uncertain about PHI status

#### **2\) Definitions**

**PHI (Protected Health Information):** Information that identifies or can identify an individual AND relates to health condition, healthcare provision, or healthcare payment. Both elements required.

**ePHI (Electronic PHI):** PHI in electronic form (emails, databases, scanned documents, portal screens, text messages, digital photos).

**Identifier:** Data element that identifies or can identify an individual. Includes direct identifiers (name, MRN, SSN, account number, phone, email, address, photo) and indirect identifiers (age if rare, dates tied to care, small geographic areas).

**Direct Identifier:** Immediately identifies individual (name, MRN, SSN, specific account number, contact information, photo, biometric data).

**Indirect Identifier:** May identify individual in combination with other information (age over 89, dates related to care/payment, geographic subdivision smaller than state if population \< 20,000, device IDs).

**De-identification (needs\_review):** Process of removing identifiers to create information that cannot reasonably identify an individual. Two methods exist per federal standards (Expert Determination and Safe Harbor); client-specific de-identification requirements need\_review.

**Mixed Content:** Work objects (emails, tickets, notes) containing both PHI and non-PHI information requiring selective redaction.

**Redaction:** Removal or obscuring of specific identifiers or content before sharing, printing, or storing outside primary system.

#### **3\) Step-by-Step Procedures**

**Procedure: Identify PHI in Any Work Object**

1. Identify object type receiving or reviewing (email, ticket, note, screenshot, document, portal screen, verbal conversation)  
2. Scan for identifiers using systematic approach:  
   * Names (patient, guarantor, family members if linked)  
   * Numbers (MRN, account number, claim number, insurance ID, SSN, phone number)  
   * Contact information (email, physical address, fax)  
   * Dates (DOB, admission, discharge, appointment dates, dates of service)  
   * Photos or images containing identifiable persons  
   * Account IDs or other unique identifiers  
3. Scan for health or payment context:  
   * Diagnosis, symptoms, complaints  
   * Treatment, procedures, medications  
   * Test results, clinical observations  
   * Appointment reasons or clinical service descriptions  
   * Claim status, payment information, billing details  
   * Insurance coverage or benefits information  
4. Apply two-element test:  
   * If identifier present BUT no health/payment context: may be sensitive but not PHI (e.g., patient name in general directory)  
   * If health/payment context present BUT no identifier: may be sensitive but not PHI (e.g., "patient with diabetes" in training with no identifiers)  
   * If BOTH identifier AND health/payment context present: treat as PHI  
5. When uncertain: treat as PHI and escalate with sanitized excerpt (Rule 5 from Module 0.6)  
6. Before sharing or storing outside primary system: apply minimum necessary redaction (remove unnecessary identifiers or context)

**Procedure: Apply Redaction Before Sharing**

1. Confirm purpose of sharing (why does recipient need this information?)  
2. Identify minimum necessary elements for that purpose  
3. Redact using approved method:  
   * Electronic documents: use redaction tool (permanent removal, not highlighting or strike-through)  
   * Emails: copy needed text to new email, do not forward with thread history containing extra PHI  
   * Screenshots: never take screenshots of PHI screens (Module 3 will reinforce); if existing screenshot must be shared for training, redact identifiers permanently  
   * Tickets: use structured fields to limit PHI, avoid free-text dumps  
4. Verify redaction permanence (cannot be removed or reversed)  
5. Confirm redacted version removes all unnecessary PHI  
6. Share redacted version only  
7. Document redaction in share note if required by procedure

**Safe Stop Rules:**

* Stop if unsure whether content contains PHI — treat as PHI until confirmed otherwise  
* Stop if you cannot determine minimum necessary scope — escalate before sharing  
* Stop if redaction method is unclear — escalate for approved tool/technique

**Escalation Path:** Supervisor → Compliance lead (for complex PHI determination questions)

**Documentation Requirements:**

* Redaction decisions documented in ticket or share notes ("Redacted name and DOB per minimum necessary")  
* Uncertain PHI status escalations documented with sanitized excerpt only

#### **4\) Worked Examples**

**Compliant Example 1:** Ticket note reads: "Pt \+ account 789456 called re aged balance. Coverage update provided. Requested resubmission via approved portal method. F/U scheduled."

**Analysis:**

* Identifiers: "Pt" (ambiguous but in system context identifies patient), account number 789456  
* Health/payment context: "aged balance," "coverage," "resubmission" (payment context)  
* PHI present: Yes (identifier \+ payment context)  
* Minimum necessary applied: Uses "pt" abbreviation instead of full name, provides account number (necessary for record tracking), describes action without unnecessary clinical detail

**Why Compliant:** PHI minimized while maintaining necessary documentation for continuity.

**Compliant Example 2:** Training artifact created from real ticket. All patient names, account numbers, phone numbers, dates of service, and diagnosis details removed. Template shows only: "Patient contacted regarding \[issue type\]. Action: \[generic action\]. Outcome: \[generic outcome\]."

**Analysis:**

* Original contained PHI  
* Redaction removed all identifiers  
* Health/payment context genericized to point of non-identification  
* Artifact suitable for training

**Why Compliant:** Complete removal of PHI for training use; no identifiable information remains.

**Non-Compliant Example:** Screenshot of live patient portal showing patient name "Sarah Johnson," DOB, MRN, diagnosis "leukemia," and appointment list. Screenshot sent via email with subject "Quick question about portal layout" to colleague for help troubleshooting navigation issue.

**Analysis:**

* Multiple identifiers present: name, DOB, MRN  
* Health context present: diagnosis, appointments  
* PHI clearly present  
* Screenshot unnecessary for navigation question  
* Email subject contains no PHI but body/attachment contains significant PHI  
* Purpose (navigation help) does not require patient identifiers

**Why Non-Compliant:** Screenshots of PHI screens prohibited (Module 3 will reinforce). Purpose did not require identifiable patient data; could have used training environment or described navigation issue without screenshot. Creates incident requiring immediate reporting and escalation per Module 10\. Sanctions likely (potentially acceleration clause depending on severity and repeat patterns).

#### **5\) Practice Pack**

**Drill Set: PHI Identification (15 Artifacts, Timed 10 Minutes)**

Identify whether each contains PHI (Yes/No) and specify elements:

1. Email: "Please call Mrs. Anderson at 555-1234 to schedule her post-op follow-up."

   * **Answer:** Yes. Identifier: name \+ phone. Health context: post-op follow-up.  
2. Note: "System downtime scheduled for Saturday 2-4 AM."

   * **Answer:** No. No identifiers, no health/payment context.  
3. Ticket: "Account 12345 \- benefits verification complete, prior auth approved."

   * **Answer:** Yes. Identifier: account number. Payment context: benefits, prior auth.  
4. Screenshot showing clinic lobby with patient visible in waiting area.

   * **Answer:** Yes. Identifier: photo of individual. Health context: clinic setting (receiving healthcare).  
5. Email subject: "Claim status update."

   * **Answer:** No (subject line alone). No identifier present in subject. (Body may contain PHI.)  
6. Calendar entry: "Meeting with Johnson family \- discharge planning."

   * **Answer:** Yes. Identifier: family name. Health context: discharge planning.  
7. Training slide: "ICD-10 code J44.0 represents COPD with acute lower respiratory infection."

   * **Answer:** No. Code and condition definition with no patient identifier.  
8. Voicemail: "Hi, this is Dr. Smith's office calling for John Doe about your lab results. Call us back at 555-7890."

   * **Answer:** Yes. Identifiers: patient name implied by "John Doe" \+ caller ID context \+ callback number. Health context: lab results.  
9. Database export with columns: Account\_ID, Service\_Date, Service\_Code, Amount\_Billed (no names).

   * **Answer:** Yes. Identifier: Account\_ID (links to patient). Payment context: billing information.  
10. Sticky note: "Call scheduler re: afternoon slots."

    * **Answer:** No. No patient identifier, no specific health/payment context.  
11. Email thread with patient name in history section three emails down, current email has no identifiers.

    * **Answer:** Yes (thread contains PHI). Must review entire thread before forwarding.  
12. Portal screen showing "Patient Dashboard" title but all patient fields blank (test environment).

    * **Answer:** No. Test environment with no actual patient data.  
13. "Our clinic treats pediatric asthma cases."

    * **Answer:** No. General service description, no patient identifiers.  
14. "Sarah Lee, DOB 3/15/80, needs appointment rescheduled."

    * **Answer:** Yes. Identifiers: name \+ DOB. Health context: appointment (healthcare provision).  
15. Faxed document with patient name and diagnosis on page 1, page 2 is blank template.

    * **Answer:** Yes (document contains PHI on page 1). Cannot share page 2 alone if it was part of PHI-containing fax.

**Scoring:** 80% required \= 12/15 correct

**Scenario Exercise:** **Scenario:** You receive email from clinic staff: "Can you help me understand why this claim denied? \[Screenshot attached showing patient name, MRN, claim number, denial code, denial reason 'diagnosis not specific enough'\]" You know how to resolve the issue (needs more specific diagnosis from provider). How do you respond applying PHI identification and minimum necessary?

**Answer:**

1. Identify PHI in email: Screenshot contains identifiers (name, MRN, claim number) \+ payment context (claim, denial) \= PHI present  
2. Assess minimum necessary for response: Clinic staff needs to know resolution steps; does NOT need you to reference patient-specific details in your response  
3. Respond: "The denial reason 'diagnosis not specific enough' requires provider documentation update. The provider should review the record and submit a more specific diagnosis code. I can help you with the resubmission process after the documentation is updated. Please do not send screenshots with patient information via email; you can reference the claim number only or call me to discuss."  
4. Document: Do not forward screenshot further; if you need to escalate, reference claim number only

**Why Compliant:** Provided resolution guidance without repeating patient identifiers, educated sender on screenshot prohibition, applied minimum necessary in response.

**Mini-Simulation Script:** **Trainer plays:** Colleague asking for help  
 **Learner plays:** Employee applying PHI identification

**Trainer:** "Hey, can you look at this ticket? I'm not sure what to do next. \[Shows screen with patient name, DOB, account number, and issue description visible\]"

**Learner expected actions:**

* Observe screen contains PHI (name, DOB, account number visible)  
* Assess own need-to-know: "Do I have access rights to this patient's account?"  
* If yes (authorized to help): Review ticket details as shown, provide guidance  
* If no (not authorized): "I cannot view patient details I'm not authorized for. Can you describe the issue without showing me the patient-specific screen? Or we can escalate to your supervisor."  
* Remind colleague: "In future, please describe the issue type without showing patient identifiers when asking for general guidance."

**Checklist: PHI Identification and Redaction**

* \[ \] Scanned object for identifiers (names, numbers, contacts, dates, images)  
* \[ \] Scanned object for health/payment context (diagnosis, treatment, claims, benefits)  
* \[ \] Applied two-element test (both identifier AND context \= PHI)  
* \[ \] If PHI present: determined minimum necessary for purpose  
* \[ \] If sharing: redacted unnecessary PHI permanently  
* \[ \] If uncertain: treated as PHI and escalated with sanitized excerpt  
* \[ \] Documented redaction decision or escalation

**Scoring Rubric:**

* PHI identification accuracy (15-item drill): 5 points (80% \= 12/15)  
* Redaction procedure: 2 points  
* Scenario application: 2 points  
* Checklist completion: 1 point  
* **Total: 10 points (8/10 \= 80% passing)**

#### **6\) Knowledge Check (20 Items)**

**Item 1 (MCQ):** PHI requires: A) Identifier only  
 B) Health context only  
 C) Both identifier AND health/payment context  
 D) Electronic format

**Answer:** C  
 **Rationale:** PHI \= identifier \+ health/payment context per definition.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** A — identifier alone is not sufficient.

**Item 2 (MCQ):** Which is NOT PHI? A) Patient name \+ diagnosis  
 B) MRN \+ medication list  
 C) "Diabetes education class schedule" (no patient names)  
 D) Account number \+ claim status

**Answer:** C  
 **Rationale:** No identifier present in general class schedule.

**Item 3 (True/False):** An email thread containing PHI in older messages is not PHI if your current reply has no PHI.

**Answer:** False  
 **Rationale:** Entire thread must be assessed; historical PHI makes thread PHI-containing.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** True — forgetting to review full thread history.

**Item 4 (MCQ):** Before sharing a ticket excerpt with a colleague, you should: A) Forward the entire ticket for complete context  
 B) Redact unnecessary PHI and share minimum necessary  
 C) Ask colleague to look over your shoulder instead  
 D) Print and hand-deliver to avoid electronic trail

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Apply minimum necessary through redaction before sharing.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** A — full ticket likely contains more PHI than necessary.

**Item 5 (Scenario MCQ):** A screenshot shows portal navigation buttons but no patient data visible. Is this PHI? A) Yes, portal screenshots are always PHI  
 B) No, no patient identifiers or health context visible  
 C) Yes, portal implies healthcare context  
 D) Depends on who views it

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** PHI requires identifier \+ context; blank navigation screen has neither.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** A — not all portal screenshots contain PHI; depends on content.

**Item 6 (MCQ):** "Pt \+ acct 789 called re balance" contains: A) No PHI  
 B) Identifier only  
 C) Health context only  
 D) PHI (identifier \+ payment context)

**Answer:** D  
 **Rationale:** "Pt" \+ account number (identifiers) \+ balance (payment context) \= PHI.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** B — missing that "balance" is payment context.

**Item 7 (True/False):** If you are unsure whether content contains PHI, you should treat it as non-PHI to avoid over-restricting workflow.

**Answer:** False  
 **Rationale:** Safe stop rule: if uncertain, treat as PHI and escalate.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** True — underestimating risk of misidentification.

**Item 8 (MCQ):** Redaction means: A) Highlighting PHI in yellow  
 B) Using strike-through text  
 C) Permanent removal or obscuring that cannot be reversed  
 D) Saving file in protected folder

**Answer:** C  
 **Rationale:** Redaction must be permanent and irreversible.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** B — strike-through can often be removed.

**Item 9 (Scenario MCQ):** You need to show a trainer how to complete a specific form field. The form has patient data populated. What do you do? A) Show the live form as-is  
 B) Use a test environment or blank template  
 C) Verbally describe without showing screen  
 D) Show quickly so it's not a disclosure

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Training should use test environments or blank templates, not live PHI.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** D — duration does not exempt from PHI handling rules.

**Item 10 (MCQ):** DOB alone without any other identifier is: A) Always PHI  
 B) Never PHI  
 C) PHI if combined with health/payment context and can identify individual  
 D) Only PHI for children

**Answer:** C  
 **Rationale:** DOB becomes PHI when combined with health context and can identify individual (especially if rare DOB in dataset).  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** B — DOB can be PHI in combination.

**Item 11 (MCQ):** Which scenario requires immediate PHI incident reporting? A) You identify PHI in a ticket and redact before sharing  
 B) You accidentally view PHI you don't need, immediately close, report  
 C) You apply minimum necessary successfully  
 D) You ask supervisor if content contains PHI

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Unnecessary access (even if immediately corrected) is reportable incident.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** A — proper redaction before sharing is compliant, not an incident.

**Item 12 (True/False):** "Patient with hypertension" in a training scenario with no names or numbers is PHI.

**Answer:** False  
 **Rationale:** No identifier present; health context alone is not PHI.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** True — confusing sensitive content with PHI.

**Item 13 (MCQ):** Direct identifiers include: A) Age and gender  
 B) Name and MRN  
 C) Diagnosis and treatment  
 D) State and city

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Direct identifiers immediately identify individuals (name, MRN, SSN, etc.).  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** A — age and gender are attributes but not direct identifiers.

**Item 14 (Scenario MCQ):** Colleague asks "Can you check if John Smith's claim processed?" How do you respond applying minimum necessary? A) "Yes, I'll check John Smith's claim."  
 B) "What is the account or claim number? I'll check by that."  
 C) "I cannot help with patient-specific questions."  
 D) "Let me look up John Smith in the system."

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Use account/claim number (necessary) instead of name when possible (minimum necessary).  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** A — repeating name unnecessarily in your response.

**Item 15 (MCQ):** ePHI includes: A) Only encrypted data  
 B) Only data in electronic health records  
 C) Any PHI created, stored, transmitted, or received electronically  
 D) Only data on secure servers

**Answer:** C  
 **Rationale:** ePHI is any PHI in electronic form regardless of security status or location.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** B — not limited to EHRs.

**Item 16 (True/False):** Indirect identifiers can only identify individuals when combined with other information.

**Answer:** True  
 **Rationale:** Indirect identifiers (age over 89, small geographic areas, rare dates) identify in combination.

**Item 17 (MCQ):** You create training materials from real tickets. What must you do? A) Use tickets as-is for realism  
 B) Remove all identifiers and genericize health/payment context  
 C) Only remove patient names  
 D) Encrypt the files

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Training artifacts must be fully de-identified (all identifiers removed, context genericized).  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** C — removing only names leaves other identifiers (account numbers, dates, etc.).

**Item 18 (Scenario MCQ):** You receive fax with patient name on page 1 and blank form on page 2\. You need to share the blank form with a colleague as a template. What do you do? A) Share page 2 only  
 B) Share entire fax since page 2 is blank  
 C) Recreate blank form from scratch or use approved template library  
 D) Redact name on page 1 and share both pages

**Answer:** C  
 **Rationale:** Even blank page from PHI-containing document may carry contamination risk; use approved templates or recreate.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** A — separating pages may not fully remove association with PHI document.

**Item 19 (Short Answer):** List three examples of direct identifiers.

**Answer:** (Any three of: name, MRN, SSN, account number, phone number, email address, physical address, photo, biometric data, IP address, device ID)

**Rationale:** Direct identifiers immediately identify individuals.

**Item 20 (Scenario MCQ):** Ticket note says "Contact provided re aged balance. Action: sent statement." Contains account number in system but not in note text. Is the note PHI? A) No, note text has no identifiers  
 B) Yes, account number in system associates note with patient  
 C) Only if you copy the note outside the system  
 D) Only if amount is visible

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Note in patient account context creates identifier association even if note text doesn't repeat identifier.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** A — context within system creates PHI association.

**Evidence of Competence:**

* Redacted artifact set submitted (5 examples of before/after redaction)  
* PHI identification drill score (15 items, 12/15 \= 80%)  
* Knowledge check score (20 items, 16/20 \= 80%)  
* Scenario application scored by rubric

**Supervisor Review Checklist:**

* \[ \] Learner redactions are permanent and complete  
* \[ \] Learner identifies PHI accurately in workplace content  
* \[ \] Learner applies minimum necessary reflexively  
* \[ \] Learner escalates uncertain cases appropriately with sanitized excerpts

* Module 1 completion with all artifact submissions logged  
* Drill scores and quiz scores stored  
* Module 1 score recorded as required training record field (assessment scores)
