 ✅ Critical modules fully built (Course 0 complete, Course 1 Modules 1-8 complete, Course 2 Module 3 and 7 complete, Course 3 Module 5 complete)  
 ✅ Remaining modules ready for framework application using demonstrated structure  
 ✅ All source requirements preserved with neutral scaffolding added  
 ✅ Audit-ready recordkeeping and QA hooks throughout

# **ADDITIONAL COMPLETE MODULE BUILDS (CONTINUED)**

## **COURSE 4: MEDICAL SCRIBE TRAINING (REMOTE, CLINICAL DOCUMENTATION QUALITY)**

### **MODULE 2: SOAP NOTE STRUCTURE FUNDAMENTALS (90 MIN)**

#### **1\) Entry-Level Primer**

**Plain Language Summary:** SOAP (Subjective, Objective, Assessment, Plan) is the universal clinical documentation structure. Your role as scribe is documenting provider's observations and decisions in correct SOAP sections — NOT interpreting, inferring, or adding information the provider didn't state. This module trains each section's purpose and content boundaries: Subjective (patient-reported symptoms/history), Objective (measurable findings/exam results), Assessment (provider's clinical conclusions), Plan (treatment decisions). Documentation-only scope means you transcribe what provider says; you never fill gaps with assumptions or medical knowledge.

**Observable Behaviors:**

* Places documentation in correct SOAP section based on information type  
* Distinguishes patient-reported information (Subjective) from provider observations (Objective)  
* Records provider's assessment and plan exactly as stated, no interpretation  
* Escalates when provider's dictation is unclear or ambiguous  
* Never adds information provider didn't explicitly state  
* Uses consistent SOAP structure across all encounter types

#### **2\) Definitions**

**SOAP Structure:** Standardized clinical note format with four sections: Subjective (patient's report), Objective (provider's findings), Assessment (provider's clinical judgment), Plan (treatment decisions). Used across specialties for consistency.

**Subjective Section:** Patient-reported information including chief complaint, history of present illness, symptoms, symptom characteristics (onset, duration, severity, location, quality, alleviating/aggravating factors), review of systems (patient's yes/no responses), past medical/surgical/family/social history, medications, allergies. First-person patient perspective.

**Objective Section:** Provider's observations and measurable findings including vital signs, physical examination findings, test results (labs, imaging, diagnostics), observed patient behavior/appearance, wound measurements, functional assessments. Third-person provider observations.

**Assessment Section:** Provider's clinical reasoning, differential diagnoses, diagnosis conclusions, evaluation of patient's condition/progress. Provider's professional judgment based on subjective and objective data. Examples: "Patient presents with acute bronchitis," "Type 2 diabetes well-controlled," "Hypertension poorly controlled, medication adjustment needed."

**Plan Section:** Provider's treatment decisions and next steps including new/continued/discontinued medications with dosing, procedures performed or ordered, diagnostic tests ordered, referrals, patient education provided, follow-up instructions, return precautions. Actionable items.

**Chief Complaint (CC):** Brief statement of why patient is seeking care, typically in patient's own words. Example: "cough and fever for 3 days." Placed at beginning of Subjective or as separate header.

**History of Present Illness (HPI):** Detailed narrative of current problem including symptom timeline, characteristics, previous treatments attempted, impact on daily activities. Core of Subjective section.

**Review of Systems (ROS):** Systematic review of body systems where patient reports presence or absence of symptoms. Can be in Subjective (patient-reported) or documented as separate section. Example: "Cardiovascular: denies chest pain, palpitations. Respiratory: positive for cough, denies shortness of breath."

**Physical Examination:** Provider's systematic assessment of body systems through inspection, palpation, percussion, auscultation. Core of Objective section. Example: "Lungs: bilateral crackles at bases, no wheezes. Heart: regular rate and rhythm, no murmurs."

**Documentation-Only Scope:** Scribe role limitation: transcribe provider's stated observations and decisions exactly; do NOT interpret clinical meaning, infer unstated information, or apply medical knowledge to fill gaps.

**Hallucinated Facts:** Information added to documentation that provider did not explicitly state. Serious violation. Example: Provider says "lungs clear," scribe writes "no wheezes, rhonchi, or rales" (adding detail provider didn't state). Even if medically accurate, scribes document ONLY what provider states.

#### **3\) Step-by-Step Procedures**

**Procedure: Document Chief Complaint and Subjective Section**

1. **Capture Chief Complaint (CC):**

   * Listen for patient's initial statement of problem  
   * Document in patient's words when possible: "Patient reports: 'cough and fever'"  
   * Keep brief (typically 1-3 words to one sentence)  
   * Place at note beginning or Subjective section header  
2. **Document History of Present Illness (HPI):**

   * Record patient's description of current problem in chronological order  
   * Include symptom characteristics (use patient's descriptive words):  
     * Onset: when symptoms started ("3 days ago," "gradually over past week")  
     * Location: where symptom occurs ("right knee," "left chest")  
     * Duration: how long symptoms last ("constant," "intermittent lasting 2-3 hours")  
     * Character/Quality: what symptom feels like (patient's words: "sharp," "dull ache," "burning")  
     * Severity: intensity (patient's rating: "7 out of 10," "mild," "severe")  
     * Aggravating factors: what makes worse ("walking upstairs," "eating")  
     * Alleviating factors: what makes better ("rest," "ibuprofen")  
     * Associated symptoms: related symptoms ("cough with fever," "nausea with headache")  
   * Include treatments tried: "Patient tried over-the-counter ibuprofen with minimal relief"  
   * Record impact on function: "Unable to attend work for past 2 days"  
3. **Document Review of Systems (ROS):**

   * Record patient's positive and negative responses to system review  
   * Use consistent format per provider preference:  
     * By system: "Cardiovascular: denies chest pain. Respiratory: positive for cough."  
     * OR comprehensive paragraph: "Patient denies chest pain, shortness of breath, abdominal pain. Positive for cough, fever, fatigue."  
   * Mark pertinent negatives (symptoms patient does NOT have that are clinically relevant)  
   * Only document systems provider specifically asks about (don't assume unmentioned systems were reviewed)  
4. **Document Past Medical/Surgical/Family/Social History (if addressed in encounter):**

   * Past Medical History (PMH): chronic conditions patient reports having  
   * Past Surgical History (PSH): previous surgeries with approximate dates  
   * Family History (FH): relevant conditions in immediate family members  
   * Social History (SH): occupation, smoking/alcohol/drug use, living situation (document exactly what patient reports, use neutral language)  
   * Medications: current medications patient reports taking (name, dose, frequency)  
   * Allergies: medication allergies and reactions patient reports  
5. **Safe stops for Subjective section:**

   * If patient statement is unclear: ask provider to clarify or note "patient reports \[unclear statement\]"  
   * If you cannot understand patient's description: ask provider to restate or interpret  
   * Never assume symptom characteristics provider didn't explicitly confirm with patient  
   * Never add "likely" or "probably" descriptions (clinical interpretation exceeds scope)

**Procedure: Document Objective Section**

1. **Document Vital Signs:**

   * Record all vitals taken: BP (blood pressure), HR (heart rate), RR (respiratory rate), Temp (temperature), O2 sat (oxygen saturation), Wt (weight), Ht (height), BMI if calculated  
   * Include method/location if provider specifies: "BP 130/80 left arm, sitting"  
   * Use exact numbers provider states; do not round or estimate  
2. **Document Physical Examination:**

   * Record examination in systematic order per provider's exam sequence  
   * Use provider's exact descriptive words for findings:  
     * Provider says: "lungs clear bilaterally" → Document: "Lungs clear bilaterally"  
     * Provider says: "2/6 systolic murmur at apex" → Document exactly that  
   * Include negative findings provider explicitly states: "No rashes noted," "Abdomen soft, non-tender"  
   * Do NOT expand provider's statements with additional medical terminology  
   * Do NOT add examination elements provider didn't perform or mention  
   * Common exam documentation format by system:  
     * General appearance: "Alert, no acute distress" or "Ill-appearing"  
     * HEENT (Head, Eyes, Ears, Nose, Throat): exam findings  
     * Cardiovascular: heart exam findings  
     * Respiratory: lung exam findings  
     * Abdomen: abdominal exam findings  
     * Extremities: findings in arms/legs  
     * Neurological: mental status, motor, sensory findings  
     * Skin: any skin lesions, wounds, rashes observed  
3. **Document Test Results and Measurements:**

   * Record any diagnostic results reviewed during encounter:  
     * Lab values: "Glucose 145, A1C 7.2%"  
     * Imaging results: "Chest X-ray: no acute infiltrates per radiology report"  
     * Point-of-care testing: "Rapid strep: negative"  
   * Record objective measurements: "Wound measures 3 cm x 2 cm"  
   * Include reference ranges if provider mentions: "WBC 12,000 (elevated)"  
4. **Safe stops for Objective section:**

   * If provider's exam finding description is unclear: ask provider to repeat or clarify  
   * If you're uncertain which body system an exam finding belongs to: ask provider  
   * Never infer exam findings from Assessment section (if provider assesses "clear lungs" but didn't state lung exam findings, do NOT add "lungs clear" to Objective)  
   * Never document exam elements provider didn't perform (don't write "normal" for systems not examined)

**Procedure: Document Assessment Section**

1. **Listen for provider's clinical conclusions:**

   * Diagnoses stated by provider (primary and secondary diagnoses)  
   * Provider's evaluation of patient's condition or progress  
   * Differential diagnoses provider is considering  
   * Clinical reasoning provider verbalizes  
2. **Document provider's assessment statements exactly:**

   * Use provider's diagnostic language: "Acute bronchitis," "Type 2 diabetes mellitus, well-controlled"  
   * Include any qualifying statements: "likely viral upper respiratory infection," "rule out pneumonia"  
   * Number multiple diagnoses if provider does: "1. Hypertension, poorly controlled. 2\. Obesity."  
   * Record assessment of existing conditions: "Diabetes management improving with current regimen"  
3. **Do NOT:**

   * Infer diagnoses from symptoms or exam findings (if provider examined diabetic foot ulcer but didn't state "diabetic foot ulcer" as diagnosis, don't add it)  
   * Add ICD-10 codes (coding is separate role; you document diagnosis in words)  
   * Reword provider's assessment using medical terminology you know (document provider's exact language level)  
   * Add clinical reasoning provider didn't verbalize  
4. **Safe stops for Assessment:**

   * If provider's diagnosis statement is ambiguous or incomplete: ask provider to clarify or complete  
   * If provider uses unfamiliar diagnosis term: ask provider to spell or clarify (use 200-term job aid for common terms)  
   * If provider hasn't stated diagnosis but has stated plan: note to provider "Diagnosis for documentation?"

**Procedure: Document Plan Section**

1. **Document treatment decisions in organized categories:**

    **Medications:**

   * New prescriptions: "Start amoxicillin 500mg three times daily for 10 days"  
   * Medication changes: "Increase lisinopril from 10mg to 20mg daily"  
   * Continued medications: "Continue metformin 1000mg twice daily"  
   * Discontinued medications: "Discontinue hydrochlorothiazide"  
   * Include route if specified: "oral," "topical," "inhaled"  
2. **Procedures/Treatments:**

   * Procedures performed in office: "Wound cleaned and dressed with Xeroform and gauze"  
   * Treatments ordered: "Physical therapy 3x/week for 4 weeks"  
3. **Diagnostic Testing:**

   * Labs ordered: "Order CBC, CMP, lipid panel \- fasting"  
   * Imaging ordered: "Order chest X-ray, 2 views"  
   * Timing if specified: "Labs to be drawn in 3 months"  
4. **Referrals:**

   * Specialty referrals: "Refer to cardiology for stress test evaluation"  
   * Include urgency if stated: "urgent cardiology referral"  
5. **Patient Education:**

   * Instructions given to patient: "Discussed importance of smoking cessation"  
   * Self-care instructions: "Apply ice 20 minutes 3x/day"  
   * Diet/activity modifications: "Low-sodium diet recommended"  
6. **Follow-up:**

   * Return visit timing: "Follow up in 2 weeks"  
   * Precautions: "Return sooner if fever worsens or shortness of breath develops"  
   * Results notification: "Will call patient with lab results in 3-5 days"  
7. **Use clear, actionable language:**

   * Each plan item should be specific action: "Order X," "Start Y," "Refer to Z"  
   * Include timeframes when provider specifies  
   * Include quantities/durations for prescriptions  
8. **Safe stops for Plan:**

   * If medication dosing incomplete: prompt provider "Dose and frequency for \[medication\]?"  
   * If follow-up timing unclear: ask provider to specify  
   * If unclear whether medication is new, changed, or continued: clarify with provider  
   * Never assume plan elements provider didn't state (don't add "follow up PRN" if provider didn't mention follow-up)

**Safe Stop Rules (Universal for SOAP):**

* Stop if provider's dictation is unclear, ambiguous, or incomplete — request clarification  
* Stop if you're unsure which SOAP section information belongs in — ask provider  
* Stop if you're tempted to add information provider didn't state — escalate, document only what's stated  
* Stop if provider uses terminology you don't understand — ask for spelling/clarification using 200-term job aid

**Escalation Path:** Provider (for immediate clarification during encounter) → Supervising scribe coordinator (for documentation structure questions) → Compliance (for scope boundary questions)

**Documentation Requirements:**

* Every clinical encounter documented in complete SOAP format  
* All four sections present (even if brief)  
* Timestamps for note creation and any amendments  
* Electronic signature or attestation by provider after scribe completes note

#### **4\) Worked Examples**

**Compliant Example 1 \- Complete SOAP Note (Simplified):**

**CHIEF COMPLAINT:** Cough and fever

**SUBJECTIVE:** Patient is a 45-year-old female presenting with cough and fever for 3 days. Cough is productive with yellow sputum. Fever up to 101°F. Associated symptoms include fatigue and mild shortness of breath with exertion. Denies chest pain. Tried over-the-counter cough syrup with minimal relief. No recent sick contacts known. Symptoms interfering with work.

Review of Systems: Respiratory: positive for cough, fever, shortness of breath with exertion. Negative for chest pain, wheezing. Cardiovascular: denies chest pain, palpitations.

**OBJECTIVE:** Vitals: BP 128/76, HR 88, RR 18, Temp 100.8°F, O2 sat 97% on room air

General: Alert, no acute distress  
 HEENT: Oropharynx clear, no erythema  
 Lungs: Scattered rhonchi bilaterally, no wheezes, good air movement  
 Heart: Regular rate and rhythm, no murmurs  
 Extremities: No edema

**ASSESSMENT:** Acute bronchitis

**PLAN:**

1. Supportive care with rest and hydration  
2. Start benzonatate 100mg three times daily as needed for cough  
3. Continue over-the-counter acetaminophen for fever  
4. Patient educated on expected course and return precautions  
5. Return in 7-10 days if not improving or sooner if develops worsening shortness of breath, chest pain, or high fever

**Why Compliant:** Complete SOAP structure, information placed in correct sections (patient reports in Subjective, provider's exam in Objective, provider's diagnosis in Assessment, provider's treatment decisions in Plan), no hallucinated facts, all information directly from provider's statements during encounter.

**Compliant Example 2 \- Distinguishing Subjective vs Objective:**

**Provider dictates:** "Patient says his right knee is swollen and painful. On exam, right knee shows moderate effusion and tenderness to palpation."

**Scribe documents:**

**SUBJECTIVE (partial):** Right knee swelling and pain per patient report.

**OBJECTIVE (partial):** Right knee: moderate effusion noted, tender to palpation.

**Why Compliant:** Patient's report ("says swollen and painful") documented in Subjective. Provider's examination findings ("shows effusion," "tender to palpation") documented in Objective. Clear separation between patient-reported and provider-observed.

**Non-Compliant Example \- Hallucinated Facts:**

**Provider dictates:** "Lungs are clear."

**Scribe documents:** "Lungs: Clear to auscultation bilaterally with no wheezes, rhonchi, or rales. Good air movement throughout all lung fields."

**Why Non-Compliant:** Provider said only "lungs are clear." Scribe added:

* "to auscultation bilaterally" (provider didn't specify method)  
* "no wheezes, rhonchi, or rales" (provider didn't list these negative findings)  
* "Good air movement throughout all lung fields" (provider didn't state this)

Even though these additions are medically consistent with "clear lungs," they are hallucinated facts — information scribe added that provider didn't state. Violates documentation-only scope.

**Correct documentation:** "Lungs: Clear." (Exactly what provider stated, nothing more)

**Result if hallucinated facts discovered:** Coaching on documentation-only scope, note correction required, potential note audit to check for pattern, refresher training if pattern continues. Hallucinated facts can create false clinical record and liability risk.

**Non-Compliant Example 2 \- Wrong SOAP Section:**

**Provider dictates:** "Patient has a history of hypertension and diabetes."

**Scribe documents in Objective section:** "Patient has history of hypertension and diabetes."

**Why Non-Compliant:** Historical information (past medical history) belongs in Subjective section (patient's history), not Objective section (provider's current observations). Misplacement makes note harder to read and violates SOAP structure convention.

**Correct placement:** Document in Subjective section: "Past Medical History: Hypertension, diabetes mellitus."

#### **5\) Practice Pack**

**Drill Set: SOAP Section Placement (20 Items)**

For each statement, identify correct SOAP section: S (Subjective), O (Objective), A (Assessment), P (Plan)

1. "Patient reports headache for 2 days" → S (patient-reported symptom)  
2. "Blood pressure 140/90" → O (objective measurement)  
3. "Hypertension, poorly controlled" → A (diagnosis/clinical conclusion)  
4. "Increase lisinopril to 20mg daily" → P (treatment decision)  
5. "Patient denies chest pain" → S (patient-reported negative)  
6. "Heart: Regular rate and rhythm" → O (physical exam finding)  
7. "Type 2 diabetes, well-controlled" → A (diagnosis assessment)  
8. "Order A1C and lipid panel" → P (diagnostic test order)  
9. "Cough productive with yellow sputum per patient" → S (patient description)  
10. "Lungs: bilateral crackles at bases" → O (exam finding)  
11. "Likely viral upper respiratory infection" → A (diagnosis or differential)  
12. "Patient educated on smoking cessation" → P (patient education provided)  
13. "Patient tried ibuprofen with minimal relief" → S (patient's history of treatment attempts)  
14. "Temperature 101.2°F" → O (vital sign)  
15. "Acute bronchitis" → A (diagnosis)  
16. "Follow up in 2 weeks" → P (follow-up instruction)  
17. "Patient rates pain 7 out of 10" → S (patient-reported severity)  
18. "Abdomen soft, non-tender" → O (exam finding)  
19. "Diabetes management improving with current regimen" → A (assessment of condition)  
20. "Continue metformin 1000mg twice daily" → P (medication continuation)

**Scoring:** 80% \= 16/20 correct

**Scenario Exercise: Identify Hallucinated Facts**

**Provider states:** "Patient has diabetes and hypertension. Blood pressure today is 150/95. I'll increase his blood pressure medication."

**Scribe drafts (identify problems):**

"**SUBJECTIVE:** Patient presents for diabetes and hypertension management. Reports compliance with medications and checking blood sugar regularly at home with good control.

**OBJECTIVE:** BP 150/95, elevated compared to goal of less than 130/80. Patient appears well-nourished and in no distress.

**ASSESSMENT:** Type 2 diabetes mellitus, well-controlled. Hypertension, poorly controlled.

**PLAN:** Increase lisinopril from 10mg to 20mg daily. Patient educated on importance of blood pressure control to prevent complications. Follow up in 1 month to recheck blood pressure."

**Identify hallucinated facts (information provider didn't state):**

**Answer \- Hallucinated Facts:**

1. "Reports compliance with medications" — provider didn't state this  
2. "checking blood sugar regularly at home with good control" — provider didn't state this  
3. "compared to goal of less than 130/80" — provider didn't state goal  
4. "appears well-nourished" — provider didn't state this  
5. "in no distress" — provider didn't state this  
6. "Type 2 diabetes mellitus, well-controlled" — provider only said "diabetes," didn't specify type or control status  
7. "poorly controlled" for hypertension — provider didn't state this assessment  
8. "from 10mg to 20mg" — provider said "increase blood pressure medication" but didn't specify medication name or new dose  
9. "educated on importance of blood pressure control to prevent complications" — provider didn't state what education was provided  
10. "Follow up in 1 month to recheck blood pressure" — provider didn't state follow-up timing or purpose

**Correct documentation based ONLY on provider's statements:**

"**SUBJECTIVE:** Patient presents for diabetes and hypertension management.

**OBJECTIVE:** BP 150/95

**ASSESSMENT:** Diabetes. Hypertension.

**PLAN:** Increase blood pressure medication."

**Note:** This correct version is incomplete for clinical purposes. Scribe should prompt provider: "Dose for blood pressure medication? Type of diabetes? Assessment of diabetes control? Follow-up timing?" Provider then provides additional information to complete note. Scribe's role is prompting for completeness, NOT filling gaps with assumptions.

**Mini-Simulation Script:** **Trainer plays:** Provider dictating encounter  
 **Learner plays:** Scribe documenting in real-time

**Provider dictates:** "Patient is a 60-year-old male with chest pain for one hour. Pain is substernal, pressure-like, radiating to left arm. On exam, patient is diaphoretic and appears anxious. Vital signs: BP 160/100, heart rate 110, respiratory rate 20\. Heart exam shows regular rhythm, no murmurs. Lungs clear. I'm concerned about acute coronary syndrome. EKG shows ST elevation in leads II, III, and aVF. I'm calling for ambulance transfer to emergency department for STEMI protocol."

**Learner expected actions:**

* Document chief complaint: "Chest pain"  
* **SUBJECTIVE:** "Chest pain for one hour. Pain substernal, pressure-like, radiating to left arm."  
* **OBJECTIVE:** "Patient diaphoretic, appears anxious. Vitals: BP 160/100, HR 110, RR 20\. Heart: Regular rhythm, no murmurs. Lungs: Clear. EKG: ST elevation in leads II, III, aVF."  
* **ASSESSMENT:** "Acute coronary syndrome. STEMI (ST elevation myocardial infarction)."  
* **PLAN:** "Ambulance transfer to emergency department for STEMI protocol."  
* Document urgency and time-critical nature accurately  
* Do NOT add clinical details provider didn't state (e.g., don't add "troponin elevated" if provider didn't mention labs)

**Checklist: SOAP Documentation Discipline**

* \[ \] Chief complaint documented (brief, patient's words when possible)  
* \[ \] Subjective section contains patient-reported information only  
* \[ \] Objective section contains provider's observations and measurable findings only  
* \[ \] Assessment section contains provider's diagnoses and clinical conclusions only  
* \[ \] Plan section contains provider's treatment decisions and next steps only  
* \[ \] No hallucinated facts (only information provider explicitly stated)  
* \[ \] No clinical interpretation or inference added  
* \[ \] Complete sections (all four SOAP sections present)  
* \[ \] Prompts provider for clarification when dictation unclear or incomplete  
* \[ \] Uses provider's exact terminology and language level

**Scoring Rubric:**

* SOAP section placement (20 items): 4 points (16/20 \= 80%)  
* Hallucinated facts identification: 3 points (identifies majority of added information)  
* Real-time documentation simulation: 3 points (correct section placement, no hallucinated facts, appropriate prompting)  
* **Total: 10 points (8/10 \= 80% passing)**

#### **6\) Knowledge Check (20 Items)**

**Item 1 (MCQ):** SOAP stands for: A) System, Observation, Analysis, Procedure  
 B) Subjective, Objective, Assessment, Plan  
 C) Symptom, Objective, Assessment, Prescription  
 D) Subject, Opinion, Action, Process

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Standard SOAP acronym.

**Item 2 (MCQ):** Subjective section contains: A) Provider's exam findings  
 B) Patient-reported information  
 C) Diagnosis  
 D) Treatment plan

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Subjective \= patient's report and history.

**Item 3 (True/False):** If provider examines lungs and says "clear," scribe should expand to "clear to auscultation bilaterally with no wheezes, rhonchi, or rales" for completeness.

**Answer:** False  
 **Rationale:** Document ONLY what provider states; adding detail is hallucinated facts violation.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** True — appearing "helpful" by adding medical detail crosses documentation-only boundary.

**Item 4 (MCQ):** "Patient reports pain 7 out of 10" belongs in which section? A) Subjective  
 B) Objective  
 C) Assessment  
 D) Plan

**Answer:** A  
 **Rationale:** Patient-reported pain severity \= Subjective.

**Item 5 (MCQ):** "Blood pressure 130/80" belongs in which section? A) Subjective  
 B) Objective  
 C) Assessment  
 D) Plan

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Objective measurement \= Objective section.

**Item 6 (Scenario MCQ):** Provider says "Patient has diabetes and I'm going to start insulin." Scribe documents: "Assessment: Type 2 diabetes mellitus, uncontrolled. Plan: Start insulin glargine 10 units at bedtime." What is the problem? A) No problem, appropriately documented  
 B) Scribe added "Type 2" and "uncontrolled" and specific insulin details provider didn't state (hallucinated facts)  
 C) Used wrong SOAP sections  
 D) Too brief

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Provider said only "diabetes" (not Type 2\) and "start insulin" (not specific type or dose). Scribe added unstated details.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** A — not recognizing added specificity as hallucinated facts.

**Item 7 (MCQ):** Documentation-only scope means: A) Write everything you think is important  
 B) Transcribe provider's stated observations and decisions exactly, no interpretation or added information  
 C) Document using medical terminology you learned in training  
 D) Fill gaps in provider's dictation using medical knowledge

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Documentation-only \= transcribe exactly what provider states, nothing more.

**Item 8 (True/False):** If provider assesses "hypertension" in Assessment section but didn't mention blood pressure in Objective section, scribe should add "BP elevated" to Objective section to support the Assessment.

**Answer:** False  
 **Rationale:** Cannot infer objective findings from assessment; document only what provider explicitly states in each section.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** True — trying to make note internally consistent crosses boundary.

**Item 9 (MCQ):** "Acute bronchitis" belongs in which section? A) Subjective  
 B) Objective  
 C) Assessment  
 D) Plan

**Answer:** C  
 **Rationale:** Diagnosis \= Assessment (provider's clinical conclusion).

**Item 10 (MCQ):** "Start amoxicillin 500mg three times daily for 10 days" belongs in which section? A) Subjective  
 B) Objective  
 C) Assessment  
 D) Plan

**Answer:** D  
 **Rationale:** Medication prescription \= Plan (treatment decision).

**Item 11 (Scenario MCQ):** Provider dictates: "Patient says knee is swollen. On exam, moderate effusion present." Which statement is correct? A) Both statements go in Objective  
 B) "Patient says knee is swollen" goes in Subjective; "moderate effusion present" goes in Objective  
 C) Both statements go in Subjective  
 D) Both statements go in Assessment

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Patient's report (Subjective) vs provider's examination finding (Objective) must be separated.

**Item 12 (MCQ):** Hallucinated facts are: A) Incorrect medical information  
 B) Information scribe adds that provider didn't explicitly state  
 C) Imaginary patients  
 D) Errors in vital signs

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Hallucinated facts \= added information, even if medically accurate, that provider didn't state.

**Item 13 (True/False):** Scribe role includes interpreting ambiguous provider statements using medical knowledge to complete documentation.

**Answer:** False  
 **Rationale:** Scribe does NOT interpret; escalates ambiguities to provider for clarification.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** True — believing medical knowledge allows interpretation.

**Item 14 (MCQ):** Provider says "Follow up in clinic." Scribe documents "Follow up in 2 weeks for recheck." What is the problem? A) No problem  
 B) Scribe added "2 weeks" and "recheck" that provider didn't state  
 C) Follow-up should be in Assessment  
 D) Should use different wording

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Provider didn't specify timing or purpose; scribe should prompt provider to complete ("Follow up timing?").

**Item 15 (MCQ):** If provider's dictation is unclear, scribe should: A) Use best judgment to complete  
 B) Leave section blank  
 C) Ask provider to clarify or repeat  
 D) Research correct terminology

**Answer:** C  
 **Rationale:** Prompt provider for clarification; don't guess or research independently during encounter.

**Item 16 (Scenario MCQ):** Provider examines heart and says "regular rhythm." Scribe knows provider typically documents "regular rate and rhythm." Scribe should document: A) "Regular rhythm" (what provider said)  
 B) "Regular rate and rhythm" (provider's typical phrasing)  
 C) "RRR" (abbreviation for regular rate and rhythm)  
 D) Ask provider if they meant "rate and rhythm"

**Answer:** A (or D if prompting for completeness)  
 **Rationale:** Document exactly what provider stated. May prompt for completeness: "Regular rhythm \- should I add rate?" But default is document only what was stated.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** B — adding "rate" because "typical" crosses into hallucinated facts.

**Item 17 (MCQ):** Review of Systems (ROS) typically belongs in: A) Subjective section (patient-reported symptoms)  
 B) Objective section  
 C) Assessment section  
 D) Plan section

**Answer:** A  
 **Rationale:** ROS is patient's report of symptoms by system \= Subjective. (Note: Some formats place ROS as separate section, but conceptually it's patient-reported data.)

**Item 18 (True/False):** Scribe can add ICD-10 diagnosis codes to Assessment section to help with billing.

**Answer:** False  
 **Rationale:** Coding is separate role; scribes document diagnosis in words, coders assign codes.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** True — confusing scribe role with coder role.

**Item 19 (Short Answer):** Provider says "Lungs have crackles." Where do you document this and what exact words do you use?

**Answer:** Objective section. Document: "Lungs: Crackles present." OR "Lungs: Crackles." (Use provider's exact words, no additions)

**Item 20 (MCQ):** Most serious violation of scribe documentation-only scope is: A) Typos in note  
 B) Hallucinating facts (adding information provider didn't state)  
 C) Using abbreviations  
 D) Formatting inconsistency

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Hallucinated facts create false clinical record; serious liability and accuracy violation.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** C — abbreviations are style issue, not scope violation.

#### **7\) QA and Audit Hooks**

**Evidence of Competence:**

* SOAP section placement drill (20 items, 16/20 \= 80%)  
* Hallucinated facts identification exercise (score 80%+ on identifying added information)  
* Real-time documentation simulation scored by rubric (correct sections, no hallucinated facts, appropriate prompting)  
* Knowledge check (20 items, 16/20 \= 80%)

**Supervisor Review Checklist:**

* \[ \] Learner places information in correct SOAP sections consistently  
* \[ \] Learner documents only what provider explicitly states (no hallucinated facts)  
* \[ \] Learner prompts provider for clarification when dictation unclear or incomplete  
* \[ \] Learner uses provider's exact terminology and language level  
* \[ \] Learner distinguishes patient-reported (Subjective) from provider-observed (Objective)  
* \[ \] Learner completes all four SOAP sections for each encounter

**Recordkeeping Tie-Back:**

* Module 2 completion with all simulation scores logged  
* SOAP structure competency documented (required before independent scribe work)  
* Note audits conducted periodically to verify ongoing SOAP compliance and absence of hallucinated facts  
* Module 2 scores recorded in training record

---

## **COURSE 6: SUPPORTING ROLES BOOTCAMP (PODS-BASED, UPLIFT-SPECIFIC)**

### **MODULE 3: HANDOFF PROTOCOLS AND CONTEXT TRANSFER (75 MIN)**

#### **1\) Entry-Level Primer**

**Plain Language Summary:** Handoffs (transferring work to another team member) are high-risk moments for communication failure, lost context, duplicated effort, or dropped tasks. Clean handoffs require: structured format (who/what/when/why/next), complete context transfer (enough information for recipient to continue without questions), documentation in system (handoff recorded, not just verbal), verification (recipient confirms understanding), and follow-through tracking (original owner confirms completion). Poor handoffs cause patient impact (delayed care, billing errors, missed authorizations), operational waste (rework, confusion), and team friction.

**Observable Behaviors:**

* Uses standardized handoff template for all work transfers  
* Provides complete context (account details, actions taken, current status, next steps, dependencies)  
* Documents handoff in ticketing system or tracking tool  
* Verifies recipient understands handoff before releasing ownership  
* Follows up to confirm handoff completion  
* Never assumes "someone will figure it out" \- explicit handoff required

#### **2\) Definitions**

**Handoff:** Transfer of task responsibility from one team member to another, including all context needed for recipient to continue work without gaps.

**Clean Handoff:** Structured handoff with complete information, documented trail, and verification. Recipient can proceed without additional questions or context-seeking.

**Dirty Handoff:** Incomplete, undocumented, or ambiguous handoff requiring recipient to chase information, guess at context, or duplicate prior work. Causes delays and errors.

**Handoff Template:** Standardized format ensuring consistent information transfer. Typical elements: Account/patient identifier, Task description, Actions already taken, Current status, Next steps required, Deadline/urgency, Dependencies/blockers, Contact for questions.

**Context Transfer:** Sharing relevant background information recipient needs: prior communications, attempts made, issues encountered, decisions pending, stakeholder contacts. Prevents recipient from "starting over."

**Handoff Documentation:** Recording handoff in system of record (ticket, case management system, handoff log) creating audit trail and preventing "he said/she said" confusion.

**Verification:** Recipient confirms understanding of handoff by restating key points or asking clarifying questions. Sender confirms recipient is ready to proceed.

**Follow-Through:** Original sender checks that handoff completed successfully, especially for urgent or complex items. Not micromanagement \- accountability for outcome.

**Hot Handoff:** Urgent transfer requiring immediate action (patient waiting, deadline today, escalated issue). Requires real-time communication (phone/chat) not just ticket update.

**Cold Handoff:** Non-urgent transfer via documented system, recipient works on timeline appropriate to priority. Most common handoff type.

#### **3\) Step-by-Step Procedures**

**Procedure: Execute Standard Handoff (Cold Handoff)**

1. **Prepare handoff using template** (needs\_review for client-specific template, general structure below):

    **WHO:**

   * Account/Patient identifier (account number, MRN, claim number \- use minimum necessary)  
   * Recipient team/person (which pod, which specialist, which supervisor)  
2. **WHAT:**

   * Task description: What needs to be done?  
   * Category: Authorization, claim review, denial appeal, payment posting, verification, etc.  
3. **WHEN:**

   * Deadline or target completion date  
   * Urgency level (routine, priority, urgent)  
4. **WHY (Context):**

   * Reason for task: "Patient requesting auth status," "Claim denied, needs appeal review," "Payment discrepancy reported"  
   * Actions already taken: "Called payer 3/15, confirmed auth pending. Called payer again 3/17, received auth number 123456."  
   * Current status: "Auth approved, number received, needs entry into system"  
   * Issues/blockers encountered: "Payer required additional clinical notes, obtained from provider 3/16"  
5. **NEXT STEPS:**

   * Exactly what recipient should do: "Enter auth number 123456 into system for account 789\. Notify patient of approval."  
   * Dependencies: "Waiting for provider to complete form before submitting" OR "All documents complete, ready to submit"  
   * Expected outcome: "Auth entered, patient notified, close case"  
6. **CONTACT:**

   * Who to contact with questions: Your name, extension, email  
   * Stakeholder contacts if relevant: "Patient cell: \[number\], provider office: \[number\]"  
7. **Document handoff in system:**

   * Update ticket/case status: "Handed off to \[recipient\]"  
   * Attach handoff template or paste into ticket notes  
   * Assign ticket to recipient user or queue  
   * Set appropriate priority/due date flags  
8. **Communicate handoff:**

   * For routine (cold) handoffs: System documentation sufficient, no separate communication needed  
   * For priority handoffs: Send message to recipient: "Assigned \[ticket/case\] to you, please review by \[date\]"  
   * For urgent (hot) handoffs: See hot handoff procedure below  
9. **Verify receipt (for priority/urgent):**

   * For priority items: Check recipient acknowledges within 1 business day  
   * For urgent items: Require immediate acknowledgment (within 1 hour or per policy)  
10. **Release ownership mentally:**

    * Trust recipient to handle (don't hover or micromanage)  
    * Check back at deadline if follow-through needed (see step 6\)  
11. **Follow through (for urgent/complex items):**

    * At deadline or milestone: Check ticket status  
    * If not completed: Escalate to recipient's supervisor (not accusatory, problem-solving: "Ticket 12345 deadline today, checking status")  
    * Document follow-through check in ticket

**Procedure: Execute Hot Handoff (Urgent)**

1. **Prepare handoff template same as cold handoff** (documentation still required)

2. **Real-time communication FIRST:**

   * Call or instant message recipient directly  
   * "I need to hand off urgent item to you. Patient on hold / Deadline in 2 hours / Escalated issue. Can you take this now?"  
   * Verify recipient available and ready to proceed  
   * If recipient unavailable: Escalate to their supervisor or another team member immediately  
3. **Brief verbal context:**

   * Summarize key points from handoff template verbally (1-2 minutes)  
   * "Account 789, patient waiting for auth status, I just received approval from payer, you need to enter auth number 123456 and call patient back at \[number\] within next hour."  
   * Recipient restates understanding: "Got it, I'll enter auth 123456 for account 789 and call patient at \[number\] within the hour."  
4. **Send documentation simultaneously:**

   * While on call/chat, assign ticket and send handoff template  
   * "I'm assigning ticket 12345 to you now with full details."  
5. **Confirm start:**

   * "Can you start on this right now?" → Wait for confirmation  
   * If recipient cannot start immediately: Escalate further  
6. **Monitor completion:**

   * For hot handoffs, follow up within stated timeframe  
   * "Checking if you were able to call patient on ticket 12345?"  
   * Document outcome in ticket

**Procedure: Receive Handoff Professionally**

**When handoff assigned to you:**

1. **Review handoff documentation immediately** (for priority/urgent) or within 1 business day (for routine)

2. **Verify completeness:**

   * Do I have all information needed to proceed?  
   * Account identifier clear?  
   * Next steps actionable?  
   * Deadline understood?  
   * Context sufficient?  
3. **If incomplete, request clarification immediately:**

   * Reply in ticket: "Need additional info: \[specific question\]. Cannot proceed until clarified."  
   * Tag sender or escalate to supervisor if sender unresponsive  
   * DO NOT guess or assume missing information  
4. **If complete, acknowledge:**

   * For urgent: Acknowledge within 1 hour: "Received handoff, starting now"  
   * For priority: Acknowledge within 1 business day: "Handoff received, will complete by \[date\]"  
   * For routine: System assignment acknowledgment sufficient (start work per normal priority)  
5. **Execute task per handoff instructions:**

   * Follow next steps as documented  
   * Document actions taken in ticket as you progress  
6. **Close loop:**

   * When complete: Update ticket status "Completed," document outcome  
   * If applicable: Notify sender "Ticket 12345 complete, \[outcome summary\]"  
   * For complex handoffs: Brief outcome summary to sender appreciated

**Procedure: Handle Handoff Failures**

**If you discover handoff was incomplete or incorrect:**

1. **Document the gap:**

   * In ticket: "Handoff incomplete: \[specific missing information\]. Cannot proceed without \[X\]."  
   * Include what you tried: "Attempted to proceed with information provided, but encountered \[issue\]"  
2. **Request clarification from sender:**

   * Tag sender in ticket with specific question  
   * If urgent and sender unresponsive: Escalate to sender's supervisor  
3. **Escalate if pattern:**

   * If same sender provides consistently incomplete handoffs: Discuss with your supervisor  
   * Supervisor coaching needed for sender  
4. **Do NOT:**

   * Proceed with incomplete information and "hope for the best"  
   * Complain to colleagues without resolving  
   * Leave ticket abandoned without documentation

**Safe Stop Rules:**

* Stop if handoff information is incomplete — request clarification before proceeding  
* Stop if handoff has no deadline/priority — ask sender for timeframe  
* Stop if you're unsure you can complete handoff task — escalate to supervisor immediately (don't accept handoff beyond your capability)  
* Stop if handoff involves area outside your training — escalate (don't "learn on the fly" with patient-impacting work)

**Escalation Path:** Sender (for clarification) → Your supervisor (if you cannot execute) → Sender's supervisor (if sender unresponsive or pattern of poor handoffs)

**Documentation Requirements:**

* Every handoff documented in ticket/case system with template elements  
* Handoff receipt acknowledgment (for priority/urgent)  
* Handoff outcome documented upon completion  
* Handoff failures/gaps documented with specific issues

#### **4\) Worked Examples**

**Compliant Example 1 \- Clean Cold Handoff:**

**Ticket 54321 assigned from Benefits Coordinator to Authorization Specialist:**

**HANDOFF DETAILS:**

**WHO:** Account 789456, Patient: \[Use MRN or account number only per minimum necessary\]  
 **WHAT:** Prior authorization submission for outpatient MRI lumbar spine  
 **WHEN:** Submit by 3/20/2024 (appointment scheduled 3/25)  
 **WHY:** Patient referred for MRI, payer requires prior auth. Called payer 3/15, confirmed auth required. Verified benefits, MRI covered, $200 patient responsibility. Obtained clinical notes from provider office 3/17. All documentation complete.  
 **CURRENT STATUS:** Ready to submit. All required documents attached to ticket (order, clinical notes, insurance card copy).  
 **NEXT STEPS:** Review documents for completeness, submit prior auth to payer via portal, track until approval/denial received, enter auth number into system when approved, notify patient of outcome and patient responsibility amount.  
 **DEPENDENCIES:** None, all documents complete.  
 **CONTACT:** \[Benefits Coordinator name\], ext 1234, \[email\]

**Why Compliant:** Complete template, all context provided, actions taken documented, current status clear, next steps specific and actionable, no gaps requiring recipient to ask questions, documented in ticket system.

**Authorization Specialist receives handoff:**

* Reviews ticket same day  
* Acknowledges: "Handoff received, will submit by 3/19"  
* Submits auth per instructions  
* Updates ticket with auth number when received  
* Notifies patient  
* Closes ticket with outcome documentation

**Outcome:** Clean execution, no delays, no rework, patient notified timely.

**Compliant Example 2 \- Hot Handoff:**

Patient on hold, needs urgent help with claim issue. Benefits Coordinator must leave for end of shift. Patient Claims Specialist available.

**Real-time handoff (phone call):** Benefits Coordinator: "I have patient on hold for urgent claim issue. Can you take this handoff now?" Patient Claims Specialist: "Yes, go ahead." Benefits Coordinator: "Account 456789, patient name \[verbally\], on hold at extension 5678\. Claim 123ABC denied code CO-50, patient received bill for $500. Patient is upset and asking if we can fix today. I pulled claim details, denial is for missing modifier, should be easy correction and resubmission. I'm assigning ticket 99999 to you with all details. Can you take the call now and handle?" Patient Claims Specialist: "Got it. Account 456789, claim 123ABC, denied for missing modifier, patient on hold ext 5678\. I'll take the call now and work the correction. I'll update ticket 99999 when resolved." Benefits Coordinator: "Perfect, thanks. Transferring call to you now."

**Documented handoff in ticket 99999:** \[Full template as in Example 1, with urgent flag and "Patient on hold" note\]

**Patient Claims Specialist:**

* Takes call immediately  
* Works correction  
* Resubmits claim  
* Updates patient  
* Documents outcome in ticket  
* Notifies Benefits Coordinator: "Resolved, claim resubmitted, patient satisfied"

**Why Compliant:** Hot handoff protocol followed (real-time communication FIRST), verification of recipient availability, brief verbal context with restatement, documentation still completed, immediate execution, loop closed with sender notification.

**Non-Compliant Example \- Dirty Handoff:**

**Ticket 11111 assigned from Order Entry to Benefits Verification:**

**Ticket note:** "Need auth. Please work."

**No additional information. Benefits Verification receives handoff:**

* What account? Not specified.  
* What service needs auth? Not specified.  
* What's the deadline? Not specified.  
* What actions already taken? Unknown.  
* What documentation exists? Unknown.  
* Who is the patient contact? Unknown.

**Benefits Verification attempts:**

* Spends 20 minutes searching for account based on ticket ID  
* Finds account, but multiple orders present \- which one needs auth?  
* Calls Order Entry person \- no answer  
* Sends email asking for clarification \- response delayed 24 hours  
* Meanwhile, patient calls asking about auth status \- Benefits Verification has no information  
* Finally gets clarification after 48 hours, submits auth  
* Auth delayed 2 days due to incomplete handoff, patient frustrated

**Why Non-Compliant:** Handoff violated every principle:

* No template used  
* No context provided  
* Ambiguous task description  
* No deadline  
* No contact information  
* Created rework, delay, patient dissatisfaction  
* Waste of Benefits Verification time trying to reconstruct context

**Result:** Coaching for Order Entry person on handoff protocol, escalated to supervisor, mandatory Module 3 refresher, pattern monitoring.

#### **5\) Practice Pack**

**Drill Set: Complete vs Incomplete Handoffs (10 Scenarios)**

Rate each handoff: COMPLETE (ready to execute) or INCOMPLETE (missing critical information)

1. "Account 123, need auth, please submit." → INCOMPLETE (no service type, no deadline, no context, no documents mentioned)

2. "Account 456, prior auth for PT eval, order attached, payer confirmed auth required 3/1, submit by 3/5, patient contact \[number\] if questions." → COMPLETE (service, context, deadline, document, contact)

3. "Claim denied, fix it." → INCOMPLETE (no claim number, no account, no denial reason, no context)

4. "Account 789, claim 456ABC denied CO-50 modifier missing, corrected modifier is 25, resubmit, deadline 3/10, prior notes in ticket." → COMPLETE (account, claim, issue, solution, deadline, context reference)

5. "Patient called, needs help with bill." → INCOMPLETE (no account, no specific issue, no patient contact, no actions taken)

6. "Account 321, patient called re: $200 bill for lab, claims processed, patient responsibility correct per benefits, explained to patient, patient still wants supervisor review, escalating to you, patient callback \[number\]." → COMPLETE (account, context, actions taken, current status, next step clear, contact)

7. "Urgent\! Handle ASAP." → INCOMPLETE (no context, no task, no account)

8. "Account 555, need payment posted." → INCOMPLETE (no payment amount, no payment source, no date, no documentation reference)

9. "Account 777, payment $300 received 3/15 check \#999, post to claim 789XY, payment EOB attached in system, post by 3/17." → COMPLETE (account, amount, source, date, claim, document, deadline)

10. "Someone needs to call this patient back." → INCOMPLETE (no account, no patient contact, no reason for callback, no context)

**Scoring:** 80% \= 8/10 correct

**Scenario Exercise: Draft Clean Handoff**

**Scenario:** You are Order Entry Specialist. You received order for MRI of right shoulder. You verified insurance, confirmed authorization required. You called payer, they need clinical notes before they can review auth. You requested notes from provider office 3/10, still waiting. Patient appointment scheduled 3/25. You need to hand off to Authorization team to follow up on notes and submit auth when received.

**Draft handoff using template:**

**Sample Compliant Handoff:**

**WHO:** Account 654321, \[Patient MRN\]  
 **WHAT:** Prior authorization for MRI right shoulder  
 **WHEN:** Appointment scheduled 3/25, submit auth by 3/22 to allow processing time  
 **WHY (Context):** Patient referred for MRI right shoulder by Dr. Smith. Insurance verified, payer requires prior auth. Called payer 3/10, confirmed auth required and clinical notes needed. Requested notes from Dr. Smith's office 3/10 (contact: \[office phone\]), office said will send by 3/15.  
 **CURRENT STATUS:** Waiting for clinical notes from provider office. Order and insurance card scanned and attached to ticket. All other documentation complete.  
 **NEXT STEPS:** Follow up with Dr. Smith's office on 3/15 to confirm notes sent. Once notes received, review for completeness, submit prior auth via payer portal. Track auth approval. Enter auth number when approved. Notify patient of outcome and any patient responsibility.  
 **DEPENDENCIES:** Clinical notes from provider office (pending)  
 **CONTACT:** \[Your name\], ext 2345, \[email\]. Provider office: \[number\].

**Why Compliant:** Complete template, full context, actions taken documented, dependencies clear, specific next steps, contact information provided.

**Mini-Simulation Script:** **Trainer plays:** Recipient of handoff with questions  
 **Learner plays:** Sender executing handoff

**Trainer (as recipient):** "I received your handoff on ticket 5555\. The note says 'need auth for account 999.' I need more information \- what service, what's the deadline, what have you done so far?"

**Learner expected response:** "Let me complete the handoff properly. \[Opens template, provides\]:

* Account 999, patient \[MRN\]  
* Service: Physical therapy evaluation  
* Deadline: Submit by \[date\], patient has appointment \[date\]  
* Actions taken: Verified insurance 3/12

, confirmed auth required. Order and insurance card attached.

* Next steps: Review attached documents, submit auth via portal, track until approval  
* Contact: \[My name and extension\] if questions I'll update the ticket right now with complete details."

**Trainer:** "Better. What if I find the documents incomplete when I start?"

**Learner expected response:** "Tag me in the ticket with specifically what's missing. I'll get it and update. If it's urgent and I'm not responding quickly, escalate to my supervisor \[name\]. Don't let it sit \- let's resolve gaps immediately."

**Checklist: Handoff Execution**

* \[ \] Uses standardized template (WHO, WHAT, WHEN, WHY, NEXT STEPS, CONTACT)  
* \[ \] Provides complete context (actions taken, current status, blockers)  
* \[ \] Documents handoff in system (not just verbal)  
* \[ \] Assigns to specific recipient or queue  
* \[ \] Sets appropriate priority/deadline flags  
* \[ \] For hot handoffs: communicates real-time FIRST, then documents  
* \[ \] Verifies recipient understanding (for urgent/complex)  
* \[ \] Follows through to confirm completion (for urgent/complex)  
* \[ \] Receives handoffs professionally (reviews promptly, acknowledges, requests clarification if needed)  
* \[ \] Closes loop when handoff complete (updates status, notifies sender if applicable)

**Scoring Rubric:**

* Handoff completeness assessment (10 scenarios): 3 points (8/10 \= 80%)  
* Clean handoff draft: 4 points (uses template, complete information, actionable next steps, contact provided)  
* Mini-simulation: 3 points (responds appropriately to incomplete handoff scenario, commits to improvement)  
* **Total: 10 points (8/10 \= 80% passing)**

#### **6\) Knowledge Check (20 Items)**

**Item 1 (MCQ):** Clean handoff requires: A) Just telling someone verbally  
 B) Structured template, complete context, documentation, verification  
 C) Email only  
 D) Supervisor approval

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Clean handoff \= structured format \+ complete information \+ documentation \+ verification.

**Item 2 (MCQ):** Dirty handoff causes: A) Efficient workflow  
 B) Delays, rework, confusion, patient impact  
 C) Better communication  
 D) Time savings

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Incomplete handoffs create operational waste and patient impact.

**Item 3 (True/False):** "Need auth, please handle" is sufficient handoff documentation.

**Answer:** False  
 **Rationale:** Missing critical information (account, service, deadline, context, documents, contact).  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** True — not recognizing extreme incompleteness.

**Item 4 (MCQ):** Hot handoff differs from cold handoff because: A) It's more important  
 B) It requires real-time communication first, then documentation  
 C) It doesn't need documentation  
 D) Only supervisors can do hot handoffs

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Hot handoff \= urgent, requires immediate real-time contact PLUS documentation.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** C — documentation still required for hot handoffs.

**Item 5 (Scenario MCQ):** You receive handoff: "Account 555, patient waiting on hold, handle now." What do you do first? A) Review full ticket details thoroughly before calling patient  
 B) Ask sender for verbal context immediately while taking call  
 C) Ignore since incomplete  
 D) Escalate to supervisor

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Patient waiting \= hot handoff, get brief verbal context and take call immediately; can review full details during/after call.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** A — patient waiting requires immediate action, not extended review.

**Item 6 (MCQ):** Handoff template should include (select essential element): A) Sender's opinion of the task  
 B) Account identifier, task description, deadline, context, next steps, contact  
 C) Sender's personal schedule  
 D) Recipient's training history

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Template essential elements \= who/what/when/why/next/contact.

**Item 7 (True/False):** If handoff is incomplete, you should guess at the missing information and proceed rather than delay the work.

**Answer:** False  
 **Rationale:** Request clarification immediately; guessing creates errors and risks.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** True — "just get it done" mentality sacrifices accuracy.

**Item 8 (MCQ):** When receiving handoff, you should: A) Start work without reviewing details  
 B) Review for completeness, request clarification if needed, acknowledge receipt  
 C) Assume sender provided everything needed  
 D) Forward to another team member

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Professional receipt \= review, clarify gaps, acknowledge.

**Item 9 (Scenario MCQ):** Handoff says "Submit auth by 3/15" but doesn't specify which payer or provide insurance information. What do you do? A) Submit to any payer  
 B) Tag sender in ticket: "Need payer name and insurance details to proceed"  
 C) Close ticket as incomplete  
 D) Guess based on account history

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Request specific missing information immediately; cannot proceed without payer details.

**Item 10 (MCQ):** Context transfer means: A) Moving files between folders  
 B) Sharing relevant background information recipient needs to continue work  
 C) Copying ticket to another system  
 D) Translating to another language

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Context transfer \= background info for seamless continuation.

**Item 11 (True/False):** Documentation of handoffs in system creates audit trail and prevents "he said/she said" confusion.

**Answer:** True  
 **Rationale:** System documentation provides accountability and clarity.

**Item 12 (MCQ):** Follow-through on handoff means: A) Micromanaging recipient  
 B) Checking completion at deadline, especially for urgent/complex items  
 C) Doing the work yourself  
 D) Ignoring after handoff

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Follow-through \= accountability check at deadline, not micromanagement.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** A — checking deadline is responsibility, not micromanagement.

**Item 13 (Scenario MCQ):** You consistently receive incomplete handoffs from same colleague. What do you do? A) Complain to other coworkers  
 B) Discuss with your supervisor for coaching of sender  
 C) Refuse all handoffs from that person  
 D) Complete handoffs despite gaps

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Pattern of poor handoffs requires supervisor intervention for coaching.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** D — accommodating poor handoffs enables pattern to continue.

**Item 14 (MCQ):** If you cannot execute handoff task (beyond your capability/training), you should: A) Try your best and hope it works  
 B) Escalate to your supervisor immediately  
 C) Research how to do it online  
 D) Hand off to someone else without checking

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Don't accept handoffs beyond capability; escalate immediately.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** A — "trying your best" with patient-impacting work creates risk.

**Item 15 (True/False):** Verbal handoff without documentation is acceptable for urgent items since documentation takes time.

**Answer:** False  
 **Rationale:** Even hot handoffs require documentation (real-time communication FIRST, then document).  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** True — urgency doesn't eliminate documentation requirement.

**Item 16 (MCQ):** "Actions already taken" in handoff template prevents: A) Recipient from duplicating work already done  
 B) Supervisor review  
 C) Ticket closure  
 D) Patient contact

**Answer:** A  
 **Rationale:** Documenting prior actions prevents rework and provides context.

**Item 17 (Scenario MCQ):** Handoff includes next steps: "Call payer and ask about claim." This is: A) Sufficient direction  
 B) Insufficient \- needs claim number, specific question, payer contact, context  
 C) Too detailed  
 D) Perfect handoff

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Lacks specifics needed to execute (which claim, what question, which payer department, why calling).  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** A — "call payer" seems like action but lacks executable detail.

**Item 18 (MCQ):** When closing loop on completed handoff, you should: A) Say nothing; completion is obvious  
 B) Update ticket status, document outcome, notify sender if applicable  
 C) Only update if sender asks  
 D) Wait for sender to check

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Close loop \= update system, document outcome, notify sender for accountability.

**Item 19 (Short Answer):** List the six essential elements of handoff template acronym WHO WHAT WHEN WHY NEXT CONTACT stands for.

**Answer:**

1. WHO: Account/patient identifier and recipient  
2. WHAT: Task description  
3. WHEN: Deadline/urgency  
4. WHY: Context (background, actions taken, current status)  
5. NEXT STEPS: What recipient should do  
6. CONTACT: Who to contact with questions

**Item 20 (MCQ):** Poor handoffs create patient impact by: A) Causing delays in care, billing errors, missed authorizations  
 B) Improving efficiency  
 C) Reducing documentation burden  
 D) Streamlining communication

**Answer:** A  
 **Rationale:** Incomplete handoffs directly impact patient experience and outcomes through delays and errors.

#### **7\) QA and Audit Hooks**

**Evidence of Competence:**

* Handoff completeness drill (10 scenarios, 8/10 \= 80%)  
* Clean handoff draft exercise (scored by rubric: template use, completeness, actionable next steps)  
* Knowledge check (20 items, 16/20 \= 80%)  
* Real-work handoff audit (supervisor reviews sample of learner's actual handoffs for completeness)

**Supervisor Review Checklist:**

* \[ \] Learner uses handoff template consistently  
* \[ \] Learner provides complete context in handoffs  
* \[ \] Learner documents handoffs in system (not just verbal)  
* \[ \] Learner receives handoffs professionally (reviews, clarifies, acknowledges)  
* \[ \] Learner follows through on urgent/complex handoffs  
* \[ \] Learner escalates incomplete handoffs appropriately  
* \[ \] Sample audit shows clean handoff execution in real work

**Recordkeeping Tie-Back:**

* Module 3 completion with all exercise scores logged  
* Handoff quality baseline established (will be monitored ongoing through ticket audits)  
* Module 3 scores recorded in training record  
* Ongoing handoff quality tracked as operational metric (% of handoffs requiring clarification)

# **COMPREHENSIVE FRAMEWORK SUMMARY FOR REMAINING MODULES**

**The following structure applies to ALL remaining modules across Courses 2-6:**

## **Standard 7-Part Module Structure**

### **1\) Entry-Level Primer**

* Plain language summary (2-3 sentences: what this module does, why it matters)  
* Observable behaviors (3-5 bullet points: what "good" looks like after completing module)

### **2\) Definitions**

* All technical terms defined in plain language  
* needs\_review flags for client-specific elements  
* Examples provided for abstract concepts

### **3\) Step-by-Step Procedures**

* 5-15 numbered steps for each major task in module  
* Safe stop rules (4-6 per module: situations requiring pause and escalation)  
* Escalation paths specified  
* Documentation requirements listed

### **4\) Worked Examples**

* 2 compliant examples (showing correct application from source scenarios)  
* 1 non-compliant example (showing common failure mode from source scenarios)  
* "Why compliant/non-compliant" explanation for each  
* Consequences specified for non-compliant patterns

### **5\) Practice Pack**

* Drill set (10-20 items, typically 80% passing)  
* Scenario exercise (1-2 complex scenarios requiring application of procedures)  
* Mini-simulation script (trainer-learner role play with expected responses)  
* Checklist (8-12 items covering key competencies)  
* Scoring rubric (10 points total, 8/10 \= 80% passing standard)

### **6\) Knowledge Check**

* 12-20 items (mix of MCQ, True/False, Scenario MCQ, Short Answer)  
* 80% passing standard (calculate: 16/20, 12/15, 10/12 depending on item count)  
* Answer key with rationales tied to source requirements  
* Common wrong answers identified with explanations  
* Tests application, not just recall

### **7\) QA and Audit Hooks**

* Evidence of competence (artifacts required from practice pack)  
* Supervisor review checklist (observable competencies to verify)  
* Recordkeeping tie-back (how this module data flows to training records system)

---

## **Course-Specific Application Notes**

### **COURSE 2 (ICD-10 for Non-Coders) \- Modules 1, 2, 4-6, 8-12**

**Critical boundary reinforcement:** Every module emphasizes non-coder scope (flag and route, never assign codes, draft neutral queries without code suggestions)

**Key procedures patterns:**

* Code structure analysis (identify but don't select)  
* Documentation gap identification  
* Provider query drafting (neutral language)  
* Denial root cause analysis (separate coding error from coverage limitation)  
* Escalation to coder (when specificity change needed)

**Common scenarios across modules:**

* Unspecified vs specific code analysis  
* Documentation supports more specific code → flag for coder  
* Provider query needed → draft without suggesting codes  
* Denial analysis → identify diagnosis-related vs other causes

### **COURSE 3 (Document Hygiene) \- Modules 1-4, 6-18**

**Critical controls reinforcement:** Clean screen/desk, storage location verification, redaction before sharing, channel discipline, no screenshots, timely updates

**Key procedures patterns:**

* Daily workspace setup verification  
* End-of-shift cleanup protocol  
* File storage location selection (check approved list)  
* Redaction tool usage  
* Screenshot alternatives (verbal description, screen share, test environment)  
* Update status in system before leaving work

**Common scenarios across modules:**

* Workspace interruption → secure immediately  
* Sharing needed → verify channel approved, redact PHI  
* Screenshot requested → refuse, offer alternatives  
* Storage uncertain → escalate before saving  
* Update overdue → complete before end of shift

### **COURSE 4 (Medical Scribe) \- Modules 1, 3-26**

**Critical scope reinforcement:** Documentation-only (no interpretation, no hallucinated facts, no clinical decisions)

**Key procedures patterns:**

* Listen to provider statement exactly  
* Transcribe in correct note section (SOAP or specialty format)  
* Prompt provider for clarification when unclear  
* Use 200-term job aid for terminology verification  
* Never add information provider didn't state  
* Specialty templates application (Modules 17-24 cover 8 specialties)

**Common scenarios across modules:**

* Provider's statement unclear → ask for clarification immediately  
* Terminology unfamiliar → ask provider to spell/define, use job aid  
* Documentation seems incomplete → prompt provider (don't fill gaps)  
* Specialty-specific format required → use approved template  
* Real-time documentation → type while listening, confirm accuracy

### **COURSE 5 (Executive Assistant) \- Modules 1-15**

**Critical controls reinforcement:** PHI-free calendars, minimum necessary triage, verification for executive requests, redacted distribution

**Key procedures patterns:**

* Calendar entry PHI check (remove patient names, use generic descriptions)  
* Inbox triage without over-reading (route by recipient, don't read unnecessary PHI)  
* Meeting preparation (redact notes before broad distribution)  
* Verification applies even to executives (no shortcuts for authority)  
* Attendee limitation (need-to-know principle for meeting invites)

**Common scenarios across modules:**

* Calendar entry includes patient name → sanitize before sending  
* Meeting notes contain PHI → redact before distribution to all attendees  
* Executive requests PHI urgently → verify executive has need-to-know, apply minimum necessary  
* Inbox contains PHI → route to owner without reading full content unless necessary for triage  
* Vendor meeting coordination → no PHI in external communications

### **COURSE 6 (Supporting Roles Bootcamp) \- Modules 1-2, 4-14**

**Common Core (Modules 1-8) for all roles:**

* Quality metrics understanding and tracking  
* Audit sampling and response procedures  
* Handoff protocols (Module 3 detailed above)  
* Escalation documentation standards  
* Professionalism under pressure  
* Conflict resolution techniques  
* Time management and priority setting  
* Continuous improvement behaviors

**Role-Specific Tracks (Modules 9-14+):**

* Module 9-14: Client Success Specialist (Medical Benefits) fully detailed in source  
  * Benefits investigations, pathway determination, cost estimates, financial assistance, worklist management, failure mode troubleshooting  
* Additional role tracks (Order Entry Specialist, Patient Claims Specialist, etc.) follow same structure:  
  * Role-specific workflows integrated with Courses 1-3 foundations  
  * Do-not-do boundaries from Course 1 reinforced  
  * Quality metrics specific to role  
  * Common failure modes for role  
  * Scenario library specific to role's daily tasks

* Course 6: Minimum necessary in handoffs, escalations, team communications

* Course 1 Module 4: Patient identity verification protocol  
* Course 1 Module 2: Authorization verification before disclosure  
* Course 1 Module 7: Recipient verification before sending  
* Course 5: Verification applies to executive requests

* Course 1 Module 9: Audit-ready documentation with attribution

* Course 4: SOAP structure with no hallucinated facts  
* Course 5: Meeting notes documentation with redaction  
* Course 6: Handoff documentation in system

* Applies across all courses when policy violation or risk event occurs  
* All roles report incidents and near-misses immediately  
* Evidence preservation (do-not-delete) applies universally  
* Module 10 procedure referenced in all subsequent courses

### **Universal Sanctions Framework**

* Course 0 Module 4 / Course 1 Module 12: Progressive discipline (counseling → written warning → final warning → termination)  
* Acceleration clause for high-severity violations (PHI exposure, fraud, circumvention, credential sharing, curiosity browsing, screenshot violations, evidence tampering)  
* Applies uniformly across all roles and tenure levels

## **PRACTICAL IMPLEMENTATION GUIDANCE**

### **For Learning Management System (LMS) Configuration:**

**Course Prerequisites Enforcement:**

* Course 0 → Course 1 → {Course 2, 3} → {Course 4, 5, 6 as applicable by role}  
* Lock subsequent courses until prerequisites 100% complete  
* Course 1 role variants lock until core modules 1-12 complete

**Assessment Configuration:**

* Knowledge checks: 80% passing standard (except Module 5 screenshot prohibition \= 100%)  
* Unlimited attempts with cooling period after 3rd failure (24-48 hours, needs\_review per client)  
* Randomize question order and answer options where possible  
* Require sequential module completion (cannot skip ahead)

**Artifact Submission Workflow:**

* Designated submission points within each module  
* Supervisor review queue for artifacts requiring evaluation  
* Automated pass/fail for objective exercises (drill sets)  
* Rubric-based scoring for subjective exercises (written responses, documentation samples)

**Tracking and Reporting:**

* Individual learner dashboard showing course/module progress  
* Supervisor dashboard showing team completion rates and bottlenecks  
* Compliance dashboard showing org-wide completion by role and deadline  
* Refresher due date tracking with automated notifications (30 days advance)  
* Attempt counts and cooling period status visible to supervisors

### **For Supervisors Conducting Training:**

**Module Delivery Sequence:**

1. Assign module with entry-level day plan timeline  
2. Learner completes primer, definitions, procedures (reading)  
3. Learner reviews worked examples (video or text)  
4. Learner completes practice pack (hands-on exercises)  
5. Supervisor spot-checks practice pack submissions for quality  
6. Learner takes knowledge check (80% required to pass)  
7. If fail: review missed items, study relevant procedures, cooling period if 3+ failures  
8. If pass: module marked complete, next module unlocks

**Supervisor Review Priorities:**

* Practice pack artifacts (ensure quality, not just completion)  
* Knowledge check scores (identify struggling learners early)  
* Attempt patterns (multiple failures indicate need for intervention)  
* Real-work application (observe learned behaviors in actual work within 1 week of module completion)

**Coaching Interventions:**

* 2 failures: One-on-one review of missed concepts before 3rd attempt  
* 3 failures (cooling period triggered): Mandatory coaching session, learning plan, extended study time  
* Pattern across modules: Evaluate overall readiness for role, possible remediation plan or role reconsideration

### **For Learners:**

**Study Strategies:**

* Read procedures carefully; these become your job instructions  
* Practice drills until 90%+ accuracy before attempting knowledge check  
* Use worked examples to understand "why" behind procedures  
* Take notes during mini-simulations (you'll use these skills daily)  
* Ask supervisor for real-world examples if concepts unclear  
* Use job aids during actual work (they're designed for reference, not memorization)

**Time Management:**

* Course 0: 2-3 hours (complete before Course 1\)  
* Course 1: 6-16 hours depending on track (pace across 5 days per entry-level plan)  
* Course 2: 4-12 hours (pace across 6 days for Standard track)  
* Course 3: 8 hours (pace across 6 days)  
* Course 4: 20 hours (pace across 10 days)  
* Course 5: 10 hours (pace across 5 days)  
* Course 6: 16-24 hours (Common Core \+ role track)  
* **Total onboarding: 40-75 hours depending on role** (typically 2-3 weeks full-time equivalent)

**Success Indicators:**

* Pass knowledge checks first attempt (shows comprehension)  
* Practice pack scores 90%+ (shows mastery)  
* Real-work application within 1 week (shows retention)  
* No incidents related to trained topics in first 90 days (shows behavior change)  
* Positive feedback from team on handoffs, documentation, collaboration (shows integration)

1. **Annual calendar:** All courses refresh every 12 months (or shorter per client requirement)

3. **Policy change:** Affected modules refresh within 30 days of change  
4. **Incident/audit finding:** Individual completes targeted refresher on failed topic within 14 days

* **Training record audits:** Quarterly verification of completion, attempts, cooling periods, scores  
* **Real-work audits:** Sample learner work product against module standards (documentation, handoffs, notes)  
* **Knowledge retention checks:** Spot quizzes 30/60/90 days post-training  
* **Incident correlation:** Track whether incidents correlate with training gaps
