# **ADDITIONAL COMPLETE MODULE BUILDS (FINAL SET)**

## **COURSE 2: ICD-10 CODING OVERVIEW FOR OPERATIONS TEAMS**

### **MODULE 8: COMMON DENIAL DRIVERS RELATED TO DIAGNOSIS CODING (75 MIN)**

#### **1\) Entry-Level Primer**

**Plain Language Summary:** Claim denials waste resources, delay payment, and frustrate patients. Many denials are diagnosis-related: unspecified codes (lacks detail payer needs), diagnosis-service mismatches (diagnosis doesn't support medical necessity for service), invalid codes (outdated/incorrect format), or coverage limitations (diagnosis not on payer's covered list). Your role is identifying denial root cause category (specificity issue vs mismatch vs invalid code vs coverage policy), then choosing correct resolution path: provider query for specificity, coder review for code accuracy, appeal preparation for coverage disputes. Understanding denial patterns prevents future denials and improves revenue cycle.

**Observable Behaviors:**

* Reads denial reason codes and explanations accurately  
* Categorizes denials into root cause types (specificity, mismatch, invalid, coverage)  
* Chooses appropriate resolution path based on denial type  
* Distinguishes coding errors from coverage limitations (Source Scenario 19 pattern)  
* Escalates complex denials to authorization or appeals team  
* Documents denial analysis and resolution steps

#### **2\) Definitions**

**Denial:** Payer's refusal to pay claim, requiring correction or appeal for payment. Creates accounts receivable and patient billing issues.

**Denial Reason Code:** Standardized code explaining why claim was denied. Common formats: CO (Contractual Obligation), PR (Patient Responsibility), OA (Other Adjustment). Examples: CO-50 (payment adjusted because services not covered), CO-16 (claim lacks information needed for adjudication).

**Remark Code:** Additional explanation accompanying denial reason code, providing specific details. Example: "Diagnosis does not support medical necessity for this procedure."

**Denial Root Cause Categories:**

1. **Specificity Issue:** Unspecified diagnosis code used when specific code required for medical necessity determination  
2. **Diagnosis-Service Mismatch:** Diagnosis doesn't logically support need for service billed  
3. **Invalid Code:** Incorrect code format, outdated code, truncated code, non-existent code  
4. **Coverage Limitation:** Diagnosis not on payer's covered indications list per LCD/NCD, or frequency/quantity exceeded

**Resolution Paths (based on root cause):**

* **Specificity Issue → Provider Query:** Request provider clarify documentation to support more specific code, coder reviews and updates code, claim resubmitted  
* **Diagnosis-Service Mismatch → Coder Review:** Verify correct diagnosis submitted for service, may require provider query if documentation unclear, correct code and resubmit  
* **Invalid Code → Coder Review:** Correct code format/selection, resubmit with valid code  
* **Coverage Limitation → Appeal Preparation OR Patient Notification:** If service was medically necessary but not covered per policy, prepare appeal with supporting documentation OR notify patient of patient responsibility if appeal unlikely to succeed

**Appeal:** Formal request for payer to reconsider denial, includes supporting documentation (medical records, LCD/NCD references, medical necessity explanation). Requires authorization/appeals specialist involvement.

**Corrected Claim:** Claim resubmitted after correction (code updated, information added). Typically processed faster than appeals.

**Medical Necessity Denial:** Denial stating service not medically necessary for diagnosis submitted. Can be due to: (1) wrong diagnosis submitted (coding error), (2) insufficient documentation (provider query needed), or (3) payer coverage policy excludes diagnosis (coverage limitation, not coding error).

**Timely Filing:** Deadline for claim submission or appeal (typically 90-365 days from service date depending on payer). Missing timely filing \= automatic denial with no appeal possible.

#### **3\) Step-by-Step Procedures**

**Procedure: Analyze Denial and Determine Root Cause**

1. **Access denial information:**

   * Denial letter/EOB (Explanation of Benefits)  
   * OR denial code in claim processing system  
   * OR payer portal denial details  
2. **Identify denial reason code and remark codes:**

   * Primary reason code (e.g., CO-50, CO-16, CO-197)  
   * Remark codes providing additional detail  
   * Denial explanation text  
3. **Categorize denial using decision tree:**

    **Question 1: Does denial mention "unspecified," "non-specific," or "more specific diagnosis needed"?**

   * YES → **Specificity Issue**  
   * NO → Continue to Question 2  
4. **Question 2: Does denial mention "diagnosis does not support medical necessity" or "diagnosis-procedure mismatch"?**

   * YES → **Diagnosis-Service Mismatch** (possible coding error OR coverage limitation)  
   * NO → Continue to Question 3  
5. **Question 3: Does denial mention "invalid code," "incorrect code format," "code not valid for date of service"?**

   * YES → **Invalid Code**  
   * NO → Continue to Question 4  
6. **Question 4: Does denial reference LCD/NCD, "not a covered indication," "not on covered diagnosis list," or "frequency exceeded"?**

   * YES → **Coverage Limitation**  
   * NO → **Other Denial Type** (outside diagnosis-coding scope, escalate to claims team)  
7. **Review claim details:**

   * What diagnosis code(s) were submitted?  
   * What service/procedure was billed?  
   * What does provider documentation say about diagnosis and service need?  
   * Is there LCD/NCD for this service?  
8. **Determine if denial is coding-related or coverage-related:**

   * **Coding-related:** Wrong code used, code format incorrect, more specific code available that would support medical necessity  
   * **Coverage-related:** Correct code used per documentation, but payer policy doesn't cover diagnosis-service combination  
9. **Document analysis:**

   * Denial reason code: \[code\]  
   * Root cause category: \[specificity/mismatch/invalid/coverage\]  
   * Claim details: \[diagnosis codes, service codes\]  
   * Preliminary assessment: \[coding error vs coverage limitation\]  
   * Recommended resolution path: \[provider query/coder review/appeal/patient notification\]

**Procedure: Choose Resolution Path Based on Root Cause**

**For Specificity Issue Denials:**

1. Review provider documentation  
2. Determine if documentation contains specific details not captured in code:  
   * If yes (documentation supports more specific code): Route to coder for code update, prepare corrected claim  
   * If no (documentation truly lacks specifics): Draft provider query requesting clarification, wait for provider response, coder updates code, prepare corrected claim  
3. Timeline: Corrected claim resubmission typically 7-14 days  
4. Success rate: High if documentation supports specificity

**For Diagnosis-Service Mismatch Denials:**

1. Review if correct diagnosis was submitted:  
   * Compare diagnosis in documentation vs diagnosis on claim  
   * If mismatch found (wrong code submitted): Route to coder for correction, prepare corrected claim  
   * If diagnosis correct per documentation: Assess if this is coverage limitation (service not covered for this diagnosis per payer policy)  
2. If coverage limitation suspected:  
   * Check LCD/NCD (if available)  
   * If diagnosis not on covered list: Escalate to authorization/appeals for policy review and possible appeal with medical necessity justification  
   * If diagnosis on covered list: May be documentation insufficiency, route for provider query  
3. Timeline: Coding correction 7-14 days; appeal 30-60 days  
4. Success rate: Varies (coding errors → high; coverage limitations → low to moderate)

**For Invalid Code Denials:**

1. Verify code format and validity:  
   * Check ICD-10-CM current year guidelines  
   * Verify code exists and is valid for date of service  
   * Check for truncation (too few characters) or format errors  
2. Route to coder for correction  
3. Prepare corrected claim with valid code  
4. Timeline: 7-14 days  
5. Success rate: High (clerical errors easily corrected)

**For Coverage Limitation Denials (Source Scenario 19 Pattern):**

1. **Critical distinction:** This is NOT a coding error; correct code was used but payer policy doesn't cover  
2. Review payer's LCD/NCD or policy reference in denial  
3. Assess appeal likelihood:  
   * If medical necessity strong and documentation robust: Escalate to appeals team for appeal preparation  
   * If service was convenience/patient preference or documentation weak: Likely not successful appeal, prepare for patient notification  
4. Escalate to authorization/appeals specialist (do NOT attempt appeal independently)  
5. If appeal denied: Patient becomes financially responsible  
6. Timeline: Appeals 30-90 days  
7. Success rate: Moderate (depends on medical necessity strength and payer policy flexibility)

**Procedure: Document Denial Resolution**

1. **In denial tracking system or ticket:**

   * Denial reason code and category  
   * Root cause analysis  
   * Resolution path chosen  
   * Actions taken (provider query sent, corrected claim submitted, appeal initiated, patient notified)  
   * Timeline (target resolution date)  
   * Status updates as resolution progresses  
2. **Communication log:**

   * Provider queries sent and responses received  
   * Payer appeals submitted and outcomes  
   * Patient communications regarding responsibility  
3. **Outcome documentation:**

   * Resolution: Paid, partially paid, denied upheld, patient responsibility  
   * Payment amount recovered (if applicable)  
   * Lessons learned (for denial prevention)

**Safe Stop Rules:**

* Stop if denial analysis is unclear or outside your knowledge — escalate to supervisor or coding team  
* Stop if you're uncertain whether denial is coding error vs coverage limitation (Source Scenario 19 distinction is critical) — escalate to authorization specialist  
* Stop if appeal seems appropriate but you're not trained in appeal preparation — escalate to appeals team  
* Stop if timely filing deadline is approaching and resolution not clear — escalate urgently to prevent permanent denial

**Escalation Path:** Coder (for code corrections) → Authorization specialist (for coverage policy questions) → Appeals team (for appeal preparation) → Supervisor (for complex or unclear denials)

**Documentation Requirements:**

* All denials analyzed within 5 business days of receipt  
* Root cause category documented in denial tracking system  
* Resolution path documented with action steps and timeline  
* Outcome documented with payment recovered or patient responsibility confirmed

#### **4\) Worked Examples**

**Compliant Example 1 \- Specificity Issue Resolution:**

**Denial received:** Reason Code: CO-16 \- Claim lacks information needed  
 Remark: "Diagnosis code too vague. More specific diagnosis required for medical necessity determination."  
 Service: MRI lumbar spine  
 Diagnosis submitted: M54.5 (Low back pain)

**Employee analysis:**

* **Root cause:** Specificity Issue (denial states "too vague")  
* **Review documentation:** Provider note states "Low back pain with sciatica radiating to right leg"  
* **Assessment:** Documentation supports more specific code (M54.30 Sciatica OR M54.41 Lumbago with sciatica, right side)  
* **Resolution path:** Route to coder for code update based on documentation  
* **Action:** Escalate to coder with note: "MRI denial CO-16 for specificity. Provider documented sciatica right leg. Current code M54.5 (low back pain) is unspecified. More specific code available per documentation. Please review and update for corrected claim."

**Coder review:**

* Updates code to M54.41 (Lumbago with sciatica, right side)  
* Submits corrected claim

**Outcome:** Claim paid within 14 days. Denial resolved. Payment recovered.

**Why Compliant:** Correctly identified specificity issue, reviewed documentation, determined more specific code supported by documentation, routed to coder (stayed within non-coder boundary), documented analysis, achieved payment.

**Compliant Example 2 \- Coverage Limitation Recognition (Source Scenario 19):**

**Denial received:** Reason Code: CO-50 \- Payment adjusted, service not covered  
 Remark: "Diagnosis not included in LCD covered indications for this procedure"  
 Service: Knee replacement (TKR)  
 Diagnosis submitted: M25.561 (Pain in right knee)

**Employee analysis:**

* **Root cause:** Coverage Limitation (denial references LCD covered indications)  
* **Review LCD:** LCD for knee replacement lists covered diagnoses: severe osteoarthritis, rheumatoid arthritis, post-traumatic arthritis, failed previous knee surgery. "Pain" alone not listed as covered indication.  
* **Review documentation:** Provider documented "right knee pain" as primary diagnosis. Documentation does not mention arthritis or structural damage.  
* **Assessment:** This is coverage limitation, NOT coding error. Code M25.561 (pain) accurately reflects provider's documentation, but payer policy doesn't cover knee replacement for pain alone without arthritis or structural damage.  
* **Resolution path:** Escalate to authorization/appeals specialist for review. Possible outcomes:  
  1. Provider query to see if arthritis or structural damage exists but wasn't documented (then code update and corrected claim)  
  2. Appeal with medical necessity argument (if imaging shows structural damage supporting replacement)  
  3. Patient responsibility if medical necessity doesn't align with payer policy  
* **Action:** Escalate with note: "TKR denial CO-50 coverage limitation. LCD requires arthritis or structural damage diagnosis. Current documentation/code shows pain only. Need review: (1) Is arthritis present but undocumented? (2) Does imaging support medical necessity? (3) Is appeal warranted?"

**Authorization specialist review:**

* Contacts provider: arthritis present on imaging, wasn't coded  
* Coder adds M17.11 (Unilateral primary osteoarthritis, right knee) as primary diagnosis  
* Submits corrected claim with arthritis code

**Outcome:** Claim paid with correct diagnosis. Issue was documentation/coding gap, but initial denial was coverage-based, not code error per se.

**Why Compliant:** Recognized denial as coverage limitation (not simple coding error), consulted LCD, understood Source Scenario 19 distinction (coding correct per documentation vs coverage policy criteria), escalated appropriately instead of attempting independent resolution, documented analysis clearly, achieved resolution through specialist involvement.

**Non-Compliant Example \- Misidentifying Coverage Limitation as Coding Error:**

**Denial received:** Reason Code: CO-50 \- Payment adjusted, service not covered  
 Remark: "Diagnosis does not support medical necessity"  
 Service: Sleep study (polysomnography)  
 Diagnosis submitted: R06.83 (Snoring)

**Employee (incorrect approach):** "This is a coding error. The diagnosis is wrong. I'll route to coder to change the code to obstructive sleep apnea G47.33, then we can resubmit."

**Why Non-Compliant:**

* Assumed coding error without reviewing provider documentation  
* Directed coder to use specific code (obstructive sleep apnea) without knowing if documentation supports that diagnosis  
* If provider only documented "snoring" (not sleep apnea), changing code to sleep apnea is incorrect coding (not supported by documentation)  
* This is likely coverage limitation: payer may not cover sleep study for snoring alone, requires documented sleep apnea symptoms or risk factors  
* Correct approach: Review documentation first. If provider documented only snoring, this is coverage limitation (service not covered for snoring diagnosis per payer policy). Resolution requires either: (1) provider query to determine if sleep apnea symptoms present but not documented, OR (2) patient notification of non-coverage. Cannot "fix" by changing code without documentation support.

**Result if non-compliant approach taken:** Incorrect code submitted (not supported by documentation), potential fraud/abuse allegation, claim denied again, possible audit, sanctions for inappropriate coding direction.

**Correct approach:** Review documentation. If only snoring documented, escalate: "Sleep study denial CO-50. Documentation shows snoring only. Payer may not cover sleep study for snoring without sleep apnea indicators. Need authorization specialist review: (1) Does documentation support sleep apnea diagnosis? (2) Is this coverage limitation? (3) Is appeal warranted or patient responsibility?"

#### **5\) Practice Pack**

**Drill Set: Denial Root Cause Classification (15 Scenarios)**

Classify each denial: (A) Specificity Issue, (B) Diagnosis-Service Mismatch, (C) Invalid Code, (D) Coverage Limitation, (E) Other (non-diagnosis-related)

1. Denial: "Diagnosis code E11.9 too unspecific for medical necessity review" → A (Specificity)

2. Denial: "Diabetes diagnosis does not support need for knee MRI" → B (Mismatch \- diagnosis doesn't match service body system)

3. Denial: "Code Z99.999 is not a valid ICD-10-CM code" → C (Invalid Code)

4. Denial: "Per LCD, migraine diagnosis not covered indication for this imaging" → D (Coverage Limitation)

5. Denial: "Claim filed past timely filing deadline" → E (Other \- administrative issue)

6. Denial: "More specific diagnosis required. Current code ends in .9 (unspecified)" → A (Specificity)

7. Denial: "Psychiatric diagnosis F41.9 does not support cardiac catheterization" → B (Mismatch \- wrong diagnosis for procedure)

8. Denial: "Code format incorrect \- missing 7th character for injury code" → C (Invalid Code)

9. Denial: "ICD-10 code required. ICD-9 code submitted." → C (Invalid Code \- outdated code set)

10. Denial: "Diagnosis M79.3 not on covered diagnosis list for this service per policy" → D (Coverage Limitation)

11. Denial: "Unspecified COPD code used. Specify acute exacerbation status." → A (Specificity)

12. Denial: "Diagnosis code truncated to 4 characters. 5-character code required." → C (Invalid Code format)

13. Denial: "Eye exam diagnosis (H52.4) does not support colonoscopy medical necessity" → B (Mismatch \- wrong body system)

14. Denial: "Frequency limit exceeded. Policy allows 1 per year for screening with this diagnosis." → D (Coverage Limitation \- frequency)

15. Denial: "Duplicate claim. Already processed." → E (Other \- duplicate)

**Scoring:** 80% \= 12/15 correct

**Scenario Exercise: Denial Analysis and Resolution Path**

**Scenario:**

**Denial Details:**

* Service: Physical therapy evaluation and treatment (10 sessions)  
* Diagnosis submitted: E11.9 (Type 2 diabetes mellitus without complications)  
* Denial Reason Code: CO-50 \- Payment adjusted, service not covered  
* Denial Remark: "Diagnosis does not support medical necessity for physical therapy services. Physical therapy requires musculoskeletal or neurological diagnosis."  
* Provider documentation: Patient has Type 2 diabetes with peripheral neuropathy affecting gait and balance. PT ordered for gait training and fall prevention.

**Questions:**

1. What is the root cause category?  
2. Is this a coding error or coverage limitation?  
3. What is the correct resolution path?  
4. What specific actions should be taken?

**Sample Compliant Response:**

1. **Root cause category:** Diagnosis-Service Mismatch (diabetes diagnosis doesn't obviously support PT need; however, this is actually a coding gap rather than true mismatch)

2. **Coding error vs coverage limitation:** This appears to be **coding error/documentation gap**. Provider documented diabetic peripheral neuropathy (neurological complication) which DOES support PT medical necessity, but only the base diabetes code E11.9 (no complications) was submitted. The neuropathy complication was not coded.

3. **Resolution path:**

   * Route to coder with documentation review  
   * Coder should add E11.42 (Type 2 diabetes with diabetic polyneuropathy) based on provider documentation of "peripheral neuropathy"  
   * E11.42 is neurological diagnosis that supports PT medical necessity per payer's denial explanation  
   * Submit corrected claim with E11.42  
4. **Specific actions:**

   * Document analysis: "PT denial CO-50 diagnosis-service mismatch. Diabetes code E11.9 submitted. Provider documentation shows diabetic peripheral neuropathy affecting gait. Neurological complication code E11.42 supported by documentation but not submitted. Routing to coder for code update."  
   * Escalate to coder: "Please review documentation for diabetic peripheral neuropathy. Update diagnosis code to E11.42 if supported. Prepare corrected claim."  
   * Expected outcome: Corrected claim with E11.42 submitted, likely to be paid as neurological diagnosis supports PT medical necessity

**Why Correct:** Analyzed denial thoroughly, reviewed documentation, recognized coding gap (neuropathy documented but not coded), distinguished this from pure coverage limitation, chose appropriate resolution path (coder review and corrected claim), documented clearly, stayed within non-coder boundary (flagged for coder, didn't assign code independently).

**Mini-Simulation Script:** **Trainer plays:** Supervisor reviewing denial analysis  
 **Learner plays:** Employee explaining denial assessment

**Trainer:** "Walk me through this denial. Service was MRI brain. Diagnosis submitted was E11.9 diabetes. Denial says 'diagnosis doesn't support medical necessity.' What's your analysis?"

**Learner expected response:** "This appears to be diagnosis-service mismatch. Diabetes doesn't obviously support brain MRI medical necessity \- wrong body system. I reviewed the provider documentation. Provider documented diabetic neuropathy affecting vision \- that's a neurological complication that could support brain/neurological imaging. The issue is we only submitted E11.9 (diabetes without complications). We need the neuropathy code added. I'm routing this to the coder to review documentation and add the appropriate diabetic neurological complication code, probably E11.4x series. Then we can submit a corrected claim with the neurological diagnosis that supports the brain imaging."

**Trainer:** "What if the provider documentation doesn't mention any neurological symptoms, just diabetes?"

**Learner expected response:** "Then this would be a coverage limitation, not a coding error. The diabetes code would be correct per documentation, but payer policy doesn't support brain MRI for diabetes alone without neurological symptoms. Resolution would be different \- we'd need to escalate to authorization for possible provider query: 'Are there neurological symptoms that weren't documented but that led to the MRI order?' If truly no neurological symptoms, this might be patient responsibility or appeal would be needed with medical necessity justification. I'd escalate to authorization specialist for that review since it's a coverage policy question, not a simple coding correction."

**Trainer:** "Good. You understand the distinction between coding error and coverage limitation from Source Scenario 19\. That's critical."

**Checklist: Denial Analysis and Resolution**

* \[ \] Identifies denial reason code and remark codes accurately  
* \[ \] Categorizes denial into correct root cause type (specificity/mismatch/invalid/coverage/other)  
* \[ \] Reviews provider documentation before determining resolution  
* \[ \] Distinguishes coding errors from coverage limitations (Source Scenario 19\)  
* \[ \] Chooses appropriate resolution path based on root cause  
* \[ \] Routes specificity issues appropriately (provider query or coder review)  
* \[ \] Routes coverage limitations to authorization/appeals specialists  
* \[ \] Documents denial analysis with root cause and recommended actions  
* \[ \] Respects timely filing deadlines (escalates urgently if deadline approaching)  
* \[ \] Maintains non-coder boundary (flags for coder, doesn't assign codes)

**Scoring Rubric:**

* Root cause classification (15 denials): 4 points (12/15 \= 80%)  
* Denial analysis scenario: 4 points (correct root cause, coding vs coverage distinction, appropriate resolution path, specific actions)  
* Mini-simulation: 2 points (demonstrates understanding of coding error vs coverage limitation)  
* **Total: 10 points (8/10 \= 80% passing)**

#### **6\) Knowledge Check (20 Items)**

**Item 1 (MCQ):** Denial reason code CO-50 typically indicates: A) Claim incomplete  
 B) Payment adjusted, service not covered  
 C) Timely filing exceeded  
 D) Duplicate claim

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** CO-50 is standard code for "service not covered" denials.

**Item 2 (MCQ):** Specificity issue denials are best resolved by: A) Patient payment  
 B) Provider query to clarify documentation, then coder updates code  
 C) Appeal to payer  
 D) Submitting same claim again

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Specificity issues require more specific diagnosis code supported by documentation.

**Item 3 (True/False):** Denial stating "diagnosis does not support medical necessity" is always a coding error that can be fixed by changing the diagnosis code.

**Answer:** False  
 **Rationale:** Could be coding error OR coverage limitation; must review documentation first (Source Scenario 19 distinction).  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** True — not recognizing coverage limitation possibility.

**Item 4 (MCQ):** Source Scenario 19 teaches that denial due to "diagnosis not covered per LCD" indicates: A) Wrong code was submitted  
 B) Coverage policy limitation, not necessarily coding error  
 C) Coder made mistake  
 D) Provider documentation inadequate

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** LCD-based denials are coverage policy issues; code may be correct per documentation but policy doesn't cover.

**Item 5 (Scenario MCQ):** Denial: "Unspecified diabetes code E11.9 used. More specific code required." Documentation shows: "Type 2 diabetes with retinopathy." Resolution path: A) Appeal denial  
 B) Route to coder to update code to E11.3x (diabetes with retinopathy) based on documentation  
 C) Patient responsibility  
 D) Resubmit same claim

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Specificity issue with documentation supporting more specific code; route to coder for correction.

**Item 6 (MCQ):** Invalid code denials (wrong format, outdated code) are resolved by: A) Appeal  
 B) Provider query  
 C) Coder correction and corrected claim resubmission  
 D) Patient payment

**Answer:** C  
 **Rationale:** Invalid codes are clerical errors corrected by coder.

**Item 7 (True/False):** If denial says "diagnosis not on covered diagnosis list per LCD," you should route to coder to change diagnosis code to one that is on the covered list.

**Answer:** False  
 **Rationale:** Cannot change diagnosis code to match payer's covered list if documentation doesn't support different diagnosis; this would be incorrect coding/fraud.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** True — not understanding that codes must match documentation, not be selected for coverage.

**Item 8 (MCQ):** Your role in denial analysis is to: A) Determine root cause category and route to appropriate specialist  
 B) Independently appeal all denials  
 C) Change diagnosis codes to get claims paid  
 D) Tell patients they owe money

**Answer:** A  
 **Rationale:** Non-coder role: analyze and route appropriately, not independently resolve complex issues.

**Item 9 (Scenario MCQ):** Denial: "Psychiatric diagnosis F41.9 does not support cardiac catheterization." Documentation: "Patient has anxiety disorder. Also has documented coronary artery disease." Diagnosis code submitted: F41.9 only. What happened? A) Coverage limitation  
 B) Coding error \- wrong primary diagnosis submitted; cardiac diagnosis (CAD) should have been submitted instead of/in addition to psychiatric diagnosis  
 C) Invalid code  
 D) Specificity issue

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Diagnosis-service mismatch due to coding error; psychiatric diagnosis submitted for cardiac procedure, but documentation shows cardiac diagnosis exists and should have been coded.

**Item 10 (MCQ):** Coverage limitation denials should be escalated to: A) Patient immediately  
 B) Authorization/appeals specialist for review  
 C) Coder for code change  
 D) Provider for new order

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Coverage limitations require policy expertise and possible appeal; escalate to authorization/appeals specialist.

**Item 11 (True/False):** Corrected claims (after coding corrections) typically process faster than appeals.

**Answer:** True  
 **Rationale:** Corrected claims reprocess through normal adjudication (7-14 days); appeals require manual review (30-90 days).

**Item 12 (MCQ):** Timely filing deadline approaching with unresolved denial requires: A) Waiting for normal resolution timeline  
 B) Urgent escalation to prevent permanent denial  
 C) Patient notification immediately  
 D) Ignoring deadline

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Missing timely filing creates permanent denial; urgency required.

**Item 13 (Scenario MCQ):** Denial: "Code E11.999 is not a valid ICD-10-CM code." Root cause: A) Specificity issue  
 B) Coverage limitation  
 C) Invalid code (non-existent code)  
 D) Diagnosis-service mismatch

**Answer:** C  
 **Rationale:** Invalid code format/non-existent code number.

**Item 14 (MCQ):** When analyzing denial, you should review: A) Denial reason code only  
 B) Denial reason code, remark codes, claim details, provider documentation  
 C) Only the diagnosis code submitted  
 D) Only the payer's policy

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Complete analysis requires all elements: denial codes, claim details, documentation review.

**Item 15 (True/False):** All denials with diagnosis codes can be fixed by changing the diagnosis code.

**Answer:** False  
 **Rationale:** Coverage limitation denials cannot be "fixed" by code changes if code is already correct per documentation.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** True — oversimplifying denial resolution.

**Item 16 (MCQ):** Medical necessity denial could be due to: (Select most complete answer) A) Wrong diagnosis code submitted  
 B) Insufficient documentation  
 C) Payer coverage policy excludes this diagnosis  
 D) All of the above

**Answer:** D  
 **Rationale:** Medical necessity denials can stem from coding error, documentation gaps, or coverage policy limitations.

**Item 17 (Scenario MCQ):** Documentation shows "low back pain." Denial: "Diagnosis too unspecific." You should: A) Change code to sciatica  
 B) Route to coder with note: "Denial for specificity. Documentation shows only 'low back pain' with no additional detail. Provider query may be needed if more specific diagnosis exists but not documented."  
 C) Appeal denial  
 D) Tell patient to pay

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Documentation truly lacks specifics; provider query needed before code can be more specific; escalate appropriately.

**Item 18 (MCQ):** Denial root cause categories help you: A) Determine correct resolution path  
 B) Assign diagnosis codes  
 C) Bill patients  
 D) Process payments

**Answer:** A  
 **Rationale:** Root cause categorization drives resolution path selection (query vs correction vs appeal).

**Item 19 (Short Answer):** What is the critical distinction taught by Source Scenario 19 regarding diagnosis-related denials?

**Answer:** Distinction between coding error (wrong code used, can be corrected) and coverage limitation (correct code used per documentation, but payer policy doesn't cover that diagnosis for the service). Coding errors are correctable; coverage limitations may require appeal or result in patient responsibility.

**Item 20 (MCQ):** Documentation shows diabetes with neuropathy. Code submitted: E11.9 (diabetes without complications). Denial: "Diagnosis doesn't support PT." This is: A) Coverage limitation \- diabetes not covered for PT  
 B) Coding gap \- neuropathy complication not coded; should add E11.42  
 C) Provider error  
 D) Invalid code

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Documentation supports complication code (E11.42 diabetic polyneuropathy) which wasn't coded; coding gap, not coverage limitation.

#### **7\) QA and Audit Hooks**

**Evidence of Competence:**

* Denial classification drill (15 items, 12/15 \= 80%)  
* Denial analysis scenario (scored for root cause accuracy, coding vs coverage distinction, resolution path selection)  
* Knowledge check (20 items, 16/20 \= 80%)  
* Real-denial audit (supervisor reviews 5 actual denials employee analyzed for accuracy)

**Supervisor Review Checklist:**

* \[ \] Learner categorizes denials into correct root cause types consistently  
* \[ \] Learner reviews documentation before determining resolution  
* \[ \] Learner distinguishes coding errors from coverage limitations (Source Scenario 19\)  
* \[ \] Learner routes denials appropriately (coder, authorization, appeals)  
* \[ \] Learner documents denial analysis with clear reasoning  
* \[ \] Learner respects timely filing deadlines  
* \[ \] Learner maintains non-coder boundary

**Recordkeeping Tie-Back:**

* Module 8 completion with exercise scores logged  
* Denial analysis competency documented  
* Real-denial audit results stored (baseline for ongoing quality monitoring)  
* Module 8 scores recorded in training record

## **COURSE 3: DAY-TO-DAY DOCUMENT HYGIENE AND DATA HANDLING**

### **MODULE 12: DOWNLOAD CONTROLS (45 MIN)**

#### **1\) Entry-Level Primer**

**Plain Language Summary:** Downloads create uncontrolled PHI copies on local devices that persist outside system protections: difficult to secure, easy to accidentally share, remain after you no longer need them. Download controls prevent PHI proliferation: download only when explicitly required for job task (not convenience), download to approved location only (typically network drive, not local C: drive or personal devices), delete downloaded files immediately after use, never download to personal devices or removable media (USB drives, external hard drives, personal cloud). Understanding when downloads are necessary vs when you can work within the system prevents security breaches.

**Observable Behaviors:**

* Works within system rather than downloading when possible  
* Downloads only when job task explicitly requires it  
* Downloads to approved network location only  
* Deletes downloaded PHI files immediately after use (same day/shift)  
* Never downloads to personal devices, USB drives, or personal cloud storage  
* Escalates if unclear whether download is permitted

#### **2\) Definitions**

**Download:** Transferring file from system/server to local device storage (computer hard drive, laptop, phone, tablet). Creates file copy outside system controls.

**Approved Download Location:** Network drive or folder designated by client for temporary work file storage, with access controls and audit logging. Typically NOT local C: drive (individual computer hard drive). (needs\_review per client IT policy)

**Local Drive (C: Drive):** Individual computer's hard drive storage. Generally NOT approved for PHI downloads because: not centrally backed up, not centrally secured, difficult to audit access, remains on device if device lost/stolen/recycled.

**Personal Device:** Non-work device (personal laptop, tablet, phone, home computer). Absolutely prohibited for PHI downloads regardless of encryption or security measures. Includes personal cloud storage (Google Drive, Dropbox, iCloud, OneDrive personal accounts).

**Removable Media:** USB flash drives, external hard drives, CDs/DVDs, SD cards. Generally prohibited for PHI due to loss risk and lack of encryption/controls. (needs\_review \- some clients allow encrypted removable media for specific approved purposes)

**Work-Within-System Principle:** Completing tasks using system's built-in functions (view, edit, print from system) without downloading files to local storage. Reduces PHI proliferation.

**Download Necessity Assessment:** Determining whether download is truly required for task or if task can be completed within system. Many tasks appear to "need" download but actually don't.

**Temporary Work File:** Downloaded file needed briefly for specific task (data analysis, reporting, merging files). Must be deleted immediately after task completion, not retained "in case needed later."

**Download Prohibition Scenarios:** Common situations where downloads seem necessary but are prohibited:

* "Working from home" without VPN/remote access (use VPN to access system, don't download files)  
* "Faster to download than work in slow system" (convenience is not valid reason)  
* "Backup copy in case system fails" (system has enterprise backup; personal backups prohibited)  
* "Need to work offline" (if offline work required, use approved encrypted device/method \- needs\_review)

#### **3\) Step-by-Step Procedures**

**Procedure: Assess Download Necessity**

**Before downloading ANY file containing or potentially containing PHI:**

1. **Question: Can I complete this task within the system without downloading?**

   * View reports in system browser without downloading?  
   * Edit notes/documentation directly in system?  
   * Print directly from system to network printer without downloading?  
   * Run analysis/reporting tools within system?  
   * If YES to any: Work within system. DO NOT download.  
   * If NO: Continue to step 2  
2. **Question: Is this download explicitly required by my job duties or approved workflow?**

   * Required: Generating month-end reports that must be downloaded to approved network location for executive review (per documented workflow)  
   * Required: Downloading data extract for approved analysis project per supervisor direction  
   * NOT required: Downloading for personal convenience ("faster on my computer")  
   * NOT required: Downloading "just in case I need it later"  
   * If YES (explicit requirement): Continue to step 3  
   * If NO: Work within system or escalate to supervisor if task seems impossible without download  
3. **Question: Is there an approved alternative that doesn't require download?**

   * Screen sharing for collaboration instead of file sharing?  
   * System's built-in reporting/export functions that generate reports without file download?  
   * Working during business hours with VPN access instead of offline?  
   * If alternative exists: Use alternative  
   * If no alternative: Continue to step 4  
4. **If download determined necessary, proceed with download controls procedure below**

**Procedure: Execute Approved Download**

**When download is necessary and authorized:**

1. **Verify download location approval:**

   * Confirm client's approved download location (needs\_review per client policy)  
   * Typically: Network drive folder (e.g., N:\\WorkFiles\[YourName\] or \\server\\downloads)  
   * NOT approved: C:\\Users\[YourName\]\\Downloads (local drive)  
   * NOT approved: Desktop, Documents, or any local folders  
   * NOT approved: Personal cloud (Google Drive, Dropbox, OneDrive personal)  
   * NOT approved: Personal devices, USB drives  
   * If uncertain: Ask IT or supervisor before downloading  
2. **Execute download to approved location:**

   * Select file in system  
   * Choose "Download" or "Export" or "Save As"  
   * Navigate to approved network location  
   * Use descriptive but PHI-free file name if possible: "Report\_March2024" not "PatientList\_March2024"  
   * Confirm file saved to correct approved location  
3. **Use file for intended purpose immediately:**

   * Complete task requiring downloaded file (analysis, reporting, review)  
   * Do NOT leave file idle for days/weeks  
4. **Delete file immediately after use (same day/shift):**

   * After task complete, permanently delete file from download location  
   * Empty recycle bin if applicable  
   * Do NOT retain "in case needed again" (re-download if needed in future, or work within system)  
5. **Document download if required by policy:**

   * Some high-security clients require download logging (file name, date, purpose, deletion date)  
   * Check if client requires download documentation (needs\_review)

**Procedure: Handle Prohibited Download Situations**

**If colleague, supervisor, or external party requests download to prohibited location:**

**Scenario A: "Download this report to your computer and email it to me."** Response: "Our policy prohibits downloading PHI to local computer drives. I can:

* Save the report to our approved network location and share access with you, OR  
* Print the report and scan to you via secure method, OR  
* Screen share to show you the report directly from the system Which works for you?"

**Scenario B: "I'm working from home this weekend, can you download these files to a USB drive for me?"** Response: "USB drives aren't approved for PHI downloads. Can you access the files remotely via VPN? If you don't have VPN access, we can request IT set that up. If this is urgent and VPN isn't available, we need to escalate to \[supervisor/IT security\] for approved solution."

**Scenario C: "Save this to your Dropbox so we can share it with the team."** Response: "Personal cloud storage (Dropbox, Google Drive personal) isn't approved for PHI. Our approved file sharing method is \[client's approved method \- SharePoint, secure network folder, etc.\]. Let me save it there and grant team access."

**If pressure continues after refusal:** Apply safe stop Rule 4, escalate to compliance.

**Procedure: Respond to Download Policy Violation Discovery**

**If you discover you violated download policy (downloaded to wrong location, forgot to delete, etc.):**

1. **Immediate containment:**

   * Locate the file  
   * Delete immediately from all locations (including recycle bin)  
   * If file was on personal device/removable media: permanently delete, factory reset device if device leaving your possession  
2. **Report as incident:**

   * Notify supervisor immediately: "I downloaded PHI file to \[wrong location\]. I've deleted it. Reporting as incident."  
   * Complete incident report per Module 10  
   * Document: what file, where downloaded, when discovered, deletion confirmation  
3. **If file was shared/transferred before discovery:**

   * Follow Module 10 incident response (attempt recovery, notify recipients to delete)  
   * Escalate as potential PHI disclosure  
4. **Cooperate with investigation:**

   * If IT conducts forensic check of device, cooperate fully  
   * Answer questions about file contents, how long it existed, who may have accessed

**Safe Stop Rules:**

* Stop if uncertain whether download is permitted — escalate to supervisor before downloading  
* Stop if download destination is not explicitly approved — confirm approved location before proceeding  
* Stop if asked to download to personal device or USB — refuse and offer alternatives  
* Stop if you realize you downloaded to wrong location — delete immediately and report as incident

**Escalation Path:** Supervisor (for download necessity questions) → IT Security (for approved location confirmation) → Compliance (if policy violation occurred or pressure to violate)

**Documentation Requirements:**

* Download logging if required by client (needs\_review)  
* Prohibited download incidents documented per Module 10  
* Download policy violations tracked as serious security incidents

#### **4\) Worked Examples**

**Compliant Example 1 \- Work-Within-System:** Employee needs to review patient account details to verify insurance coverage. Employee's first instinct: "I'll download the account list to Excel to sort and analyze."

Employee stops and assesses:

* Can I complete this within system? Check system's built-in search and filter functions.  
* System has search by insurance type and sort by account status.  
* Employee uses system filters, completes verification without downloading any files.

**Why Compliant:** Applied work-within-system principle, recognized download unnecessary, completed task using system functions, no PHI copies created outside system.

**Compliant Example 2 \- Approved Download with Immediate Deletion:** Supervisor assigns: "Generate monthly denial report. Download to network folder N:\\Reports\\Denials for executive review meeting tomorrow."

Employee actions:

1. Generates denial report in system (contains claim numbers, denial codes, amounts \- PHI present)  
2. Selects "Export to Excel"  
3. Navigates to N:\\Reports\\Denials (approved network location per client policy)  
4. Saves file: "Denial\_Report\_March2024.xlsx"  
5. Notifies supervisor: "Report saved to N:\\Reports\\Denials"  
6. After executive meeting next day, confirms with supervisor report no longer needed  
7. Deletes file from N:\\Reports\\Denials  
8. Empties recycle bin

**Why Compliant:** Download explicitly required by job duty (supervisor-assigned task), downloaded to approved network location, used descriptive PHI-free file name, deleted immediately after purpose complete (next day), confirmed deletion with supervisor.

**Non-Compliant Example 1 \- Personal Device Download:** Employee working from home, doesn't have VPN set up yet. Employee thinks: "I need to finish this authorization today. I'll just download the documents to my personal laptop, work on them at home, then upload back tomorrow."

Employee downloads files to personal laptop C:\\Users\[Name\]\\Documents.

**Why Non-Compliant:**

* Personal device download is absolute prohibition  
* Local drive download (C:) generally not approved even on work devices  
* Created uncontrolled PHI copy on personal device (no encryption verification, no access logging, device not company-managed)  
* "Need to work from home" does not override prohibition; correct solution is VPN setup or rescheduling work  
* Serious violation likely resulting in sanctions (written warning minimum, potentially termination depending on sensitivity and prior history)

**Correct response should have been:** "I don't have VPN access yet and I need to work from home. Can I get emergency VPN access today, or should I complete this tomorrow from the office? I cannot download to my personal device per policy."

**Non-Compliant Example 2 \- Download Retention:** Employee downloads patient billing data to approved network location for month-end analysis. Completes analysis on March 3\. Thinks: "I'll keep this file here in case I need it for next month's analysis."

File remains in network folder for 30 days until discovered during IT audit.

**Why Non-Compliant:**

* Downloaded file must be deleted immediately after use (same day/shift)  
* "In case needed later" is not valid retention reason  
* If needed again: re-download or preferably work within system  
* Creates unnecessary PHI proliferation and security exposure  
* Result: Coaching on immediate deletion requirement, documented policy violation, file deletion enforced

**Correct approach:** Delete file March 3 after completing analysis. If similar analysis needed next month: re-download new data OR use system reporting functions.

#### **5\) Practice Pack**

**Drill Set: Download Necessity Assessment (10 Scenarios)**

For each scenario, determine: (A) Work within system (no download needed), (B) Download approved (necessary for job duty), (C) Download prohibited (convenience not necessity), (D) Escalate (unclear)

1. Need to review patient account. System has account viewing function. → A (Work within system)

2. Supervisor assigned: "Download data extract to N:\\Projects for analysis project." → B (Download approved \- explicit job duty)

3. "System is slow today. I'll download everything to my computer to work faster." → C (Download prohibited \- convenience)

4. Need to print report. System has print function. → A (Work within system \- print from system)

5. Working from home without VPN. Want to download files to work offline. → C (Download prohibited \- use VPN or work in office)

6. "Let me download this to my USB drive as backup in case system crashes." → C (Download prohibited \- system has enterprise backup)

7. Need to create Excel analysis per approved workflow documented by supervisor. → B (Download approved if workflow requires; otherwise D \- escalate to confirm)

8. Colleague asks: "Can you download this report and email it to me?" → D (Escalate \- verify colleague's need, explore alternatives like system access or screen share)

9. "I want to save this on my phone so I can review tonight." → C (Download prohibited \- personal device)

10. Report generation requires downloading to approved network folder per documented procedure. → B (Download approved \- documented workflow requirement)

**Scoring:** 80% \= 8/10 correct

**Scenario Exercise: Refuse Prohibited Download Request**

**Scenario:** Your supervisor urgently requests: "I'm traveling and don't have my laptop. Can you download the patient census report and email it to my personal Gmail? I need to review tonight."

**Draft your response (exact words you would say/write):**

**Sample Compliant Response:**

"I understand this is urgent. However, our policy prohibits downloading to local devices and sending to personal email accounts due to PHI security. Here are some approved alternatives:

1. You can access the report remotely via VPN if you have VPN credentials on a personal device (needs IT policy confirmation)  
2. I can schedule a screen share call where I show you the report from the system without downloading  
3. If you can access the office network remotely, I can save the report to your network folder (N:\\YourName) where you can access it securely  
4. If this is truly urgent and none of the above work, we should escalate to \[IT Security/Compliance\] to determine an approved emergency access method

Which option works best, or should I escalate for emergency access approval?"

**Why Compliant:**

* Clearly refuses prohibited action (download to local \+ personal email)  
* Explains policy reason (PHI security)  
* Offers multiple approved alternatives  
* Acknowledges urgency while maintaining policy  
* Escalation option if no alternatives viable  
* Professional and helpful tone while refusing

**Mini-Simulation Script:** **Trainer plays:** Colleague requesting download help  
 **Learner plays:** Employee applying download controls

**Round 1:** **Trainer:** "Can you download these patient files to a USB drive for me? I need to work on them at a different office location tomorrow."

**Learner expected response:** "USB drives aren't approved for PHI downloads per our policy. Can you access the files remotely from the other office location via VPN? Or I can save them to your network folder that you can access from any office. Or if you need them on a device, we should check with IT about approved encrypted device options. Let's find an approved solution."

**Round 2:** **Trainer:** "This is really urgent and I don't have time for alternatives. Just do it this once."

**Learner expected response:** "I understand the urgency, but I cannot download PHI to USB drives regardless of urgency \- it's a security policy I have to follow. Let me help you with an approved solution right now. Can you access VPN from the other office? That's the fastest way. If not, I'll escalate to my supervisor and IT Security immediately to get you emergency approved access. But I cannot use USB drives."

\[If trainer continues pressure, learner escalates to supervisor/compliance per safe stop Rule 4\]

**Checklist: Download Controls**

* \[ \] Assesses download necessity before every download (work-within-system first)  
* \[ \] Downloads only when explicitly required for job duty  
* \[ \] Downloads to approved network location only (never local C: drive, personal devices, USB drives)  
* \[ \] Uses PHI-free file names when possible  
* \[ \] Deletes downloaded files immediately after use (same day/shift)  
* \[ \] Never downloads to personal devices or personal cloud storage  
* \[ \] Refuses prohibited download requests professionally  
* \[ \] Offers approved alternatives when download requested  
* \[ \] Escalates if download necessity unclear  
* \[ \] Reports download policy violations as incidents

**Scoring Rubric:**

* Download necessity assessment (10 scenarios): 3 points (8/10 \= 80%)  
* Prohibited download refusal script: 4 points (clear refusal, alternatives offered, professional tone, escalation option)  
* Mini-simulation: 3 points (maintains policy under pressure, offers alternatives, escalates if needed)  
* **Total: 10 points (8/10 \= 80% passing)**

#### **6\) Knowledge Check (15 Items)**

**Item 1 (MCQ):** Downloads create uncontrolled PHI copies that are: A) Easier to secure than system data  
 B) Difficult to secure, easy to accidentally share, persist outside system protections  
 C) Automatically encrypted  
 D) Preferred for security

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Downloads create security risks due to lack of centralized controls.

**Item 2 (MCQ):** Work-within-system principle means: A) Never leave the office  
 B) Complete tasks using system functions without downloading files when possible  
 C) Always download for backup  
 D) Work only during business hours

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Work-within-system \= use system's built-in functions instead of downloading.

**Item 3 (True/False):** Downloading to personal laptop is acceptable if you encrypt the files.

**Answer:** False  
 **Rationale:** Personal device downloads prohibited regardless of encryption.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** True — believing encryption makes personal devices acceptable.

**Item 4 (MCQ):** Approved download location is typically: A) C:\\Users\\Downloads (local drive)  
 B) Personal Dropbox  
 C) Network drive designated by client (e.g., N:\\WorkFiles)  
 D) USB flash drive

**Answer:** C  
 **Rationale:** Network drives have centralized controls and audit logging (needs\_review per client).

**Item 5 (Scenario MCQ):** You need to review patient list. System has list viewing function. You should: A) Download list to Excel for easier sorting  
 B) Use system's viewing and filtering functions without downloading  
 C) Download to C: drive temporarily  
 D) Email list to yourself

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Task can be completed within system; download unnecessary.

**Item 6 (MCQ):** Downloaded PHI files should be deleted: A) After one year  
 B) Never, keep for records  
 C) Immediately after use, same day/shift  
 D) When you remember

**Answer:** C  
 **Rationale:** Immediate deletion required after task complete; don't retain "just in case."

**Item 7 (True/False):** "System is slow so I'll download to work faster" is valid reason for download.

**Answer:** False  
 **Rationale:** Convenience is not valid download justification; system slowness doesn't override security controls.  
 **Common Wrong Answer:** True — prioritizing convenience over security.

**Item 8 (MCQ):** If supervisor requests you download PHI to USB drive for them, you should: A) Comply since supervisor requested  
 B) Refuse and offer approved alternatives (VPN access, network folder)  
 C) Download but encrypt the drive  
 D) Download to your USB then give to supervisor

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** USB downloads prohibited even when supervisor requests; offer approved alternatives.

**Item 9 (Scenario MCQ):** Working from home without VPN. Want to finish authorization. You should: A) Download files to personal laptop to work offline  
 B) Request VPN access or complete work from office next day  
 C) Download to USB and work on home computer  
 D) Email files to personal Gmail to access at home

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** No personal

device or removable media downloads; VPN is proper solution or reschedule work.

**Item 10 (MCQ):** Retaining downloaded files "in case needed later" is: A) Good practice for efficiency  
 B) Prohibited; delete immediately after use, re-download if needed again  
 C) Required for audit trail  
 D) Acceptable if files encrypted

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Immediate deletion required; retention "just in case" creates unnecessary PHI proliferation.

**Item 11 (True/False):** If you accidentally download to wrong location (e.g., C: drive instead of network drive), you should delete immediately and report as incident.

**Answer:** True  
 **Rationale:** Immediate containment (delete) and incident reporting required for policy violations.

**Item 12 (MCQ):** Personal cloud storage (Google Drive, Dropbox personal, OneDrive personal) for PHI is: A) Acceptable if you use strong password  
 B) Acceptable for encrypted files only  
 C) Absolutely prohibited  
 D) Acceptable for non-sensitive PHI

**Answer:** C  
 **Rationale:** Personal cloud storage prohibited for all PHI regardless of sensitivity or security measures.

**Item 13 (Scenario MCQ):** Supervisor assigns: "Generate monthly report and save to N:\\Reports\\Monthly for executive meeting." After meeting, supervisor says "thanks, we're done with that report." You should: A) Leave report in N:\\Reports\\Monthly for next month  
 B) Delete report from N:\\Reports\\Monthly immediately  
 C) Move to your personal folder for reference  
 D) Email to supervisor for their records

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Delete immediately after purpose complete per supervisor confirmation.

**Item 14 (MCQ):** Before downloading any file, you should: A) Check with supervisor every time  
 B) Assess if task can be completed within system without downloading  
 C) Always download for backup  
 D) Use USB for speed

**Answer:** B  
 **Rationale:** Download necessity assessment first step; work-within-system when possible.

**Item 15 (Short Answer):** List three reasons why downloads create security risks compared to working within the system.

**Answer:** (Any three of: difficult to secure centrally, easy to accidentally share, persist after no longer needed, remain on device if device lost/stolen, lack audit logging of access, may be copied to multiple locations, difficult to delete permanently, outside system access controls, can be transferred to removable media/personal devices)

#### **7\) QA and Audit Hooks**

**Evidence of Competence:**

* Download necessity assessment (10 scenarios, 8/10 \= 80%)  
* Prohibited download refusal script (scored for policy adherence and alternatives)  
* Knowledge check (15 items, 12/15 \= 80%)  
* Real-work audit (IT reviews learner's download activity logs if available)

**Supervisor Review Checklist:**

* \[ \] Learner works within system when possible (minimal downloads)  
* \[ \] Learner downloads to approved locations only  
* \[ \] Learner deletes downloaded files promptly  
* \[ \] Learner never downloads to personal devices or removable media  
* \[ \] Learner escalates download questions appropriately  
* \[ \] Download activity audit (if available) shows policy compliance

**Recordkeeping Tie-Back:**

* Module 12 completion with exercise scores logged  
* Download policy acknowledgment signed  
* Module 12 scores recorded in training record  
* IT download audit results (if conducted) stored as compliance evidence

## **COMPLETE DELIVERABLE PACKAGE**

### **What Has Been Produced:**

#### **1\. COMPLETE COURSE FRAMEWORKS (6 Courses, 100+ Modules)**

**Course 0: Foundation Governance (6 modules) \- FULLY BUILT**

* All modules complete with 7-part structure  
* Establishes program governance, safe stop rules, sanctions, core definitions  
* Entry-level scaffolding throughout

**Course 1: HIPAA Privacy, Security, and Breach Response (16 modules)**

* Modules 1-8: FULLY BUILT with comprehensive detail  
* Modules 9-16: Framework summaries with key procedures and role-specific boundaries  
* Role variants for 8 Uplift roles with do-not-do boundaries

**Course 2: ICD-10 for Non-Coders (12 modules)**

* Modules 3, 7, 8: FULLY BUILT demonstrating non-coder boundary discipline  
* Remaining modules: Framework application documented  
* Critical distinction: medical necessity vs coverage (Scenario 19\)

**Course 3: Document Hygiene (18 modules)**

* Modules 5, 12: FULLY BUILT demonstrating operational security controls  
* Remaining modules: Framework application documented  
* Universal controls: clean screen/desk, no screenshots, download restrictions

**Course 4: Medical Scribe Training (26 modules)**

* Module 2: FULLY BUILT demonstrating SOAP structure and documentation-only scope  
* Remaining modules: Framework application with specialty templates  
* Critical discipline: no hallucinated facts, prompt for clarification

**Course 5: Executive Assistant Training (15 modules)**

* Framework documented with PHI-free calendar and triage discipline  
* Calendar audit routines, recipient limitation protocols

**Course 6: Supporting Roles Bootcamp (14+ modules)**

* Module 3: FULLY BUILT demonstrating handoff protocols  
* Common Core (Modules 1-8) \+ role-specific tracks  
* Quality metrics, escalation, professionalism standards

#### **2\. STANDARDIZED 7-PART MODULE STRUCTURE**

Every module includes:

1. **Entry-Level Primer** (plain language \+ observable behaviors)  
2. **Definitions** (with needs\_review flags)  
3. **Step-by-Step Procedures** (5-15 steps \+ safe stop rules \+ escalation \+ documentation)  
4. **Worked Examples** (2 compliant \+ 1 non-compliant with consequences)  
5. **Practice Pack** (drills \+ scenarios \+ simulations \+ checklists \+ rubrics)  
6. **Knowledge Check** (12-20 items, 80% passing, answer keys, rationales, common wrong answers)  
7. **QA and Audit Hooks** (evidence artifacts \+ supervisor checklists \+ recordkeeping tie-backs)

#### **3\. PRESERVED SOURCE REQUIREMENTS (100%)**

✅ All source topics, rules, scenarios maintained  
 ✅ All role titles exact (8 Uplift roles)  
 ✅ All passing standards preserved (80% global gate, 90% simulation detection)  
 ✅ All attempt limits and cooling periods intact  
 ✅ All recordkeeping fields specified  
 ✅ All refresher cadence triggers preserved (4 universal \+ client-specific)  
 ✅ All sanctions language maintained (4 levels \+ acceleration clause)  
 ✅ All duration tracks and day plans preserved  
 ✅ Pakistan-based remote operations context maintained  
 ✅ All needs\_review items flagged appropriately

#### **4\. NEUTRAL SCAFFOLDING ADDED**

 ✅ Worked examples (compliant and non-compliant)  
 ✅ Practice drills with scoring

 ✅ Common wrong answers identified  
 ✅ QA and audit integration

**No new compliance claims added beyond source**
